Refutation of Astrology as Determinative
Nasafi refutes astrology's claim to causal power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic position that celestial bodies are subjugated by Allah and have no independent causal power, and how the example of Prophet Abraham (peace be upon him) is correctly interpreted.

Core Idea
Stars are signs, not causes; only Allah determines events.

This lesson addresses a common challenge: doesn't the Quran mention that Prophet Abraham looked at the stars and predicted his sickness? Does that validate astrology? Nasafi clarifies the Ahl al-Sunna position, showing that the stars are subservient to Allah's command, and that Abraham's knowledge came from Allah, not from star-gazing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Focus on the three parts: the statement of Ahl al-Sunna, the objection, and the refutation.
Notice the Quranic verse cited.
2
Identify the core claim and objection
Pinpoint the central claim that stars are subjugated, and the objection that astrology was true because Abraham was taught it.
The objection uses the story of Abraham (Surah 37:88-89).
3
Analyze the refutation
Understand that Abraham's knowledge of his sickness came from Allah, not from the stars. The glance at stars was not causal.
The market example shows that God may inform through signs, but signs are not causes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة أن البروج والنجوم والشمس والقمر مستورات ليس لها من الله شيء وجود إلا وهي مسخرات بأمره كما قال الله ﴿والشمس والقمر والنجوم مسخرات بأمره﴾ فإن قيل علم النجوم كان حقا فعلمه الله إبراهيم عليه السلام ومن قال بذلك تأويله الدليل قوله تعالى خبر عن إبراهيم عليه السلام ﴿فنظر نظرة في النجوم فقال إني سقيم﴾ استعمل النظر إلى النجوم أنه سقيم والجواب قلنا إن إبراهيم عليه السلام علم أنه سقيم وأما زمان نظره إلى النجوم عليه السلام قال ليس التدبير بالنجوم ولكن الله تعالى أخبرهم في كتابهم أن نجا يدخل ذاك بيع موضع كذا فاعلم أنه سيكون كذا وكذا
And Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said: The constellations, stars, sun, and moon are subjugated; they have no existence from God except that they are subservient by His command, as God said: 'And the sun, the moon, and the stars are subjugated by His command.' If it is said: The science of stars (astrology) was true, for God taught it to Abraham (peace be upon him), and whoever said that his evidence is the saying of God Most High reporting from Abraham (peace be upon him): 'Then he glanced a glance at the stars and said: Indeed, I am sick' – he used the glance at the stars to conclude that he was sick. The answer: We say that Abraham (peace be upon him) knew that he was sick. As for the time of his glance at the stars, that was not management by the stars, but God Most High had informed them in their book that if such and such a market enters such and such a place, then know that such and such will happen.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage deals with the Islamic stance on astrology (علم النجوم). Nasafi states the Ahl al-Sunna position: the heavenly bodies (sun, moon, stars, and constellations) are subjugated beings (musakhkharat) that have no independent power or will; they exist only by God's command and are entirely subservient to Him. This is supported by Quran 7:54 and 16:12. An objection is raised: the science of stars (astrology) was true and even taught to the Prophet Abraham (upon him peace), and his claim of being sick (as in Quran 37:88-89) was based on his observation of the stars. Nasafi refutes this by explaining that Abraham already knew he was sick due to God's knowledge, not because the stars caused his sickness. The mention of the 'market' passage is unclear in the OCR; it likely refers to another narrative about Abraham using the stars for guidance but not as causes. The key point is that stars are signs (ayāt) but not agents of events; only God determines outcomes.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة
البروج
النجوم
مسخرات
علم النجوم
إبراهيم عليه السلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Astrology (علم النجوم) can determine future events or cause sickness.
Correction: Nasafi explains that celestial bodies are subjugated by Allah and have no independent power; they are signs, not causes. The example of Abraham shows that his knowledge came from Allah, not from star-gazing.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the relationship between stars and events on earth?
A) Stars cause events directly
B) Stars are subjugated by God and have no independent power
C) Stars are deities controlling destiny
D) Stars are irrelevant to events

Key Takeaway
The sun, moon, and stars are signs of Allah's power, not independent causes; only Allah determines events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan your day or make decisions, do you ever subconsciously rely on what feels like 'signs' or omens instead of trusting Allah's decree? How does this passage confront that tendency?
?
Consider a time you attributed a positive outcome to luck, a charm, or a natural phenomenon. Does your heart truly believe that only Allah determines events? What would change in your daily reliance if you fully embraced this?
?
If you were in a situation where worldly causes seem to point to a certain future, do you find yourself anxious or secure? How does the truth that the stars are simply subjugated signs—not independent actors—reshape your trust in Allah's sole control?

Refuting the Astrologers' Claim about the Stars' Location
Nasafi refutes astrologers using Quranic verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi uses Quranic verses to refute the astrological claim that the sun, moon, and stars reside in the fourth heaven, and why the Sunni position places them in the lowest heaven.

Core Idea
The Quran places the stars in the lowest heaven, not the fourth.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi confronts a claim made by astrologers that the sun, moon, and stars are located in the fourth heaven. He presents the Sunni position that they are in the lowest heaven and supports it with two Quranic proofs. He also points out inconsistencies in the astrologers' own system. Let's examine his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Note the key terms: السماء الدنيا (lowest heaven) and السماء الرابعة (fourth heaven).
2
Identify the two Quranic proofs
The author cites two verses: 'Indeed We adorned the lowest heaven with the adornment of the stars' and the story of Dhu al-Qarnayn finding the sun setting in a muddy spring. Understand how each supports the Sunni view.
The first verse explicitly mentions 'lowest heaven', the second shows the sun is observed from earth.
3
Understand the refutation of astrologers
The author notes that even astrologers place the moon in the lowest heaven, contradicting their general claim. He details their planetary spheres to highlight inconsistency.
This shows that the astrologers' own system doesn't fully align with their claim.
4
Reflect on the lunar eclipse argument
The author asks: 'Nor do we witness the eclipse of the moon with its eye in the lowest heaven?' This implies that our observation of lunar eclipses confirms the moon's proximity.
The phrase 'with its eye' may mean 'in the same heaven' or 'from our perspective'.
5
Note the author's conclusion
The passage ends by saying 'And Allah knows best', affirming that the true knowledge of the heavens belongs to Allah.
This humbly acknowledges the limits of human knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أهل النجوم: الشمس والقمر والنجوم في السماء الرابعة. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: في السماء الدنيا. يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا زَيَّنَّا السَّمَاءَ الدُّنْيَا بِزِينَةِ الْكَوَاكِبِ﴾. وقوله تعالى في قصة ذي القرنين: ﴿وَجَدَهَا تَغْرُبُ فِي عَيْنٍ حَمِئَةٍ﴾ وهو لم يبلغ السماء الرابعة. والله الهادي. أقول: الشمس والقمر والنجوم في السماء الدنيا خلاف أصل علم النجوم والتقويم. فإنهم قالوا ذلك جميعاً في السماء الرابعة. لكن المشهور عندهم أن القمر في السماء الدنيا والشمس في الرابعة. وأما النجوم: فزحل في السابعة والمريخ في السادسة والمشتري في الرابعة والزهرة في الثالثة وعطارد في الثالثة لنا؟ وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَقَدْ زَيَّنَّا السَّمَاءَ الدُّنْيَا بِزِينَةِ الْكَوَاكِبِ﴾ هو شامل الكل. والمراد بالزينة قيل منورها، وقيل أشكالها المختلفة كشكل الثريا والجوزاء. وقوله تعالى في قصة ذي القرنين: ﴿وَجَدَهَا تَغْرُبُ فِي عَيْنٍ حَمِئَةٍ﴾ وجه الاستدلال: أن ذا القرنين وجد الشمس تغرب في عين حمئة، ومن المعلوم أنه لم يبلغ السماء الرابعة. ولا نشاهد كسوف القمر بعينه في السماء الدنيا؟ ولا اطلاع لنا على ما في السماء الرابعة. والله أعلم.
The people of astrology said: The sun, the moon, and the stars are in the fourth heaven. The people of the Sunnah and the Community said: They are in the lowest heaven. Proof of this is His statement, exalted: 'Indeed We adorned the lowest heaven with the adornment of the stars.' And His statement, exalted, in the story of Dhu al-Qarnayn: 'He found it setting in a muddy spring' and he had not reached the fourth heaven. Allah is the Guide. I say: The sun, the moon, and the stars are in the lowest heaven, contrary to the principle of astrology and astronomy. For they claimed all of them are in the fourth heaven. However, it is well-known among them that the moon is in the lowest heaven and the sun in the fourth. As for the stars: Saturn is in the seventh, Mars in the sixth, Jupiter in the fourth, Venus in the third, and Mercury in the third for us? And His statement, exalted: 'And indeed We adorned the lowest heaven with the adornment of the stars' includes them all. By 'adornment' is meant, it is said, their light, and it is said, their different shapes like the form of the Pleiades and Gemini. And His statement, exalted, in the story of Dhu al-Qarnayn: 'He found it setting in a muddy spring' — the aspect of proof is that Dhu al-Qarnayn found the sun setting in a muddy spring, and it is known that he did not reach the fourth heaven. Nor do we witness the eclipse of the moon with its eye in the lowest heaven? And we have no knowledge of what is in the fourth heaven. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the astrologers' claim that the sun, moon, and stars reside in the fourth heaven. The author contrasts their view with that of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, who hold that these bodies are in the lowest heaven (al-sama' al-dunya). The proof is drawn from two Quranic verses: first, 'Indeed We adorned the lowest heaven with the adornment of the stars' (Quran 37:6? Actually 67:5? But the author cites 'إنا زينا السماء الدنيا بزينة الكواكب' which is similar to 37:6; the exact reference may be 37:6 or 67:5, but the point is clear); second, the story of Dhu al-Qarnayn who saw the sun setting in a muddy spring, indicating that he was observing the sun from earth and had not traveled to the fourth heaven. The author then notes that the astrologers' own system places the moon in the lowest heaven, contradicting their general claim. The details of planetary positions (Saturn, Mars, etc.) are given as per their system. The verse about adorning the lowest heaven includes all stars, and the 'adornment' is interpreted as their light or their distinct constellations like Pleiades and Gemini. The story of Dhu al-Qarnayn is used as evidence that the sun is perceived from the earth, not from a distant heaven. Finally, the author questions whether we can witness lunar eclipses from the lowest heaven, implying that our observation confirms the sun, moon, and stars are perceived from our vantage point, not from a higher sphere. The passage concludes by affirming that only Allah knows the unseen.

Key Terms
السماء الدنيا
السماء الرابعة
زينة الكواكب
ذو القرنين
عين حمئة
كسوف القمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Stars are in the fourth heaven
Correction: The Quran explicitly says they are in the lowest heaven, and the story of Dhu al-Qarnayn confirms that the sun is observed near earth.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse is used as a proof that the stars are in the lowest heaven?
A) إنا زينا السماء الدنيا بزينة الكواكب
B) وجدها تغرب في عين حمئة
C) ما أشهدتهم خلق السماوات والأرض
D) والله خلقكم وما تعملون

Key Takeaway
The Quran and the story of Dhu al-Qarnayn affirm that the stars are in the lowest heaven, refuting the astrological claim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever relied on astrology—even casually—for guidance about your future or character? In light of this lesson, what does your reliance on created bodies say about your trust in Allah's decree? Will you cut off that source of false knowledge today?
?
When you look up at the night sky, do you marvel at Allah's adornment and His direct closeness, or do you feel distant from Him? This lesson reminds us that the stars are in the lowest heaven, near to us. How does that reality change the way you turn to Allah in your daily struggles?

The Location of the Sun, Moon, and Stars in the Lowest Heaven
Imam Nasafi refutes astrologers using Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Ahl al-Sunna, the sun, moon, and stars are located in the lowest heaven, as proven by Quranic verses, contrary to the astrologers' claim.

Core Idea
Quranic revelation places celestial bodies in the lowest heaven, not the fourth.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses a cosmological disagreement between astrologers and Ahl al-Sunna. He asserts the primacy of Quranic evidence over astronomical speculation, using clear verses to settle the location of the sun, moon, and stars. This lesson presents his refutation and the scriptural proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing views
Read the opening lines to see the astrologers' claim (fourth heaven) versus Ahl al-Sunna's position (lowest heaven).
Notice that Nasafi states his own view after presenting the opposition.
2
Examine the first Quranic proof
Focus on the verse 'Indeed We adorned the lowest heaven with an adornment of stars.' Understand how this directly supports the Ahl al-Sunna view.
This verse (Quran 67:5) is the primary evidence.
3
Examine the second Quranic proof and the inference
Read the story of Dhul-Qarnayn and the sun setting in a muddy spring. Reflect on why this proves the sun is in the lowest heaven, not the fourth.
Nasafi also lists the astrologers' detailed positions to contrast with revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والله الهادي قال قال أهل النجوم: الشمس والقمر والنجوم في السماء الرابعة. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: في السما الدنيا. يدل عليه قوله تعالى: {إنا زينا السماء الدنيا بزينة الكواكب}. وقوله تعالى في قصة ذي القرنين: {وجدها تغرب في عين حمئة} وهو لم يبلغ السماء الراحة [؟]. والله الهادي. أقول: الشمس والقمر والنجوم في السما الدنيا خلاف أصل علم النجوم والتقويم فإنهم قالوا ذلك جميعًا في السماء الرابعة. دقيقه [؟] قطران [؟] المشهور عندهم: إن القمر في السماء الدنيا والشمس في الرابعة. وأما النجوم فزحل في السابعة والمريخ في السادسة والمشتري في الرابعة والزهرة في الثالثة وعطارد في الثالثة. لنا قوله تعالى: {ولقد زينا السماء الدنيا بزينة الكواكب} وهي شامل الكل. والمواد [؟] من الذنية [؟] قبل منوها [؟] د قيل أشكالها المختلفة لشكل الريا [؟] دينات نمش و الجوزاء [؟]. وقوله تعالى في قصة ذي القرنين: {وجدها تغرب في عين حمئة}. وجه الاستدلال: أن ذا القرنين وجد الشمس تغرب في عين حمئة، ومن المعلوم أنه لم يبلغ السماء الرابعة. ولا نحن نشاهد كسوف [؟] وانتمى رخوة [؟] القمر بعينانه [؟] في سما الدنيا ولا اطلاع لنا عليه وية [؟] ما في السماء الرابعة. والله تعالى أعلم.
And Allah is the Guide. He said: The astrologers said: The sun, the moon, and the stars are in the fourth heaven. And Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a said: In the lowest heaven. That is indicated by His saying, exalted is He: 'Indeed We adorned the lowest heaven with an adornment of stars' and His saying, exalted is He, in the story of Dhul-Qarnayn: 'He found it setting in a muddy spring' and he did not reach the heaven of rest [?]. And Allah is the Guide. I say: The sun, the moon, and the stars are in the lowest heaven, contrary to the principle of astrology and the calendar, for they said all that is in the fourth heaven. Its minute [?] detail [?] famous among them: That the moon is in the lowest heaven and the sun is in the fourth. As for the stars, Saturn is in the seventh, Mars in the sixth, Jupiter in the fourth, Venus in the third, and Mercury in the third. Our evidence is His saying: 'And We have certainly adorned the lowest heaven with stars' and it encompasses all. And the materials [?] from the dusty [?] before its mention [?] it was said their different forms for the form of [?] Gemini [?] and Orion [?]. And His saying in the story of Dhul-Qarnayn: 'He found it setting in a muddy spring.' The aspect of inference: that Dhul-Qarnayn found the sun setting in a muddy spring, and it is known that he did not reach the fourth heaven. And we do not witness an eclipse [?] and the sight [?] of the moon with its eyes [?] in the lowest heaven, and we have no knowledge of what is in the fourth heaven. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the astrologers' claim that the sun, moon, and stars are in the fourth heaven. Imam Nasafi begins by stating the two opposing views: the astrologers say they are in the fourth heaven, while Ahl al-Sunna say they are in the lowest heaven (sama' al-dunya). He then provides two Quranic proofs. The first is the verse: 'Indeed We adorned the lowest heaven with an adornment of stars' (Quran 67:5). The second is from the story of Dhul-Qarnayn, where he found the sun setting in a muddy spring (Quran 18:86). The inference is that Dhul-Qarnayn traveled on earth and did not ascend to the fourth heaven, so the sun he saw setting was in the lowest heaven. The author then gives his own statement, reiterating the Ahl al-Sunna position and listing the specific positions of planets according to the astrologers (e.g., Saturn in the seventh, Mars in the sixth, etc.) as a concession to their knowledge, but he insists on the Quranic evidence for the sun, moon, and stars being in the lowest heaven. The passage thus upholds the primacy of revelation over astronomical speculation.

Key Terms

أهل النجوم
أهل السنة والجماعة
زينة الكواكب
عين حمئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Astrologers claim that the sun, moon, and stars are in the fourth heaven.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna teach that they are in the lowest heaven, based on Quran 67:5 and the story of Dhul-Qarnayn.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, which Quranic verse is used to prove that the sun, moon, and stars are in the lowest heaven?
A) 'And the sun runs on its course to a resting place'
B) 'Indeed We adorned the lowest heaven with an adornment of stars'
C) 'And the heaven We built with might'
D) 'And the moon We have measured for it phases'

Key Takeaway
The sun, moon, and stars are all in the lowest heaven, as affirmed by the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a scientific claim that contradicts a clear Quranic verse, do you instinctively question the verse or the science? What would it take for you to submit fully to the Quranic text, even when it goes against dominant views?
?
Think of a time you prioritized human opinion or your own reasoning over a direct Quranic teaching. What was the outcome, and how does this lesson challenge you to change that pattern?
?
Are you willing to accept that the sun is in the lowest heaven, even if it feels counterintuitive? What does your answer reveal about the depth of your trust in Allah's revelation over human knowledge?

The Neutral State of Creation at the Covenant
Nasafi explains the initial neutrality and subsequent classification after the covenant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that human souls were created without belief or disbelief and that their response to the divine presentation determined their spiritual identity.

Core Idea
Humans were created neutral; faith and disbelief come from choice, not predestination at creation.

In this final section, Imam al-Nasafi clarifies the moment of the primordial covenant. He explains what exactly happened when Allah brought forth all human souls from Adam (AS). Far from being predetermined as believers or disbelievers, they were created without any attributes, and only after the presentation of faith and disbelief did their choices define them.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Note the author's decisive tone.
The passage begins with 'اعلم' (Know), signaling a definitive teaching.
2
Identify the three categories of response
The passage describes three possible outcomes after the presentation: believer (accepting with conviction), disbeliever (not choosing faith), and hypocrite (answering with speech without conviction).
Notice that the hypocrite is distinguished by lack of inner conviction.
3
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider why this teaching is important: it refutes the idea that humans were created already believers or disbelievers, emphasizing human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في بيان أن الله لما خلق الخلق لم يكونوا مؤمنين ولا كافرين

اعلم بأن الله تعالى لما خلق الخلق وأخرجهم من صلب آدم عليه السلام يوم الميثاق لم يكونوا مؤمنين ولا كافرين وكانوا خلقاً، ثم عرض عليهم الإيمان والكفر، وكل من اختار الإيمان وقبله اعتقاداً فهو مؤمن، وكل من لم يختر الإيمان فهو كافر، وكل من أجاب بالقول دون الاعتقاد فهو منافق بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنْ بَنِي آدَمَ مِن
Chapter
Concerning the explanation that when Allah created creation, they were not believers nor disbelievers

Know that when Allah Almighty created creation and brought them out from the loins of Adam (peace be upon him) on the Day of the Covenant, they were not believers nor disbelievers, but they were created. Then He presented to them faith and disbelief. And whoever chose faith and accepted it as conviction is a believer. And whoever did not choose faith is a disbeliever. And whoever answered with speech without conviction is a hypocrite, by the saying of the Almighty: 'And [mention] when your Lord took from the children of Adam from...'
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a new section (fadl) that explains the state of creation when Allah first brought them into existence. It clarifies that at the moment of creation, specifically at the Covenant (Day of Alast), humans were neither believers nor disbelievers; they were mere created beings. Then Allah presented them with the choice of faith and disbelief. Those who chose faith and accepted it with conviction became believers. Those who did not choose faith became disbelievers. And those who answered with their tongues but not with their hearts (i.e., without conviction) became hypocrites. The author then begins to cite the Quranic verse about the covenant, which continues the argument.

Key Terms
خلق
يوم الميثاق
إيمان
كفر
نفاق
اعتقاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think humans were created as believers or disbelievers from the very beginning of their existence.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that when Allah created them, they were not believers nor disbelievers; they were simply created. Their subsequent choices determined their spiritual state.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the state of humans when Allah first created them and brought them out from Adam's loins?
A) They were all believers.
B) They were all disbelievers.
C) They were neither believers nor disbelievers.
D) They were already destined for heaven or hell.

Key Takeaway
The first moment of existence was neutral; our choices defined our spiritual state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In which of the three categories do you truly belong today — a believer with conviction, a disbeliever who rejects faith, or a hypocrite who says the words but your heart is empty? What evidence from your daily life would you present to Allah to prove your category?
?
The passage says you were created neutral, then faith and disbelief were presented to you. When did you make your choice? Are you still choosing faith every day, or have you become complacent, assuming you are already a believer without active conviction?
?
If you honestly examine your heart, do you sometimes answer with speech without conviction, like a hypocrite? What specific area of your life is your faith merely verbal? What will you do today to turn that into true i'tiqad?

The Covenant Proof for Body and Soul
Nasafi explains the covenant verse as proof that God created bodies together with souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi uses the Quranic covenant verse to prove that Allah created human bodies and souls together from the beginning.

Core Idea
The covenant with God was made by body and soul together.

Imam Nasafi presents a proof from the Quran that the creation of body and soul was simultaneous. The famous verse of the covenant (Al-Mithaq) in Surah Al-A'raf is cited as evidence that the address was made to the complete human being, body and soul. This passage explains how the events of the covenant demonstrate that both were created at once.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse
Start by reading the verse fragment and its literal translation. Notice the context of the covenant: God takes the offspring from Adam's loins and makes them testify.
The verse is from Surah Al-A'raf 7:172.
2
Identify Nasafi's argument
Nasafi points out that the address 'Am I not your Lord?' was directed to bodies with souls. This shows that the entire human being, not just the soul, was present at the covenant.
This is the core of the proof.
3
Trace the narrative sequence
Follow the sequence: from the covenant, God returns them to the loins of their fathers, then brings out generations until the Day of Resurrection. This continuity reinforces the idea that body and soul remain together.
The phrase 'from their loins' supports the physical aspect.
4
Reflect on theological significance
Consider why this matters: if the covenant was with body and soul, then the soul is not pre-existent; both are created together. This refutes those who claim the soul existed before the body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّنَهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى شَهِدْنَا أَن تَقُولُوا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ إِنَّا كُنَّا عَنْ هَذَا غَفِلِينَ. ثم الدليل على أنَّ الله تعالى خلق الأجساد مع الأرواح كما هم الآن قوله تعالى: أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ والخطاب والسؤال للأجساد مع الأرواح، ثم ردهم إلى أصلاب آبائهم، ثم أخرج أولاد آدم منه، ثم أخرج أولاً أولاده من أولاده، هكذا إلى يوم القيامة؛ لأن الله تعالى قال: مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ.
From their loins their offspring and made them testify over themselves, 'Am I not your Lord?' They said, 'Yes, we testify.' [This was] lest you say on the Day of Resurrection, 'Indeed we were unaware of this.' Then the proof that God Most High created bodies with souls as they are now is His saying: 'Am I not your Lord?' and the address and question was to bodies with souls. Then He returned them to the loins of their fathers, then He brought out the children of Adam from him, then He brought out the first of his children from his children, and so on until the Day of Resurrection, because God Most High said: 'from their loins.'
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from the Quranic verse of the covenant (mithaq) that God created the body and soul together. The author begins by quoting Surah al-A'raf 7:172, which describes how God took the offspring from Adam's loins and made them testify to His Lordship. Then he explains that this verse is evidence that God created bodies and souls at the same time as they are now. The address 'Am I not your Lord?' was directed to the entirety of the human being, both body and soul. After the covenant, God returned them to the loins of their fathers, and then they are brought out generation after generation until the Day of Resurrection, as the verse says 'from their loins.' The argument is that the covenant event shows that souls and bodies were created together, because the testifiers had both body and soul at that moment.

الأجساد (al-ajsad)
الأرواح (al-arwah)

Correction: Nasafi argues the address was to bodies with souls, proving both were created together.

Key Takeaway
The covenant verse demonstrates that Allah created human beings as unified wholes of body and soul from the beginning.

?

?

The Quran's Superiority Lies in Its Composed Letters
Nasafi interprets two verses to affirm the Quran's superiority as composed letters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi defends the createdness of the Quran by interpreting key verses to affirm that the Quran's excellence refers to its composed letters, not an uncreated attribute.

Core Idea
The Quran's best speech is composed letters, not an uncreated attribute.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses an objection: if the Quran consists of letters and sounds, how can it be called the best speech? He interprets two Quranic verses to show that the Quran's superiority is precisely in its composed form, which is created yet superior to all created speech. This clarifies the Ash'ari position that the Quran is created (makhluq) but still the word of Allah in a metaphorical sense.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the objection
The objector might think that calling the Quran 'best speech' implies it is uncreated. Notice how Nasafi anticipates this by interpreting the verse about taking away the Quran.
2
Examine the first verse (Al-Mu'minun 18)
Nasafi interprets this verse as Allah's ability to remove Quranic preservation from hearts, implying the Quran is a physical text that can be lost.
3
Examine the second verse (Az-Zumar 23)
Nasafi explicitly states that 'the best speech' refers to the composed letters (al-huruf al-munthumah), and that these letters are superior to all created speech.
4
Understand the conclusion
By grounding Quranic excellence in its composition, Nasafi upholds the createdness of the Quran while still affirming its superiority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّا عَلَى ذَهَابِ بِهِ لَقَدِرُونَ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ۱۸] يعنى ذهاب حفظه من القلوب. وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿اللَّهُ نَزَّلَ أَحْسَنَ الْحَدِيثِ ﴾ [الزمر: ٢٣]. قلنا: المراد به الحروف المنظومة، وهو أحسن من كلام المخلوقين.
And His statement: 'And indeed We are able to take away it' [Al-Mu'minun:18] meaning the removal of its preservation from the hearts. And as for His statement: 'Allah has sent down the best speech' [Az-Zumar:23]. We say: what is meant by it is the composed letters, and it is better than the speech of creatures.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The author addresses an implied challenge: if the Quran is merely letters and sounds, how can it be called the best speech? The author first explains the verse about Allah's ability to take away the Quran, interpreting it as meaning He can remove its preservation from people's hearts. Then, for the verse that the Quran is the best speech, the author states that 'the best speech' refers to the composed letters (al-huruf al-munthumah), and these letters are superior to the speech of created beings. Thus, the Quran's excellence lies in its composition, not in being a non-created eternal attribute. This clarifies the author's position that the Quran is created (letters and sounds) yet superior.

Key Terms
الحروف المنظومة
أحسن الحديث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran being called 'best speech' means it must be uncreated and eternal.
Correction: Imam Nasafi clarifies that 'best speech' refers to its composed letters, which are created yet superior to all created speech.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does 'the best speech' in Quran 39:23 refer to?
A) The eternal attribute of speech
B) The composed letters
C) The preserved tablet
D) The Angel Jibril

Key Takeaway
The Quran's superiority is due to its composed letters, which are created yet superior to all other speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly believe these very letters are the best speech ever uttered? How does that belief change the way you recite and listen to it starting today?
?
The verse warns that Allah can remove the Quran from hearts. What concrete steps will you take this week to ensure you are actively preserving it in your own heart, not just reading passively?
?
If the Quran's superiority is in its composition, not an eternal mystery, does that make it more or less accessible to you? How will you honor its letters in your daily life from now on?

Refuting Proofs for Increase of Faith
Author refutes four scriptural proofs used to argue for increase of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical Sunni scholars reinterpret Quranic verses and hadiths that seem to indicate faith increases, without compromising the doctrine that faith is one and does not increase or decrease in its essence.

Core Idea
Quranic mentions of faith increase refer to certainty or reward, not the essence of faith.

This passage demonstrates the systematic refutation of arguments used to claim that faith can increase. The author takes on two verses and two hadiths, showing that each, when properly understood, does not imply a change in the reality of faith itself. By studying his method, you will learn how theological principles guide scriptural interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source and its English translation to get the overall structure of refutations. Notice how each objection is introduced with 'وأما'.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the four objections
List the four proofs the author responds to: two Quranic verses (al-Fath 4, al-Anfal 2) and two hadiths (Abu Bakr's precedence, the grain-of-barley hadith).
3
Analyze the author's hermeneutic
For each proof, note the specific interpretive move: restriction to Companions, distinguishing faith from certainty, distinguishing faith from reward, or reconciling variant narrations.
The underlying principle: faith (tasdiq) does not vary; only its fruits do.
4
Connect to the doctrine
Understand that the author's responses are consistent with the Maturidi definition of faith as unwavering attestation. What varies is obedience (ta'a), certainty (yaqin), or reward (thawab).
5
Synthesize the lesson
Reflect on how this method preserves core Aqeedah while engaging with apparent counter-evidence. Consider how you might apply similar reasoning to other texts.
This is a model for handling mutashabihat in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله تعالى: لِيَزْدَادُوا إِيمَانًا مَعَ إِيمَانِهِمْ [الفتح: ٤]. قلنا: ذلك في حق الصحابة رضي الله عنهم؛ لأن القرآن كان ينزل في كل وقت فيؤمنون به؛ فيكون تصديقهم الثاني زائدة على الأول، أما في حقنا فلا، لأنه انقطع الوحي. وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّمَا الْمُؤْمِنُونَ الَّذِينَ إِذَا ذُكِرَ اللَّهُ وَجِلَتْ قُلُوبُهُمْ وَإِذَا تُلِيَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ آيَاتُهُ زَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَانًا وَعَلَى رَبِّهِمْ يَتَوَكَّلُونَ ﴾ [الأنفال: ٢]. قلنا: ذلك صفة المؤمنين والمؤمنون في الطاعة متفاوتون، أما في الإيمان فلا. وأما قوله تعالى: زَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَانًا المراد به اليقين لا نفس الإيمان. وأما حديث أبي بكر قلنا: ذلك ترجيح في الثواب، لأنه سابق في الإيمان. وقد قال عليه السلام: «الدال على الخير كفاعله». وأما قوله عليه السلام: «يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثل شعيرة من الإيمان». قلنا: رُوِيَ في بعض الروايات يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه الإيمان مثل شعيرة فيجب حمله على هذا عملاً بما ذكرنا من الدلائل.
And as for His statement, the Exalted: 'That they may increase faith upon their faith' [al-Fath 4]. We said: That is concerning the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, because the Qur'an used to be revealed at every time and they would believe in it; so their second attestation is additional to the first. As for us, no, because revelation has ceased. And as for His statement, the Exalted: 'The believers are only those whose hearts tremble when Allah is mentioned, and when His verses are recited to them, they increase them in faith, and upon their Lord they rely' [al-Anfal 2]. We said: That is a description of the believers, and believers vary in obedience, but not in faith. And as for His statement, the Exalted: 'Increase them in faith' — what is meant by it is certainty (al-yaqin), not faith itself. And as for the hadith of Abu Bakr, we said: That is a preponderance in reward, because he preceded in faith. And he, peace be upon him, said: 'The one who guides to good is like the doer of it.' And as for his saying, peace be upon him: 'He will come out of the Fire who has in his heart the weight of a grain of barley of faith.' We said: It has been narrated in some narrations: 'He will come out of the Fire who has in his heart faith the weight of a grain of barley.' So it must be interpreted according to this, in accordance with the proofs we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a set of responses to objections against the position that faith does not increase or decrease. The author answers four proofs: two Quranic verses and two hadiths. For each, he provides an interpretation that preserves the doctrine that faith is one and does not increase or decrease. He explains that the increase mentioned in the first verse refers to the Companions due to new revelation, that the description of believers in the second verse refers to variation in obedience not in faith, that the word 'iman' in the verse 'increase them in faith' means certainty (al-yaqin), not faith itself, that Abu Bakr's precedence is in reward, and that the hadith about the grain of barley is interpreted as referring to the minimum faith that saves from eternal Fire, not that faith itself is a grain. He concludes that the hadith must be interpreted according to the established proofs.

Key Terms
إيمان
زيادة
يقين
تصديق
ثواب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Quranic verses and hadiths about increase of faith prove that the essence of faith (tasdiq) can increase or decrease.
Correction: The author shows that such passages refer to other realities: new attestations due to revelation, increase in obedience (ta'a), certainty (yaqin), or reward (thawab). Faith itself remains a single, unchanged attestation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the author's explanation for the hadith 'He will come out of the Fire who has in his heart a grain of barley of faith'?
A) It refers to the Companions only.
B) It is to be interpreted according to the narration that says 'faith the weight of a barley grain' and not as meaning faith itself is a grain.
C) It means that faith can be increased.
D) It abrogates the other verses.

Key Takeaway
Faith does not increase or decrease; scriptural expressions of increase refer to certainty, reward, or the context of ongoing revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author insists that the essence of your faith is no different from that of the Companions. Do you live as if that is true? If you truly believed this, would you feel more or less urgency to obey Allah? What is the one obedience you will perform today based on this certainty?
?
The lesson distinguishes between increasing in faith and increasing in certainty (yaqin). Is your certainty about the existence and attributes of Allah growing? Or is it stagnant? What specific step will you take today to increase your certainty?
?
The hadith about the grain of barley suggests that even minimal faith saves from eternal Fire. Does this comfort you into complacency, or does it drive you to ensure that your faith is not merely minimal? Examine your heart: are you satisfied with a mustard seed of faith, or are you pursuing the full reality of îmân? What will you sacrifice today to deepen your attachment to Allah?

Refuting the Denial of Hellfire Punishment
Nasafi refutes the Murji'ah belief that Hell contains no torment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic evidence that refutes the Murji'ah claim that Hell contains no torment.

Core Idea
The Quran itself proves that Hellfire punishment is real and eternal.

Some groups have tried to soften the reality of Hell, claiming it is merely a state without suffering. Imam Nasafi counters this dangerous idea with clear Quranic verses that describe the cries, tasting, and renewal of torment in Hell. Let's examine the evidence he presents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the full argument in one go.
Notice the strong opening declaration of falsehood.
2
Identify the false claim
Find the Murji'ah claim that the inhabitants are like fish in water without punishment.
This comparison is meant to normalize Hell.
3
Examine the four Quranic proofs
Each verse is a direct refutation. Focus on what each verse adds to the argument.
The verses escalate from crying for help to continuous skin replacement.
4
Reflect on the refutation's strength
Consider how the author uses the Quran itself to disprove the claim, not human reasoning.
This shows the authority of scripture in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الرد على من يقول: «ليس في النار عذاب» قالت المرجئة لعنهم الله: إذا دخل أهل النار النار، فإنهم يكونون في النار بلا عذاب، كالحوت في الماء، إلا أن الفرق بين الكافر والمؤمن أن للمؤمن استمتاعاً في الجنة بأكل وشرب، وأهل النار ليس لهم استمتاع في أكل وشرب. وهذا باطل، يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُمْ يَصْطَرِخُونَ فِيهَا رَبَّنَا أَخْرِجْنَا﴾ [فاطر: 37] وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿فَذَاقَتْ وَبَالَ أَمْرِهَا﴾ [الطلاق: 9] وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿وَنَادَوْا يَا مَالِكُ لِيَقْضِ عَلَيْنَا رَبُّكَ قَالَ إِنَّكُم مَّاكِثُونَ﴾ [الزخرف: 77] وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿كُلَّمَا نَضِجَتْ جُلُودُهُم بَدَّلْنَاهُمْ جُلُودًا غَيْرَهَا لِيَذُوقُوا الْعَذَابَ﴾ [النساء: 56].
Chapter on refuting those who say: 'There is no punishment in the Fire.' The Murji'ah, may Allah curse them, said: When the inhabitants of the Fire enter the Fire, they are in the Fire without punishment, like the fish in water, except that the difference between the disbeliever and the believer is that the believer has enjoyment in Paradise in eating and drinking, and the inhabitants of the Fire have no enjoyment in eating and drinking. This is false, and evidence for it is His saying: 'And they will cry out therein: Our Lord, remove us' [35:37]; and likewise His saying: 'So it tasted the evil consequence of its affair' [65:9]; and likewise His saying: 'And they will call: O Malik, let your Lord put an end to us. He will say: Indeed, you are staying' [43:77]; and likewise His saying: 'Whenever their skins are roasted through, We will replace them with other skins so they may taste the punishment' [4:56].
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage refutes the Murji'ah claim that the inhabitants of Hell will suffer no punishment, being like fish in water. The author declares this false and provides four Quranic proofs: the inhabitants cry out for removal from the Fire (35:37); they taste the evil consequence of their deeds (65:9); they call upon the angel Malik for death but are told they will remain (43:77); and their skins are replaced to continuously taste punishment (4:56). These verses directly contradict the Murji'ah assertion.

Key Terms
المرجئة
النار
العذاب
الصراخ
الذوق
تبديل الجلود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Murji'ah believe that Hell contains no punishment, only a lack of pleasure.
Correction: The Quran explicitly describes crying, tasting consequences, begging for death, and skin replacement, proving real and severe punishment.

Checkpoint

A) 35:37
B) 65:9
C) 43:77
D) 4:56

Key Takeaway
The Quran provides multiple clear proofs that Hellfire punishment is real, intense, and eternal, refuting any claim to the contrary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that Hellfire contains real and eternal torment as proven by four Quranic verses, does your life today reflect that belief? In what concrete way will you change your actions before tonight?
?

?

Children of Polytheists: Main Views and Muslim Children
Presenting positions on polytheists' children and a note on Muslim children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni and Mu'tazilite positions on the fate of polytheists' children, the reason for Abu Hanifa's cautious 'I do not know', and the Sunni view on children of Muslims.

Core Idea
The fate of children after death is a matter of scholarly debate rooted in conflicting texts.

This lesson presents the two main theological positions on the children of polytheists: the Sunni view that they are servants in Paradise and the Mu'tazilite view of eternal fire. We also examine Abu Hanifa's famous hesitation and the Sunni consensus on Muslim children being in Paradise.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening passage
Read the Arabic passage to get an overview of the positions on polytheists' children and the note on Muslim children.
2
Identify the Sunni and Mu'tazila positions
Note that Ahl al-Sunna say they are 'servants of Paradise', while the Mu'tazila say they are eternally in the Fire like their fathers.
These are the two opposing views.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's 'I do not know'
Abu Hanifa said 'I do not know' out of caution due to conflicting evidence. His student Muhammad ibn al-Hasan asserted that Allah does not punish without sin.
The footnote clarifies that Abu Hanifa's stance leans toward them not entering the Fire.
4
Learn about Muslim children
The Sunni doctrine holds that Muslim children are in Paradise, supported by many hadiths. Abu Hanifa initially refrained from judgment in his youth but later retracted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في حكم أطفال المشركين. قال أهل السنة والجماعة: أطفال المشركين خَدَمُ أهل الجنة. وقالت المعتزلة: حُكْمُهم كحُكْم آبائهم يُخلدون في النار. واختلف علماء أهل السنة والجماعة في هذه المسألة. قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله: «لا أدري أهم في الجنة أم في النار؟» وقال محمد بن الحسن رحمه الله: «إني أعلم أنَّ الله تعالى لا يعذَّب أحدًا من غير ذنب». وإنما قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى: «لا أدري» احتياطاً لتعارض الأدلة. (١) هذه إشارة منه إلى أن أطفال المشركين لا يدخلون النار. (٢) مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة أن أطفال المسلمين يكونون في الجنة، وقد رويت في ذلك أحاديث كثيرة، وقد رُوي عن أبي حنيفة أنه كان يتوقف في أطفال المسلمين أيضًا، وقد كان هذا وقت شبابه، ولكنه رجع عن ذلك فيما بعد. وقد وقع الاختلاف في أطفال المشركين فقالوا بعضهم: خدام أهل الجنة، وقال بعضهم: هم أصحاب الأعراف، وقال بعضهم يمتحنون يومَ القيامة، فمَنْ كان من أهل السعادة أجاب ومن كان من أهل الشقاوة لم يجب، وردوا هذا القول بأن الآخرة ليست دار ابتلاء وتكليف، بل هي دار جزاء وحساب. وقيل: من آمن يوم الميثاق هو من أهل الجنة، ومن لم يؤمن فهو من أهل النار. ومنهم من قال: أمرهم إلى الله إن شاء عذبهم وإن شاء عفا عنهم.
Chapter on the ruling on children of polytheists. Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said: The children of polytheists are servants of the people of Paradise. The Mu'tazila said: Their ruling is like the ruling of their fathers; they will be eternally in the Fire. The scholars of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a differed on this issue. Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'I do not know whether they are in Paradise or in the Fire.' And Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'Indeed I know that Allah the Exalted will not punish anyone without sin.' And indeed Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, only said 'I do not know' out of caution due to conflicting evidence. (1) This is an indication from him that the children of polytheists do not enter the Fire. (2) The doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a is that the children of Muslims are in Paradise, and many hadiths have been narrated regarding that, and it has been narrated that Abu Hanifa used to refrain from judgment regarding Muslim children as well, and this was in his youth, but he later retracted it. And disagreement occurred regarding the children of polytheists: some said they are servants of the people of Paradise, some said they are inhabitants of al-A'raf (the Heights), and some said they will be tested on the Day of Resurrection; whoever is among the people of bliss will answer, and whoever is among the people of misery will not answer, and this opinion was rejected on the grounds that the Hereafter is not a place of trial and obligation, but rather a place of recompense and reckoning. And it was said: whoever believed on the Day of the Covenant is among the people of Paradise, and whoever did not believe is among the people of the Fire. And among them are those who said: Their matter is for Allah; if He wills, He punishes them, and if He wills, He forgives them.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This is a chapter on a doctrinal issue concerning the fate of children who die before reaching the age of responsibility, specifically the children of polytheists. It first states the position of Ahl al-Sunna: these children will be servants in Paradise. Then it presents the Mu'tazilite view: they will be eternally in Hell like their parents. The author then notes that Sunni scholars themselves disagreed. Abu Hanifa famously said 'I do not know' whether they are in Paradise or Hell, out of caution due to conflicting evidence. His student Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, however, asserted that Allah does not punish anyone without sin, which implies that these children, having committed no sin, will not be punished. The text then explains that Abu Hanifa's caution was due to conflicting evidence from scriptures. Then it lists other opinions: some say they are servants of Paradise, some say they dwell on al-A'raf (a place between Heaven and Hell), some say they will be tested on Judgment Day (but this is rejected because the Hereafter is not a place of trial), some say their fate is tied to whether they believed in the pre-eternal covenant, and some leave the matter entirely to Allah's will. This passage highlights the range of legitimate scholarly difference within Sunni Islam on this speculative matter.

Key Terms
أطفال المشركين
خدم أهل الجنة
المعتزلة
لا أدري
احتياط
أطفال المسلمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Abu Hanifa's 'I do not know' indicates doubt about Allah's justice.
Correction: The text explains it was caution (احتياط) due to conflicting evidence, not doubt about justice.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Ahl al-Sunna regarding children of Muslims?
A) They are in a state of limbo
B) They are in Paradise
C) They are servants of the people of Paradise
D) They are tested on the Day of Resurrection

Key Takeaway
The Sunni tradition affirms that Muslim children are in Paradise, while the fate of polytheists' children is debated, with Abu Hanifa exercising caution due to conflicting texts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the fate of children who die before reaching accountability, do you find yourself trusting more in your own sense of justice or in what Allah has revealed? What does your answer reveal about your reliance on scripture versus intellect?
?
Abu Hanifa was willing to say 'I do not know' when faced with conflicting evidence. Is there an area of your faith where you have been pretending to have certainty when you actually have doubts? How might honesty like Abu Hanifa's actually strengthen your iman?
?
The Mu'tazila insisted that God must punish the children of polytheists because it is 'just' in their view. Have you ever imposed your own standard of justice on Allah, feeling that something He did or didn't do was unfair? How does this passage challenge that tendency?

Sunni Internal Disagreements on Polytheists' Children
Enumerating multiple Sunni views on the fate of polytheists' children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various Sunni opinions on the fate of polytheists' children and the theological principles underlying each view.

Core Idea
Sunni scholars hold multiple valid views on polytheists' children, from Paradise to Allah's will.

While the broad Sunni position is known, the internal scholarly discussion on polytheists' children is remarkably diverse. This lesson explores the different views recorded in the tradition, including the idea of servants in Paradise, inhabitants of al-A'raf, a test on the Day of Resurrection, the pre-eternal covenant, and leaving the matter to Allah. Each view reflects a careful engagement with scripture and divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage listing the opinions
Read the Arabic passage that enumerates the different Sunni opinions on children of polytheists.
2
Understand the first two opinions
Some say they are servants of Paradise, others say they are inhabitants of al-A'raf (the Heights).
Al-A'raf is a place between Heaven and Hell.
3
Examine the testing opinion and its rejection
Some propose a test on the Day of Resurrection, but this is rejected because the Hereafter is not a place of trial.
This shows the principle that judgment is not ongoing.
4
Consider the covenant and leaving to Allah
Another view ties fate to belief in the pre-eternal covenant, while some leave it entirely to Allah's will.
These represent a spectrum from definite to agnostic positions.
5
Reflect on the range of legitimate difference
Note that all these views are within Sunni tradition, showing the scope for scholarly disagreement on speculative matters.

Source Text

Why was the opinion that children of polytheists will be tested on the Day of Resurrection rejected?
A) Because there are no children there

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows diversity on a matter Allah has not clearly revealed. When you face uncertainty in your faith, do you react with humility and trust, or with anxiety and a demand for clear answers? What would it mean for you to truly accept 'أمرهم إلى الله' in your own life?
?
The testing opinion is rejected because the Hereafter is not a place of trial. Is there an area where you expect Allah to act contrary to what He has revealed about His own justice or mercy? Are you willing to realign your expectations with His principles, even when they challenge your assumptions?
?
Scholars left the fate of these children to Allah's will. Can you entrust the final judgment of others—especially those whose actions you find troubling—to Allah without feeling the need to condemn or excuse them? What would that look like in your daily interactions?

Types of Addressees: Angels and Devils
Nasafi enumerates the four addressee types and details the fate of angels and devils.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four types of beings addressed by religion and the specific rulings regarding angels and devils, including their punishment and reward.

Core Idea
Angels can sin and be punished, but devils are all doomed to Hell.

In this section, Nasafi lays out the categories of beings that are addressed by divine commandments. He then focuses on the fates of angels and devils, showing that even angels can be subject to punishment for disbelief or sin, while devils are collectively condemned. This passage establishes that all rational beings are accountable, but their outcomes differ based on their actions and nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the four types of addressees: angels, humans, jinn, and devils.
The text then provides details for angels, devils, and humans; the fate of jinn is not elaborated.
2
Examine the angelic cases
Focus on the three subcategories of angels: those with disbelief (like Iblis), those with sins (like Harut and Marut), and those with obedience. Understand the outcome for each.
The story of Harut and Marut is given as proof that angels can be punished for sins.
3
Note the fate of devils
Observe that all devils are from the people of the Fire, without exception.
This contrasts with angels, who may be punished or rewarded depending on their deeds.
4
Reflect on humans and the poem
Read the brief statement about humans and the poetic summary. Consider why the author includes this poetic summary.
The poem is a mnemonic but contains unclear wording ('قيلمع').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في بيان أنواع المخاطبين بالدين
ثم المخاطبون أربعة أصناف الملائكة، وبنو آدم، والجن والشياطين. أما الملائكة: فكلُّ من وُجِدَ منه الكفر فهو من أهل النار وعليه العقاب كإبليس عليه اللعنة، وكل من وُجِدَ منه المعاصي لا الكفر فعليه العقاب. دليله قصة هاروت وماروت (۱) ، وكل مَنْ وُجِدَ منه الطَّاعة فهو من أهل الجنة ولا ثواب له.
وأما الشَّياطين فكلهم من أهل النار، وأما بنو آدم فكلهم من أهل الجنة إذا كانوا مؤمنين.
وقد جمع بعضهم هذه الأقوال في هذين البيتين قائلاً:
لقد قال أهل العلم في طفل بأعراف إمساك مشيئة ربهم
وفي جنة في النار وقف ومحنة تراب وخدام وقيلمع أصلهم
(۱) ورد بالنسخة (ج) تعليق صورته: «هاروت وماروت ملكان أنزلهما الله تعالى في الأرض ليقولا إن ما فعله بعض الناس سِحْرُ لا معجزة، وليس الساحر نبيًا، فطلب الناس منهم تعلم السحر ليفرق الساحر من النبي عليه السلام فعلَّما الناسَ السِّحر لأن السحر قد فشى في ذلك الزمان، واشتغل الناس بالسحر، واستنبطوا أمورًا كثيرًا منه وأكثروا دعوى النبوة، فبعث الله تعالى هذين الملكين ليقولا : إن ما يفعله بعض الناس سحر حتى يعلم الناس السحر والمعجزة والفرق بينهما، فعلّما الناس السحر حتى يتمكن بعض الناس من معارضة السَّحَرة الكفرة، فعاتبهما الله تعالى لتعليمهما الناس السحر». شرح المواقف وشرح المقاصد».}
Section on explaining the types of those addressed by the religion. Then the addressees are four kinds: the angels, the descendants of Adam, the jinn, and the devils. As for the angels: whoever among them is found to have disbelief is from the people of the Fire and upon him is punishment, like Iblis (upon him be curse). And whoever among them is found to have sins but not disbelief, upon him is punishment. Its proof is the story of Harut and Marut (1). And whoever among them is found to have obedience is from the people of Paradise but has no reward. As for the devils, all of them are from the people of the Fire. As for the descendants of Adam, all of them are from the people of Paradise if they are believers. And some have collected these sayings in these two verses, saying: 'Indeed, the people of knowledge have said about a child with customs, holding the will of their Lord, and in a garden in fire, pause and trial, dust and servants and [؟] with their origin.' (1) In copy (j) there is a comment whose form is: 'Harut and Marut are two angels whom Allah sent down to the earth to say that what some people do is sorcery, not a miracle, and the sorcerer is not a prophet. So people asked them to learn sorcery to distinguish the sorcerer from the prophet, upon him peace. So they taught people sorcery because sorcery had spread in that time, and people occupied themselves with sorcery, and they deduced many things from it and increased the claim of prophethood. So Allah sent these two angels to say that what some people do is sorcery so that people might know sorcery and the miracle and the difference between them. So they taught people sorcery so that some people could oppose the disbelieving sorcerers. So Allah reproached them for teaching people sorcery.' From Sharh al-Mawaqif and Sharh al-Maqasid.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage classifies the beings addressed by the religion into four types: angels, humans, jinn, and devils. The author first states the general classification, then details the fate of each. For angels: anyone found guilty of disbelief (kufr) is destined for Hell and punishment, exemplified by Iblis. Anyone guilty of sins (ma'asi) but not disbelief faces punishment as well, citing the story of Harut and Marut as proof—the footnote explains that these two angels were sent to teach sorcery to distinguish it from miracles, and were reproached. Angels who obey are in Paradise but receive no reward, because their obedience is their nature. Devils are all in Hell. Humans are all in Paradise if they are believers, but no mention of reward here. The author then notes that some scholars have summarized these rulings in two lines of poetry, though the second line is unclear.

إبليس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All angels are sinless and cannot be punished.
Correction: The passage shows that angels can commit sins (like Harut and Marut) and be punished, and Iblis is an angel who fell due to disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the fate of an angel who commits sins but not disbelief?
A) He is from the people of Paradise with reward.
B) He is from the people of the Fire with punishment.
C) He is from the people of Paradise without reward.
D) He is not subject to any judgment.

Key Takeaway
Angels are accountable and can be punished for sin or disbelief, while devils are universally condemned; human salvation depends on faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Iblis, a high-ranking angel, fell into disbelief due to arrogance, where is the seed of such arrogance in my own heart? Ask Allah to purify it today.
?
Harut and Marut sinned despite being angels. I often make excuses for my small sins. When will I truly fear the punishment that even angels could not escape?
?
The angels who obey receive no reward—their obedience is expected. Am I satisfied with merely avoiding Hell, or do I yearn for the reward that comes from faith and deeds?

The Reward of Jinn and the Scholarly Debate
Nasafi outlines the dispute over jinn reward with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different positions among early scholars on whether jinn receive reward for obedience, and the rational and textual arguments behind each view.

Core Idea
Scholars differed on jinn reward, rooted in whether reward is deserved by analogy or granted by text.

Nasafi presents a nuanced theological debate about the fate of jinn. While all agree that believing jinn enter Paradise, a key disagreement arises: do they receive reward (thawab) for their obedience? This passage introduces the positions of Abu Hanifa, his students, and al-Shafi'i, along with the logical and scriptural proofs each side employs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the basic ruling on jinn
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note that Nasafi first states the general rule: disbelieving jinn are in Hell, believing jinn are in Paradise.
This establishes the common ground before the dispute.
2
Find the disagreement on reward
Look for the names Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i. Identify who says jinn have no reward and who says they have reward.
Abu Hanifa says no reward; the other three say reward.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's qiyas argument
Read the analogy: a servant does not deserve wages from a master. The exception for humans is based on transmitted evidence (athar), not analogy. Without such evidence for jinn, the original principle applies.
This is a core legal principle in kalam.
4
Examine the opposing proof
The other scholars argue that if jinn are punished for sin, they must be rewarded for obedience. They also cite Quran 46:31 as evidence of forgiveness.
Notice the difference between qiyas and textual proof.
5
Learn additional characteristics of jinn
The passage ends with details: jinn do not eat or drink, but nourish by smell; they reproduce like humans. This leads to the next topic of devil offspring.
These details ground the discussion in physical reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجنُّ : فكلُّ مَنْ وُجِدَ منه الكفر فهو من أهل النار، وكل من تاب وآمن فله الجنة، ولا ثواب له عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله كالملائكة.
وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد والشافعي رحمهم الله لهم الثواب، والحجة لأبي حنيفة رحمه الله القياس وهو أن لا يستحق العبد الثواب على الله تعالى بالطاعة، إِلَّا أَنَّ الأثر ورَد في بني آدم فصار معدولًا عن القياس، لأن العبد إذا عمل للمولى لا يستحق الأجرة منه إذا عمل للمولى (١) وكلُّ من يقول بأنه يستحق الثّواب بالطاعة فعليه الدليل، إلَّا أنَّ الله تعالى وعَدَهم بأن يغفر لهم ذنوبهم إذا تابوا.
يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿ يَقَوْمَنَا أَجِيبُوا دَاعِيَ اللهِ وَعَامِنُوا بِهِ، يَغْفِرْ لَكُم مِّن ذُنُوبِكُمْ وَيُحركُم مِنْ عَذَابٍ أَلِيمٍ ﴾ [الأحقاف: ۳۱].
وحجتهم إذا كان لهم العقوبة عند المعاصي علمنا أن لهم الثواب على الطاعة، وليس لهم أكل وشُرْبٌ ، ولكن لهم شَمٌ، وذلك غذاءٌ لهم، ولهم التناسل كما في بني آدم وما يتصل بهذا الفصل في معرفة نَسْلِ الشَّياطين
As for the jinn: whoever among them is found to have disbelief is from the people of the Fire, and whoever repents and believes will have Paradise, but there is no reward for him according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, like the angels. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them, said: They have reward. The proof for Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, is analogy (qiyas), which is that the servant does not deserve reward from Allah Almighty through obedience, except that the transmitted report (athar) came regarding the descendants of Adam, so it deviated from the analogy, because the servant, when he works for the master, does not deserve wages from him when he works for the master. And whoever says that he deserves reward through obedience, the proof is upon him. Except that Allah Almighty promised them that He will forgive their sins if they repent. That is indicated by His saying, may He be exalted: 'O our people, respond to the caller of Allah and believe in him; He will forgive you some of your sins and protect you from a painful punishment' [Al-Ahqaf: 31]. And their proof is that if they have punishment for sins, we know that they have reward for obedience. And they (jinn) have no eating or drinking, but they have smelling, and that is their sustenance, and they have reproduction as in the descendants of Adam. And what is connected to this section regarding knowledge of the offspring of the devils.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage focuses on the jinn and the debate about whether obedient jinn receive reward. The author first states the basic rule: jinn who disbelieve are in Hell; those who repent and believe enter Paradise. Then a dispute is introduced: Abu Hanifa holds that jinn receive no reward (thawab) for their obedience, similar to angels. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad (al-Shaybani), and al-Shafi'i hold that they do receive reward. Abu Hanifa's proof is based on analogy (qiyas): a servant does not inherently deserve wages from a master for work; reward is a gratuitous gift, not a right. However, an exception was made for humans based on transmitted evidence, so the analogy is set aside for humans. For jinn, there is no such evidence, so the original principle applies. Those who claim reward must provide proof. Yet Allah did promise forgiveness for those who repent, as cited in Quran 46:31, which implies they may still be forgiven. The opposing argument: if jinn are punished for sins, they should be rewarded for obedience. The passage then provides additional information about jinn: they do not eat or drink but nourish by smelling, and they reproduce like humans. This leads into the next topic about devil offspring.

Key Terms
الجن
الثواب
القياس
الأثر
الطاعة
شَم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The debate over jinn reward is a minor speculative issue without practical implication.
Correction: The debate actually rests on a fundamental principle of kalam: whether obedience inherently merits reward (istihqaq) or whether reward is purely a gratuitous favor (tafaddul). This has broader implications for Divine justice and mercy.

Checkpoint
What is Abu Hanifa's main argument that jinn do not receive reward for obedience?
A) Jinn are not capable of earning reward.
B) The Quran explicitly denies reward to jinn.
C) By analogy, servants do not deserve wages from a master; the exception for humans is textual, not analogical.
D) Jinn are not obligated to obey Allah.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over jinn reward hinges on whether reward is deserved by analogical reasoning (qiyas) or granted by textual evidence (athar), with Abu Hanifa applying the default principle of no inherent right to reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if your good deeds obligate Allah to reward you? Abu Hanifa's analogy shows that even worship does not create a debt. How would your relationship with Allah change if you truly believed every reward is a free gift, not a wage? What one entitlement will you let go of today?
?
The scholars differed on jinn reward based on text versus analogy. Are there areas of your faith where you trust your own reasoning over what Allah has clearly revealed? What specific step will you take this week to submit your intellect to the Qur'an and Sunnah, even when it challenges your logic?

Controversies on Reproduction of Devils
Nasafi recounts and evaluates narrations on devil reproduction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the conflicting narrations about how devils reproduce and why scholars critically evaluate such reports.

Core Idea
Scholars critically evaluate narrations about devils, rejecting unsound ones.

Islamic scholarship preserves reports about the unseen world, including the nature of devils. But not all reports are accepted. In this passage, Nasafi presents several conflicting narrations about how devils reproduce, weighing their authenticity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation to get a sense of the different reports about devil reproduction.
Pay attention to how Nasafi evaluates each narration.
2
Identify the three methods
List the three methods described: egg-laying, self-copulation, and anal insertion.
Notice that only the first is deemed correct; the others are anomalous or false.
3
Examine the evaluation
See how Nasafi labels the second narration as 'shādhah' (anomalous) and the third as 'ghayr ṣaḥīḥ' (not correct).
This shows the critical approach to transmitted reports.
4
Reflect on Ibn Abbas' statement
The passage ends with a quote from Ibn Abbas about the brides of devils; consider its significance in context.
It may relate to the overall topic of devils' nature.
5
Consider the broader lesson
This passage demonstrates that not all reports about the unseen are accepted; Islamic scholarship applies rigorous criteria.
Connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيل : إنها تبيض بيضاتٍ فيخرج منها الولد، وهذا هو الصحيح.
وقد جاء في الخبر أنَّ الشَّياطين إذا فرحوا على معصية بني آدم تبيض بيضات فيخرج منها الولد، وقد جاء في الخبر أنَّ في إحدى فخذيه فرجا وفي الآخر ذكرًا، فيجامع مع نفسه فيخرج منها الولد، وهذه رواية شاذة.
وقد جاء في الخبر: أنه يُدخل ذَكَرَه في دبره فيخرج منه الولد، وهذا غير صحيح، والصحيح هو الأول.
وعن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أنه قال: ثلث عروس الشياطين: النائحة،
It was said: They (the devils) lay eggs and from them the child emerges, and this is the correct view. And it has come in the report that the devils, when they rejoice at the disobedience of the descendants of Adam, they lay eggs and from them the child emerges. And it has come in the report that in one of his thighs is a female organ and in the other is a male organ, so he copulates with himself and from that the child emerges, and this is an anomalous narration. And it has come in the report that he inserts his penis into his anus and from that the child emerges, and this is not correct, and the correct is the first. And from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: One third of the brides of the devils are the wailing woman (al-na'iha),
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage addresses the reproduction of devils (shayatin), presenting several narrations and evaluating their authenticity. The author states that the correct opinion is that devils lay eggs from which offspring emerge. One report states that when devils rejoice over human sin, they lay eggs. Another anomalous (shadhdha) narration claims that a devil has both male and female organs on opposite thighs and self-copulates. Yet another report says the devil inserts his penis into his anus to produce offspring—this is declared incorrect. The author affirms the first view as sound. Finally, a statement from Ibn Abbas is quoted: 'One third of the brides of the devils are the wailing woman (al-na'iha).' The text cuts off here. The author seems to be collecting various beliefs about devil biology and rejecting the more fantastical ones.

رواية شاذة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that all reports about devils are equally valid or that any narration about the unseen is automatically accepted.
Correction: This passage shows that scholars critically evaluate narrations, rejecting those that are anomalous (shādhah) or clearly incorrect, and affirming only what is supported by sound evidence.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Nasafi affirms that devils reproduce by laying eggs, rejecting other reports as weak.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Two Types of Reckoning: Presentation and Scrutiny
Nasafi distinguishes حساب العرض from حساب المناقشة and specifies who is exempt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between the reckoning of presentation (al-ʿarḍ) and the reckoning of scrutiny (al-munāqasha), and which groups are exempt from scrutiny.

Core Idea
Not everyone is questioned in detail; some are granted mercy through presentation alone.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi addresses a key aspect of the afterlife: the reckoning. He explains that there are two types—one is mere presentation of deeds with forgiveness, the other is detailed questioning. He also specifies who is spared the intense scrutiny, offering a glimpse of divine mercy for specific groups.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's classification of reckoning types and exempt groups become clear.
Notice the contrast between presentation and scrutiny.
2
Identify the exempt groups
List the three groups that are exempt from scrutiny: prophets, children of believers, and the ten promised Paradise. Notice the repetition of 'no reckoning, no punishment, no questioning of the grave' for each.
The ten promised Paradise are the Ashara Mubashshara.
3
Distinguish the two reckonings
Compare the descriptions: presentation reckoning says 'You did such-and-such, and I have forgiven you'; scrutiny reckoning asks 'Why did you do such-and-such?' Understand the difference in tone and outcome.
Presentation implies forgiveness; scrutiny implies accountability.
4
Reflect on divine mercy
Ask yourself: Why might these groups be exempt? What does this teach about Allah's mercy and the status of prophets, innocent children, and those promised Paradise?
This connects to the broader theme of hope in divine mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان الحساب والعرض ثم إن الأنبياء ليس عليهم حساب ولا عذاب ولا سؤال القبر وكذلك أطفال المؤمنين ليس عليهم حساب ولا عذاب ولا سؤال القبر وكذلك العشرة الذين بشرهم الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم بالجنة ليس عليهم حساب هذا كله حساب المناقشة أما حساب العرض للأنبياء والصحابة جميعا يقال فعلت كذا وعفوت عنك وحساب المناقشة يقال لم فعلت كذا
Chapter on explaining the reckoning and presentation. Then the prophets have no reckoning, no punishment, and no questioning of the grave; likewise the children of the believers have no reckoning, no punishment, and no questioning of the grave; likewise the ten who were given glad tidings of Paradise by the Messenger of Allah ﷺ have no reckoning. All of this is the reckoning of scrutiny. As for the reckoning of presentation for the prophets and the Companions collectively, it is said: 'You did such-and-such, and I have forgiven you.' And the reckoning of scrutiny is said: 'Why did you do such-and-such?'
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage classifies the two types of reckoning on the Day of Judgment: presentation (العرض) and scrutiny (المناقشة). It first lists those who are exempt from scrutiny: the prophets, the children of believers, and the ten Companions promised Paradise. For them, there is no punishment and no questioning in the grave. Then it defines the two types: presentation reckoning is when deeds are shown but the person is forgiven; scrutiny reckoning is when a person is asked why they committed a sin. The passage implies that the general believers may face some form of scrutiny but not these special groups.

Key Terms
حساب العرض
حساب المناقشة
سؤال القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think all believers face the same intense questioning on the Day of Judgment.
Correction: This passage shows that prophets, children of believers, and the ten promised Paradise are exempt from the reckoning of scrutiny. They either have a mere presentation with forgiveness or no reckoning at all.

Checkpoint

A) Prophets
B) Children of believers
C) The ten promised Paradise
D) The general Companions

Key Takeaway
Prophetic mercy and divine favor exempt certain groups from detailed scrutiny, reminding believers of Allah's boundless mercy and the special status of the prophets, innocent children, and those promised Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you living today as if you will face the detailed scrutiny of المناقشة, or are you assuming you will be among those who receive only the gentle العرض? What evidence in your actions supports that assumption?
?

?
Imagine the prophets and the ten promised Paradise—they were not exempt because they were carefree, but because of their utmost sincerity. Does your heart race with the same urgency to earn Allah's pleasure, or are you complacent, hoping for mercy without effort?
