Why We Don't See Devils, Jinn, and Angels, and the True Source of Sin
Nasafi answers objections about unseen beings and the soul's role in sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic theological explanations for why certain unseen beings are hidden from human sight, and how the devil's whispering works together with the human soul in leading to sin.

Core Idea
Devils are concealed as mercy; jinn from wind; angels from light; sin arises from soul's inclination activated by devil's whisper.

This lesson addresses two common objections about the unseen world. First, why do devils see us while we do not see them? Second, if the soul already inclines to evil, what role does the devil play? Imam al-Nasafi provides concise answers based on divine wisdom and Quranic testimony.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and first answer
Start by reading the opening objection about devils seeing us while we don't see them, and the answer that they are created in an ugly form and veiled as a mercy so we can eat and drink.
Notice that the answer emphasizes divine mercy.
2
Understand explanations for jinn and angels
The passage then explains why jinn (created from wind, which is invisible) and angels (created from light, which would overwhelm us) are also unseen. Compare the reasons.
Each reason is based on the substance of creation.
3
Reflect on the second objection about the soul
The next objection claims that the self (nafs) alone causes sin. Read carefully how Nasafi affirms this but adds the crucial role of the devil's whispering.
This preserves both human responsibility and devil's influence.
4
Connect the answer to the Quranic verse
Finish by reading the Quranic verse cited (Surah al-Nas 114:4) and see how it supports the answer: the devil whispers in people's breasts.
This grounds the theological point in revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : أَيش الحكمة في أنهم يروننا ونحن لا نراهم؟ قلنا : لأنهم خُلِقُوا على صورة قبيحة، فلو رأيناهم لم نقدر على تناول الطعام والشراب فستروا عنا رحمة من الله تعالى. وأما الجن خُلِقُوا من الريح، وأصل الريح لا يرى فكذلك ما خلق منه. وأما الملائكة خُلِقُوا من النُّور، فلو رأيناهم لطارت أرواحنا وأنفسنا. وأما قوله : بأن النفس توقعهم في المعاصي. قلنا: نعم، ولكن بواسطة وسوسة الشيطان، قال الله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِي يُوَسْوِسُ فِي صُدُورِ النَّاسِ ﴾
If it is said: What is the wisdom that they see us and we do not see them? We say: Because they were created in an ugly form, so if we saw them, we would not be able to eat and drink. So they were veiled from us as a mercy from Allah Most High. As for the jinn: they were created from wind, and the substance of wind is not seen; likewise what is created from it. As for the angels: they were created from light; if we saw them, our souls (arwāḥ) and ourselves (anfus) would fly away. And as for his statement 'that the self (nafs) causes them to fall into sins', we say: yes, but by means of the whispering of the devil, as Allah said: 'who whispers in the breasts of people.'
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer passage. It begins with an objection (فإن قيل) asking for the wisdom behind the fact that devils see humans while humans do not see them. The answer is that devils were created in an ugly form; if humans saw them, they would be unable to eat and drink due to fear or disgust. Therefore, devils are veiled as a mercy from Allah. The author then adds explanations for two other unseen beings: jinn and angels. Jinn are created from wind, which is itself invisible, so their origin explains their invisibility. Angels are created from light; if humans saw them, their souls would fly away—suggesting that the vision would be overwhelming. Finally, the author addresses another objection: that it is the human self (nafs), not the devil, that leads to sins. The answer is that this is true—the self does incite sin—but it does so only by means of the devil's whispering (waswasah), which is supported by the Quranic verse (Surah al-Nas 114:4) that describes the devil as 'the one who whispers in the breasts of people.' Thus, the passage maintains the role of the devil while acknowledging the role of the soul.

Key Terms
الحكمة
صورة قبيحة
الجن
الريح
الملائكة
النور
النفس
وسوسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Not seeing devils is a weakness or failure; the soul alone is responsible for sin.
Correction: The passage explains that devils are hidden as a mercy (not a weakness), and while the soul does cause sin, it does so through the devil's whispering, as per the Quran.

Checkpoint
What is the wisdom given for why humans do not see devils?
A) Devils are made of light and would blind us
B) Devils are made of wind and are inherently invisible
C) Devils have an ugly form that would prevent us from eating and drinking
D) Devils are not real beings

Key Takeaway
Unseen beings are hidden by divine wisdom, and sin results from the soul's inclination activated by the devil's whispering.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you honestly blame your own soul's inclination before blaming the devil? How will you take full responsibility for your choices starting today?
?
The sight of devils is veiled from you as mercy so you can eat and drink. Are you grateful for this mercy? Do you ever pause to thank Allah for protecting you from seeing their ugliness?
?
The devil whispers in your chest without you seeing him. What specific steps will you take this week to guard your heart against those whispers, such as consistent remembrance (dhikr) and seeking refuge in Allah?

Why We Don't See Jinn and Angels, and the Role of Satan in Sin
Answers why jinn/angels are hidden and clarifies sin through Satan's whisper.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wisdom behind the invisibility of jinn and angels and the role of Satan's whispering in the soul's sin.

Core Idea
Jinn and angels are hidden from us by divine mercy, and the soul sins only through Satan's prompting.

This passage from Imam Nasafi addresses two common theological questions: Why don't we see jinn and angels even though they see us? And does the soul directly cause sin? Through concise answers and a Quranic citation, the author clarifies divine wisdom and the intermediary role of Satan. As you read, notice how the answers appeal to creation substances (wind, light) and a verse from Surah an-Nas.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Note that the passage begins with an objection and then answers.
The Arabic uses a colloquial form 'أَيش' meaning 'what'.
2
Identify the two questions answered
The passage first explains why jinn/angels are unseen, then addresses the soul's role in sin. Notice the logical structure.
3
Reflect on the wisdom (hikma) behind invisibility
The author gives different reasons for jinn (from wind) and angels (from light). Contrast these.
Consider why seeing them would prevent enjoyment of food or cause loss of soul.
4
Understand the role of Satan's whispering
The soul does cause sin, but only through the means of Satan's whispering. The Quran verse confirms this.
This refutes the misconception that the soul independently leads to sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : أَيش الحكمة في أنهم يروننا ونحن لا نراهم؟
قلنا : لأنهم خُلِقُوا على صورة قبيحة، فلو رأيناهم لم نقدر على تناول الطعام والشراب فستروا عنا رحمة من الله تعالى.
وأما الجن خُلِقُوا من الريح، وأصل الريح لا يرى فكذلك ما خلق منه.
وأما الملائكة خُلِقُوا من النُّور، فلو رأيناهم لطارت أرواحنا وأنفسنا.
وأما قوله : بأن النفس توقعهم في المعاصي.
قلنا: نعم، ولكن بواسطة وسوسة الشيطان، قال الله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِي يُوَسْوِسُ فِي صُدُورِ النَّاسِ ﴾ [الناس : ٤] .
If it is said: What is the wisdom in that they see us while we do not see them? We say: Because they were created in an ugly form, so if we saw them we would not be able to consume food and drink, so they were hidden from us as a mercy from Allah Almighty. As for the jinn, they were created from wind, and the origin of wind is not seen, so likewise that which is created from it. As for the angels, they were created from light, so if we saw them our souls and selves would fly away. As for his saying that the soul causes them to fall into sins, we say: Yes, but through the means of the whispering of Satan. Allah Almighty said: {He who whispers into the breasts of mankind} [Surah an-Nas: 4].
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a Q&A session addressing objections about the invisibility of jinn and angels and the role of the soul in sin. The author first answers the question of why we do not see jinn and angels despite them seeing us. The wisdom given is that they were created in an ugly form, so seeing them would prevent us from eating and drinking; thus they are hidden out of mercy. Then he explains separately: jinn are from wind which is invisible, so their bodies are also invisible; angels are from light and would overwhelm us if seen. Finally, the author addresses the claim that the soul itself leads people to sin. He agrees that the soul does, but only through the intermediary of Satan's whispering, citing the Quranic verse about the whisperer in people's hearts.

Key Terms
الجن
الملائكة
الوسوسة
النفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul directly leads to sin without any external influence.
Correction: The soul leads to sin only through Satan's whispering.

B) They are created from light and would cause our souls to fly away.
C) They are ugly.
D) It is to test our faith.

Key Takeaway
The invisibility of jinn and angels is divine mercy, and the soul's sin occurs only through the medium of Satan's whispering.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage says the soul sins only through Satan's whispering. Are you aware of the whispers that enter your heart before you fall into sin? How can you train yourself to recognize and reject them immediately?

The Mi'raj: Mu'tazila Denial and Sunni Affirmation
Nasafi presents the Mu'tazilite objection and Sunni response to Mi'raj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila epistemological objection to Mi'raj and how the Sunnis countered by citing widespread transmission.

Core Idea
Solitary reports oblige action, not belief; widespread reports oblige both.

This passage presents a classic debate between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna over the reality of the Prophet's ascension (Mi'raj). The Mu'tazila reject it on grounds that the reports are solitary (khabar al-ahad) and therefore insufficient for creedal certainty. The Sunnis respond by arguing that the transmission is actually widespread, coming from multiple Companions. Understanding this exchange clarifies the role of hadith transmission in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get the rhythm. Then read the translation. Notice the two clear sides: Mu'tazila vs. Ahl al-Sunna.
The key terms are 'أخبار الآحاد' and 'خبر الواحد'.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila argument
Find the Mu'tazila claim: they deny Mi'raj because it comes through solitary reports, which only oblige action, not belief. This is an epistemological distinction.
3
Identify the Sunni counter-argument
The Sunnis affirm Mi'raj by pointing to multiple narrators from the Companions. They imply the reports reach tawatur (widespread transmission) or at least istifadah.
List the Companions mentioned: Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, Anas, Malik, Ibn Abbas, Umm Hani'.
4
Ask: why does this matter?
Reflect on how this debate illustrates the role of hadith in creed. For Sunnis, even if a report is not mutawatir, multiple chains strengthen it. For Mu'tazila, only mutawatir reports yield certainty.
This connects to broader discussions about khabar al-ahad in theology and law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالت المعتزلة: المعراج لم يكن، لأنه جاءت به أخبار الآحاد، وخبر الواحد يُوجب العمل، ولا يوجب الاعتقاد. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة : المعراج كان صحيحًا إلى السماء، لأنه رُوي عن أكثر أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نحو أبي سعيد الخدري، وأنس بن مالك، ومالك بن صعصعة، وابن عباس، وأمّ هانيء رضي الله عنهم أنهم قالوا: المعراج إلى السماء.
The Mu'tazila said: The Mi'raj did not occur, because it came through ahad (solitary) reports, and a solitary report obliges action, and does not oblige belief. And the People of the Sunnah and the Community said: The Mi'raj was true to the heaven, because it was reported from most of the companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him), such as Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, Anas ibn Malik, Malik ibn Sa'sa'ah, Ibn 'Abbas, and Umm Hani' (may God be pleased with them) that they said: The Mi'raj to the heaven.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage presents the initial disagreement between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna on the reality of the Mi'raj (the Prophet's ascension to heaven). The Mu'tazila deny it on epistemological grounds: the reports about the Mi'raj are khabar al-ahad (solitary reports) which, in their view, only necessitate action (in the legal sphere) but not conviction (i'tiqad) in matters of belief. The Sunni response does not contest the epistemological classification but argues that the Mi'raj is transmitted by many Companions (the phrase 'most of the companions' indicates tawatur, or at least istifadah). The names listed — Abu Sa'id, Anas, Malik, Ibn 'Abbas, Umm Hani' — are given as examples. Thus the Sunnis claim that the transmission is not isolated but widespread, thereby meeting the threshold for acceptance in creedal matters.

Key Terms
المعراج
أخبار الآحاد
خبر الواحد
العمل
الاعتقاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Sunni position relies on a single hadith.
Correction: The passage emphasizes multiple reports from many Companions, indicating widespread transmission.

Checkpoint
On what grounds did the Mu'tazila reject the Mi'raj?
A) It contradicts reason.
B) It is based on solitary reports (khabar al-ahad) which do not necessitate belief.
C) The Qur'an explicitly denies it.
D) It was a dream, not a physical event.

Key Takeaway
The Sunnis uphold the Mi'raj by highlighting its widespread transmission from multiple Companions, countering the Mu'tazila's objection based on solitary reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the reports about the unseen, like the Mi'raj, as certain truth, or do you secretly doubt because you haven't seen them yourself? What would change in your life if you truly believed the Mi'raj happened exactly as described?
?
The Mu'tazila refused to accept the Mi'raj because they felt the reports were only solitary. Are there any teachings of Islam that you accept only as 'good advice' rather than as absolute truth? What is the root of that hesitation?
?
The Sunnis affirmed the Mi'raj based on the testimony of multiple Companions. When you read the Quran and hadith, do you trust them as if you were hearing them from the Companions themselves? What concrete step can you take today to strengthen your certainty in the transmitted reports of the Prophet?

Distinction Between Isra and Mi'raj
Nasafi distinguishes between Isra and Mi'raj based on scriptural certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between the Isra and Mi'raj in terms of scriptural certainty and theological implications.

Core Idea
Denying the Isra is disbelief; the Mi'raj lacks a decisive proof.

Nasafi tackles a crucial distinction in the narrative of the Prophet's night journey. While both Isra and Mi'raj are accepted by Sunni Muslims, they differ in the strength of their scriptural evidence. This passage explains why the Mu'tazila accept the Isra but not the Mi'raj, and why denying the Isra is kufr.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and translation to grasp the two matters Nasafi addresses.
Notice the structure: 'Here are two matters...'
2
Understand the Isra
Identify how the Isra is proven by a decisive Qur'anic text and why its denial is kufr.
The Qur'anic verse is directly quoted.
3
Understand the Mi'raj
Note that the Mi'raj is not established by a decisive proof; this sets up a later discussion.
Contrast this with the Isra's clear textual basis.
4
Reflect on theological significance
Consider why the distinction matters for Islamic creed and how it relates to the authority of scripture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ها هنا شيئان: الإسراء والمعراج، أما الإسراء من مكة إلى بيت المقدس لا ينكره المعتزلة لأنه وَرَدَ به النص قال الله تعالى: ﴿سُبْحَانَ الَّذِي أَسْرَى بِعَبْدِهِ لَيْلًا مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ إِلَى الْمَسْجِدِ الْأَقْصَا ﴾ [الإسراء: ١] والإسراء هو السير بالليل، ومن أنكر الإسراء يكفر. وأما المعراج من الأرض إلى السماء السابعة لا يثبت بدليل قطعي.
Here are two matters: al-Isra and al-Mi'raj. As for al-Isra from Mecca to Bayt al-Maqdis, the Mu'tazila do not deny it because the [Qur'anic] text came with it. God Most High said: 'Exalted is He who took His Servant by night from al-Masjid al-Haram to al-Masjid al-Aqsa' [al-Isra:1]. And al-Isra is traveling by night. Whoever denies al-Isra disbelieves. As for al-Mi'raj from the earth to the seventh heaven, it is not established by a decisive proof.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage clarifies the two components of the Night Journey narrative: al-Isra (the night journey from Mecca to Jerusalem) and al-Mi'raj (the ascension from Jerusalem to the heavens). Nasafi notes that the Mu'tazila do not deny the Isra because it is explicitly mentioned in the Qur'an (verse 1 of Surah al-Isra). Denial of the Isra is tantamount to disbelief (kufr) because it contradicts a decisive Qur'anic text. In contrast, the Mi'raj from earth to the seventh heaven is not established by a decisive proof (dalil qat'i). The Arabic phrase 'لا يثبت بدليل قطعي' indicates that the Mi'raj's textual evidence is not as definitive as the Isra's; it is based on hadith that are not mutawatir in wording or clear in meaning. Nonetheless, the Sunnis affirm it based on other evidence, which will be presented in subsequent passages.

Key Terms
الإسراء
المعراج
النص
دليل قطعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Both Isra and Mi'raj have equal scriptural proof.
Correction: The Isra is proven by a decisive Qur'anic text, whereas the Mi'raj is not established by a decisive proof. This distinction affects the level of certainty and the consequences of denial.

Checkpoint
Why do the Mu'tazila not deny the Isra?
A) It is supported by reason.
B) It is mentioned in a decisive Qur'anic text.
C) There is consensus among Muslims.
D) It was witnessed by many companions.

Key Takeaway
The Isra is proven by a decisive Qur'anic text, whereas the Mi'raj is not established by a decisive proof, though accepted by Sunnis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that denying the Isra—a matter clearly stated in the Quran—is disbelief. Is there any verse of the Quran that you have ever dismissed or diluted in your heart because it was inconvenient? How will you now realign your conviction with every clear text, even when it challenges you?
?
The Mi'raj is not established by a decisive proof, yet you likely accept it as a Sunni. What is the basis of your personal certainty for unseen events not explicitly in the Quran? This lesson forces you to examine: do you follow the Prophet's teachings only when they are backed by the strongest evidence, or do you submit even to authentic hadith? Where is your limit?
?
Imagine someone denies the Mi'raj but accepts the Isra. According to the lesson, the former is not disbelief. Does that comfort you? Or does it disturb you that some aspects of your faith rest on 'less decisive' grounds? What does this reveal about your trust in the overall structure of Islamic creed—and what specific action will you take to strengthen your conviction in all revealed matters?

Refutation of Mu'tazila Denial of Guardian Angels
Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila denial of guardian angels and discusses how deeds are recorded.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah appoints guardian angels despite His omniscience, and how their recording serves as evidence on Judgement Day.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge doesn't make recording angels redundant—they serve as witnesses.

The Mu'tazila argued that since Allah knows everything, guardian angels are unnecessary. In this passage, Imam Nasafi refutes this by showing that the angels are appointed not because Allah is ignorant, but to provide a witness and a written record that will confront the servant on the Day of Resurrection. Let's examine the argument and its scriptural foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally.
Pay attention to the structure: objection, response, then subsidiary discussion.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila objection
The Mu'tazila claim that since Allah knows everything, appointing recording angels is pointless. Understand their reasoning.
3
Understand the Sunni response
Nasafi explains that the purpose of the angels is to serve as witnesses and provide a written record for accountability on Judgement Day, not to inform Allah.
This is the core refutation.
4
Explore the two opinions on recording
The passage presents two views on how angels write: Al-Dahhak says they descend with scrolls, Mujahid says the human organs are instruments. Note which is preferred and why.
Look for the Quranic evidence cited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالت المعتزلة: ليس علينا ملائكةٌ ولا حَفَظَة، وكلُّ ما يعمل الإنسان فالله تعالى عالم به يغفر لمن يشاء، ويعذب من يشاء، وإنما يحتاج إلى الحفظة أن لو كان جاهلاً، ولا يعلم ماذا يعمل عباده، والله تعالى لا يحتاج إلى أن يوكل عليهم ليكتب أعمالهم. قلنا: إنما يوكل عليهم ليكون حجةً على العبد يوم القيامة، فإذا أنكر العبد الأفعال يشهد عليه الملكان ، وإذا نسي يكون الكتاب حجة عليه. فإن قيل: بأي شيء يكتبون؟ قيل لهم: قال الضحاك: ينزل كل يوم ملكان، مع كل واحد منهما صحيفة. وقال مجاهد : لسانك قلمهما، وريقك مدادهما، ويدك كتابهما. والأول أصح، لأن الله تعالى قال: أقْرَأْ كِتَبَكَ كَفَى بِنَفْسِكَ الْيَوْمَ عَلَيْكَ حَسِيبًا [الإسراء: ١٤] وهذا يدل على أنه كان كتابًا لهم.
The Mu'tazila said: There are no angels or guardians over us, and everything that man does, Allah the Exalted knows it; He forgives whom He wills and punishes whom He wills. They only need guardians if He were ignorant, not knowing what His servants do. Allah the Exalted does not need to appoint guardians over them to write their deeds. We said: He only appoints them so that it be an argument against the servant on the Day of Resurrection. If the servant denies the actions, the two angels will testify against him, and if he forgets, the book will be an argument against him. If it is said: With what do they write? It was said to them: Al-Dahhak said: Two angels descend every day, each with a scroll. And Mujahid said: Your tongue is their pen, your saliva is their ink, and your hand is their book. The first is more correct, because Allah the Exalted said: 'Read your book; sufficient is yourself this Day as a reckoner against you' [al-Isra 17:14]. And this indicates that it was a book for them.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila who deny that Allah appoints guardian angels to record deeds. The Mu'tazila argue that since Allah knows everything, He has no need to appoint angels to write down deeds. The author (Nasafi) responds that the angels are appointed not because Allah is ignorant, but to serve as a witness against the servant on the Day of Resurrection. The angels' testimony and the written record will be evidence when the servant denies or forgets his actions. The author then addresses a subsidiary question: How do these angels write? Two views are reported: (1) Al-Dahhak says two angels descend daily each with a scroll; (2) Mujahid says the human tongue is their pen, saliva their ink, and hand their book (i.e., the deeds are recorded through the human's own actions). The author declares the first view more correct, citing the Quranic verse 'Read your book, sufficient is yourself this Day as a reckoner against you' (17:14). This verse indicates that there is an actual book, not just an internal record. Thus the passage defends the orthodox Sunni belief in the existence of recording angels against rationalist objections.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الحفظة
الملائكة
الحجة
الكتاب
الملكان
الصحيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since Allah knows everything, guardian angels are unnecessary.
Correction: Angels serve as witnesses and provide a written record for accountability on Judgement Day, not to inform Allah.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say Allah appoints guardian angels despite His knowledge of all deeds?
A) To remind Allah of what humans do.
B) To serve as a witness against the servant on Judgement Day.
C) To help humans remember their deeds.
D) Because Allah is ignorant of some things.

Key Takeaway
Allah appoints guardian angels to record deeds not because He needs to know, but to provide evidence for the servant on the Day of Judgement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if every action—every word and every glance—is being recorded by angels who will present it before you on the Day of Judgment? How would your choices today change if you truly believed that your own book is being written right now?

The Manner of Angels Recording Deeds
Discusses two opinions on how angels write deeds and the author's preference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two opinions on how angels record human deeds and the evidence supporting the view that they write on actual scrolls.

Core Idea
Angels record deeds on tangible scrolls, not metaphorically.

This passage explores how angels physically record our deeds. Two early scholars, al-Dahhak and Mujahid, offered different explanations. Al-Dahhak spoke of descending angels with scrolls, while Mujahid used metaphorical language. The author prefers al-Dahhak's view, citing a Quranic verse that implies a real book. Let's see the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the question-and-answer format.
The passage starts with 'If it is said...'.
2
Identify the two opinions
Locate al-Dahhak's opinion (two angels with scrolls) and Mujahid's opinion (tongue, saliva, hand as writing tools).
3
Understand the author's reasoning
See how the author uses Quran 17:14 to argue that the book is actual, supporting al-Dahhak's view over Mujahid's metaphorical one.
The verse says 'Read your book' – implying a physical book.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: بأي شيء يكتبون؟ قيل لهم: قال الضحاك: ينزل كل يوم ملكان، مع كل واحد منهما صحيفة. وقال مجاهد: لسانك قلمهما، وريقك مدادهما، ويدك كتابهما. والأول أصح، لأن الله تعالى قال: ﴿اقْرَأْ كِتَابَكَ كَفَى بِنَفْسِكَ الْيَوْمَ عَلَيْكَ حَسِيبًا﴾ [الإسراء: 14] وهذا يدل على أنه كان كتابًا لهم.
If it is said: With what do they write? It is said to them: al-Dahhak said: Two angels descend every day, each with a scroll. And Mujahid said: Your tongue is their pen, your saliva is their ink, and your hand is their book. The first is more correct, because Allah Most High said: 'Read your book. Sufficient is yourself today against you as a reckoner' [al-Isra: 14]. And this indicates that it was a book of theirs.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage addresses a subsidiary question: the physical means by which angels write. Two opinions are mentioned. Al-Dahhak holds that two new angels descend each day with a scroll (sahifa). Mujahid's view is metaphorical: the person's own tongue, saliva, and hand serve as the angels' writing tools. The author prefers al-Dahhak's view, citing the Quranic verse 'Read your book' (al-Isra: 14), which implies an actual book that the person will read, not a metaphorical one. Thus, the angels write on tangible scrolls.

Correction: It is considered less correct than al-Dahhak's literal view, but not entirely rejected. The author simply prefers the literal interpretation based on Quranic evidence.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

Sunni Doctrine on Guardian Angels: Number and Shift
States the Sunni position on guardian angels with Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on guardian angels: that each person has two angels by day and two by night in rotation, and that this doctrine is accepted on the basis of revelation without delving into its modality.

Core Idea
Four guardian angels rotate daily; we accept it by faith, not reason.

This passage concludes the discussion on guardian angels by laying out the clear Sunni doctrine. Imam al-Nasafi first establishes the methodological principle of accepting revealed truths about the unseen without asking 'how,' then he states the specific belief about the number and shift of angels, and finally he supports it with two Quranic verses. As you read, notice how the author refutes an alternative view by appealing directly to the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage once
Read the Arabic passage below and its English translation. Let the author's own words sink in before analyzing.
The passage starts with a methodological principle before stating the doctrine.
2
Identify the methodological principle
Notice how the author begins: 'We believe in what the textual revelation and reports have brought, and we do not occupy ourselves with its modality.' This is a key Sunni approach to matters of the unseen.
The word 'kayfiyya' (modality) is important—it means the 'how' that reason cannot grasp.
3
Understand the specific doctrine
The author states: every person has two angels by night and two by day, and they rotate (day angels descend, night angels ascend). Contrast this with the rejected view of completely new angels each day.
Memorize the numbers: two at night, two during the day.
4
Examine the Quranic proofs
Two verses are cited: al-Infitar 82:10-11 and al-Zukhruf 43:80. Read them in the passage and see how they support the existence of guardian angels who record deeds.
These verses do not explicitly mention the rotation, but they establish the constant presence of recording angels.
5
Test your understanding
Try to answer the checkpoint question below without looking back. Then check your answer and read the feedback.
This will help solidify the key details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصل الجواب: أنا نؤمن بما جاء به النص والأخبار، ولا نشتغل بكيفيته، وإن كان يأباه العقل والقياس. قال أهل السنة والجماعة: الحفظة حق، على كل واحد منا اثنان بالليل واثنان بالنهار، ينزل ملكا النهار، ويذهب ملكا الليل، وليس كما قال بعض الناس: ينزل كل يوم ملكان غير الذين كانا عليه بالأمس. يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّ عَلَيْكُمْ لَحَافِظِينَ كِرَامًا كَاتِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: 10-11] وقوله تعالى: ﴿أَمْ يَحْسَبُونَ أَنَّا لَا نَسْمَعُ سِرَّهُمْ وَنَجْوَاهُم بَلَى وَرُسُلُنَا لَدَيْهِمْ يَكْتُبُونَ﴾ [الزخرف: 80].
The summary of the answer: We believe in what the textual revelation and reports have brought, and we do not occupy ourselves with its modality, even if reason and analogy reject it. The Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said: The guardians are true; each of us has two by night and two by day; the two angels of the day descend and the two angels of the night ascend. It is not as some people said: two angels descend every day other than those who were on him the day before. This is supported by the saying of Allah Most High: 'And indeed, over you are guardians, noble scribes' [al-Infitar: 10-11] and His saying: 'Or do they think that We hear not their secrets and their private conversations? Yes, and Our messengers are with them recording' [al-Zukhruf: 80].
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage concludes the chapter with a methodological principle and a precise doctrinal statement. First, the author states the Sunni approach: belief in what the Quran and authentic hadith convey about guardian angels without delving into the 'how' (kayfiyya), even if reason or analogy seems to oppose it. Then he lays out the specific Sunni teaching: every person has four guardian angels—two during the day and two during the night. They rotate: the day angels descend and the night angels ascend. This refutes the view that completely new angels come each day. Two Quranic verses are cited as evidence: al-Infitar 10-11 calls them 'guardians, noble scribes,' and al-Zukhruf 80 affirms that Allah's messengers (angels) are with us recording.

Key Terms
النص والأخبار
الكيفية
أهل السنة والجماعة
تعاقب الملائكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people claimed that two completely new angels descend on a person every day, different from those of the previous day.
Correction: The correct Sunni doctrine is that there are two fixed angels for the day and two for the night; they rotate (the day angels descend and the night angels ascend) but are not replaced by entirely new angels each day.

Checkpoint
How many guardian angels does a person have at any given time according to the Ahl al-Sunna position in this passage?
A) Two angels total, one for day and one for night.
B) Two angels by day and two by night, totaling four in rotation.
C) Only two angels that change every day.
D) A variable number depending on the person's deeds.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni doctrine affirms four guardian angels per person (two day, two night) in a fixed rotation, accepted on the authority of revelation without seeking the 'how'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
You have four guardian angels rotating around you every day. Does that truth move you to obedience even when no human sees you? If not, what concrete step will you take to remind yourself of their presence tomorrow?

The Number of Guardian Angels: A Lesson in Speculative Caution
Records varying narrations about the number of guardian angels without specifying a fixed count.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why classical scholars refrain from specifying a fixed number for guardian angels and how this parallels belief in the prophets.

Core Idea
When reports differ on numbers, we believe without specifying.

The precise number of guardian angels is not specified in the Quran or decisive hadith. Various companions and reports give different counts. Rather than contradicting, these reports teach us a methodological principle: when authentic sources vary, we affirm the core belief and avoid fixing numbers that might lead to error. This lesson examines the reports and the lesson derived from them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the different numbers mentioned: five, two, sixty, one hundred sixty.
Pay attention to the detailed roles of the five angels from Ibn Abbas.
2
Identify the key reports
List the reports: Ibn Abbas' five angels with specific functions, then the other reports with different totals.
The five angels each have a distinct task.
3
Understand the analogy
The passage compares this to belief in the prophets. Ask yourself: why should we not specify a number for the prophets? How does that apply here?
The risk is believing in a false prophet or rejecting a real one.
4
Apply the principle
Reflect on why the author advises against specifying a number for guardian angels. What harm could come from fixing a count?

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قد اختلفت الآثار في عدد الحفظة، فقال ابن عباس رضي الله عنه مع كل مؤمن خمس من الحفظة واحد عن يمينه يكتب الحسنات، وواحد عن يساره يكتب السيئات، وواحد أمامه يلقنه الخيرات، وواحد وراءه يدفع عن الآفات، وواحد عند ناصيته يكتب ما يصلي على النبي، ويبلغه إلى الرسول. وفي بعض الأخبار: مع كل مؤمن ملكان، وفي بعضها مع كل مؤمن ستون ملكًا، وفي بعضها: مئة وستون، فصار كالإيمان بالأنبياء عليهم السلام، فإنه ينبغي أن لا يُعيَّن عدد في إيمانهم للاختلاف، فربما يؤمن بمن ليس بنبي أو لا يؤمن بمن هو نبي لو عُيّن عدد.
Reports have differed regarding the number of the guardians. Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, said: With every believer are five guardians: one on his right writing the good deeds, one on his left writing the evil deeds, one in front of him instructing him in good things, one behind him repelling afflictions, and one at his forelock writing what he sends prayers upon the Prophet and conveying it to the Messenger. And in some reports: with every believer are two angels; in some: with every believer are sixty angels; and in some: one hundred and sixty. So this becomes like belief in the prophets, peace be upon them: it is necessary that no number be specified in believing in them due to disagreement, for perhaps one would believe in someone who is not a prophet or not believe in someone who is a prophet if a number were specified.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This footnote (marginal note) presents the problem of differing reports on the exact number of guardian angels. It gives the detailed report of Ibn Abbas naming five specific angels with distinct roles. Then it mentions other reports stating two, sixty, or one hundred sixty angels per person. The author of the note draws an analogy with belief in the prophets: just as we believe in all prophets without specifying a fixed number (to avoid error), we should not specify a fixed number of guardian angels, because different authentic reports give different numbers. This reflects a cautious theological methodology: when texts vary, avoid specifying numbers that may lead to false beliefs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The differing numbers indicate contradiction or that we must pick one number as correct.
Correction: The differing numbers are accepted without specifying to avoid error, just as with the prophets.

Checkpoint
Why does the note advise against specifying a fixed number for the guardian angels?
A) Because the Quran does not mention any number.
B) Because the reports differ, and specifying one might lead to false belief (e.g., believing in a non-existent angel or disbelieving in a real one).
C) Because the Prophet forbade counting them.
D) Because the number is irrelevant to faith.

Key Takeaway
When authentic reports differ on a numerical detail, scholars avoid specifying a fixed number to prevent error, just as we believe in all prophets without enumerating them.

Belief in the Recording Angels
Ahl al-Sunnah affirm the reality of the recording angels and state their method of accepting unseen reports without asking how.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunnah belief regarding the recording angels and their rotation, and the principle of accepting revealed reports without inquiring into their modality.

Core Idea
Revelation is accepted even if reason struggles; angels guard and record every deed.

This lesson introduces a key sam‘iyyah belief: the reality of the recording angels (al-ḥafaẓah). Imam al-Nasafī begins by stating the overarching Sunni principle—we affirm what scripture brings without delving into 'how'—then applies it to the specific claim that each person has four angels rotating day and night. The lesson also refutes a deviant view and provides Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice how the author moves from a general rule to a specific doctrine.
The passage is concise; each sentence carries weight.
2
Identify the two parts
The passage has a general principle (first sentence) and a specific belief (remaining sentences). Observe how the specific belief is an application of the principle.
3
Understand the rotation of angels
Focus on the statement: two angels by night, two by day, with the day angels descending and night angels departing. Contrast with the rejected opinion.
This shows the Sunni position is precise, not vague.
4
Examine the Quranic evidence
Read the two verses cited. They confirm the existence of guardian-recording angels. Note how the verses use different words to emphasize recording.
The first verse (al-Infitar) stresses writing, the second (al-Zukhruf) stresses hearing and recording.
5
Reflect on the principle
Ask: Why does the author begin with a principle about reason and analogy? What does this tell us about the Sunni approach to unseen matters?
This connects to the core idea: revelation takes precedence over unaided reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَحَاصِلُ الْجَوَابِ: أَنَا نُؤْمِنُ بِمَا جَاءَ بِهِ النَّصُّ وَالْأَخْبَارُ، وَلَا نَشْتَغِلُ بِكَيْفِيَّتِهِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ يَأْبَاهُ الْعَقْلُ وَالْقِيَاسُ. قَالَ أَهْلُ السُّنَّةِ وَالْجَمَاعَةِ: الْحَفَظَةُ حَقٌّ، عَلَى كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَّا اثْنَانِ بِاللَّيْلِ وَاثْنَانِ بِالنَّهَارِ، يَنْزِلُ مَلَكَا النَّهَارِ، وَيَذْهَبُ مَلَكَا اللَّيْلِ، وَلَيْسَ كَمَا قَالَ بَعْضُ النَّاسِ: يَنْزِلُ كُلَّ يَوْمٍ مَلَكَانِ غَيْرُ اللَّذَيْنِ كَانَا عَلَيْهِ بِالْأَمْسِ. يَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَإِنَّ عَلَيْكُمْ لَحَنفِظِينَ كِرَامًا كَاتِبِينَ ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٠-١١] وَقَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿أَمْ يَحْسَبُونَ أَنَّا لَا نَسْمَعُ سِرَّهُمْ وَنَجْوَهُمْ بَلَى وَرُسُلُنَا لَدَيْهِمْ يَكْتُبُونَ ﴾ [الزخرف: ٨٠]
And the sum of the answer: We believe in what the text and reports have brought, and we do not occupy ourselves with its modality, even if reason and analogy reject it. The people of the Sunnah and the community said: The guardians (al-ḥafaẓah) are true; upon each one of us are two by night and two by day; the angels of the day descend, and the angels of the night go away. It is not as some people said: two angels descend every day other than the two that were upon him yesterday. Indicating it is His statement, exalted: 'And indeed, over you are keepers, noble, writing' (al-Infitar: 10-11), and His statement, exalted: 'Or do they think that We do not hear their secrets and their private conversations? Yes, and Our messengers are with them, recording' (al-Zukhruf: 80).
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the Ahl al-Sunnah position on the recording angels (al-ḥafaẓah). It begins with a general principle: the correct approach to unseen matters reported in revelation is to affirm them without delving into how (al-kayfiyyah), even if reason or analogical reasoning seems to oppose it. This principle is then applied to the specific belief about the guardians. The text states that every person has four guardians: two by night and two by day, who rotate. The angels of the day descend, and the angels of the night depart. This refutes the view of some who claimed that entirely new angels descend each day. The passage then cites two Quranic verses as proof: Surat al-Infitar (82:10-11) which affirms that there are preserving and writing angels over every person, and Surat al-Zukhruf (43:80) which confirms that God's messengers (angels) are present and writing down all secret conversations.

ملكا الليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people claim that reason and analogy must confirm the modality of unseen realities before accepting them.
Correction: The passage teaches that we believe in what the text and reports bring without occupying ourselves with how, even if reason and analogy reject it.

Key Takeaway

The Varying Reports on the Number of Guardian Angels
A marginal note on differing reports of guardian angels and the rule of not fixing a number.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the reports on the number of guardian angels vary and the theological principle of not specifying a number when reports conflict.

Core Idea
When reports differ, avoid fixing numbers to prevent error in belief.

This marginal note from the Bahr al-Kalam addresses a common question: how many guardian angels does each person have? It collects various reports and, importantly, draws a parallel with belief in prophets, teaching us a crucial principle about dealing with conflicting textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the different numbers mentioned and the reasoning that follows.
The note is a marginal addition, so it supplements the main text.
2
Identify the various reports
List the different numbers of guardian angels reported: Ibn Abbas says five, other reports mention two, sixty, and one hundred sixty. Also note the specific functions assigned to the five angels.
Ibn Abbas's report is the most detailed.
3
Understand the principle
The note compares the variation to belief in prophets. Just as we do not fix the exact number of prophets due to differing reports, we do not fix the number of guardian angels. This prevents believing in a non-prophet or disbelieving in a true prophet.
The same caution applies to the number of angels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَرَدَ بِهَامِشِ النُّسْخَةِ (أ) مَا صُورَتُهُ: «قَدِ اخْتَلَفَتِ الْآثَارُ فِي عَدَدِ الْحَفَظَةِ، فَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنه مَعَ كُلِّ مُؤْمِنٍ خَمْسٌ مِنَ الْحَفَظَةِ: وَاحِدٌ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ يَكْتُبُ الْحَسَنَاتِ، وَوَاحِدٌ عَنْ يَسَارِهِ يَكْتُبُ السَّيِّئَاتِ، وَوَاحِدٌ أَمَامَهُ يُلَقِّنُهُ الْخَيْرَاتِ، وَوَاحِدٌ وَرَاءَهُ يَدْفَعُ عَنِ الْآفَاتِ، وَوَاحِدٌ عِنْدَ نَاصِيَتِهِ يَكْتُبُ مَا يُصَلِّي عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، وَيُبَلِّغُهُ إِلَى الرَّسُولِ. وَفِي بَعْضِ الْأَخْبَارِ: مَعَ كُلِّ مُؤْمِنٍ مَلَكَانِ، وَفِي بَعْضِهَا: مَعَ كُلِّ مُؤْمِنٍ سِتُّونَ مَلَكًا، وَفِي بَعْضِهَا: مِائَةٌ وَسِتُّونَ، فَصَارَ كَالْإِيمَانِ بِالْأَنْبِيَاءِ عَلَيْهِمُ السَّلَامُ، فَإِنَّهُ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ لَا يُعَيَّنَ عَدَدٌ فِي إِيمَانِهِمْ لِلِاخْتِلَافِ، فَرُبَّمَا يُؤْمَنُ بِمَنْ لَيْسَ بِنَبِيٍّ أَوْ لَا يُؤْمَنُ بِمَنْ هُوَ نَبِيٌّ لَوْ عُيِّنَ عَدَدٌ. وَذَكَرَ فِي الْكَوَاشِيِّ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: كَاتِبُ الْحَسَنَاتِ عَلَى يَمِينِ الرَّجُلِ، وَكَاتِبُ السَّيِّئَاتِ عَلَى يَسَارِ الرَّجُلِ، وَكَاتِبُ الْحَسَنَاتِ أَمِيرٌ عَلَى كَاتِبِ السَّيِّئَاتِ، فَإِذَا عَمِلَ حَسَنَةً كَتَبَهَا صَاحِبُ الْيَمِينِ بِعَشْرٍ، وَإِذَا عَمِلَ سَيِّئَةً قَالَ صَاحِبُ الْيَمِينِ لِصَاحِبِ الشِّمَالِ: دَعْهُ سَبْعَ سَاعَاتٍ لَعَلَّهُ يُسَبِّحُ وَيَسْتَغْفِرُ».
There came in the margin of copy (A) the following: 'The reports have differed concerning the number of the guardians. Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, said: With every believer are five of the guardians: one on his right writing the good deeds, one on his left writing the evil deeds, one in front of him prompting him to good works, one behind him repelling afflictions, and one at his forelock writing what he sends of blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ and conveying it to the Messenger. And in some reports: with every believer are two angels; in some: with every believer are sixty angels; in some: one hundred and sixty. So it became like belief in the prophets, peace be upon them: it is fitting that a number should not be specified in believing in them because of the disagreement, for perhaps one might believe in someone who is not a prophet or not believe in someone who is a prophet if a number were fixed. And he mentioned in al-Kawashi that he said: The writer of good deeds is on the right of the man, and the writer of evil deeds is on the left of the man, and the writer of good deeds is an amir over the writer of evil deeds. So when he does a good deed, the one on the right writes it as ten, and when he does an evil deed, the one on the right says to the one on the left: Leave him for seven hours, perhaps he will glorify (Allah) and seek forgiveness.'
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a marginal note that collects various reports about the number of guardian angels. It begins by noting that the reports differ: Ibn Abbas reports five guardians with specific functions; other reports mention two, sixty, or one hundred sixty. The note then draws a crucial principle: just as we do not fix the exact number of prophets due to differences in reports (to avoid believing in a false prophet or disbelieving in a true one), we do not fix the number of guardian angels. The note ends with a quote from al-Kawashi describing the arrangement of the two main recording angels: the angel of good deeds on the right is in charge, and when a sin is committed, he tells the angel on the left to wait seven hours in case the person repents or seeks forgiveness.

Misconception: The differing reports about the number of guardian angels contradict each other, so one report must be chosen as correct.
Correction: The reports are not contradictory; the variation is similar to that of prophets, and we do not specify a number to avoid error or omission.

The Eternity of Paradise and Hell
Imam al-Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila annihilation and lists seven eternal creations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunnah affirm the eternity of Paradise and Hell and which seven created entities never perish.

Core Idea
Paradise, Hell, and five other creations are eternal—they never perish.

In this passage from Bahr al-Kalam, Imam al-Nasafi presents a key Sunni theological position against the Mu'tazila. The debate centers on whether Paradise and Hell will be annihilated after the trumpet blast. The Mu'tazila say yes, arguing from God's uniqueness; Ahl al-Sunnah say no, citing the Quran and listing seven permanent creations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the flow of the argument. Notice the two opposing positions.
The passage starts with the Mu'tazila claim and ends with the Sunni list.
2
Compare the two positions
Identify the Mu'tazila proof (verse al-Hadid 3) and the Sunni counter-proof (verse al-Zumar 68). Understand why each side uses its chosen verse.
The Mu'tazila emphasize Allah's sole eternity; the Sunnis emphasize the exception in the trumpet verse.
3
Memorize the seven entities
Commit to memory the list of seven things that never perish: the Throne, the Footstool, the Pen, Paradise, Hell, their inhabitants, and the souls.
These are all created, yet eternal in the sense of never-ending.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الكلام على النفخ والبعث والنشور. قالت المعتزلة: إذا أمر الله تعالى بالنفخة الأولى يُفنِي السموات والأرض، والجنة والنار، والأرواح، ثم يخلقهم الله يوم القيامة مرةً أخرى. واحتجوا بقوله تعالى: ﴿هُوَ الأَوَّلُ والآخِرُ وَالظَّاهِرُ وَالْبَاطِنُ ﴾ [الحديد: ٣]. ثم إنَّ الله تعالى كان في الأزل حيث لم يكن معه أحدٌ مِن خَلْقِهِ، فكذلك وَجَبَ أَن لا يبقي في الآخرة شيء حتى لا يبقى ببقائه أحد؛ ليكون له هذا الاسم خاصة. قال أهل السنة والجماعة: الجنة والنار هما دارا الخلد وهما للثواب والعقاب، فلا يفنيان. يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَنُفِخَ فِي الصُّورِ فَصَعِقَ مَن فِي السَّمَوَاتِ وَمَن فِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا مَن شَاءَ اللهُ ﴾ [الزمر: ٦٨] يعني الجنة والنار وأهلهما من ملائكة العذاب والحور العين. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: سبعة لا تفنى العرش والكرسي، والقلم، والجنة والنار، وأهلهما، والأرواح.
Chapter on the discourse concerning the trumpet blast, resurrection, and gathering. The Mu'tazila said: When Allah commands the first trumpet blast, He annihilates the heavens and the earth, Paradise and Hell, and the souls; then He creates them again on the Day of Resurrection. And they argued with His statement, exalted: 'He is the First, the Last, the Manifest, the Hidden' (al-Hadid: 3). Then indeed Allah was in pre-eternity when no one of His creation was with Him; so likewise it is necessary that He not leave anything in the hereafter so that no one exists alongside His continuation, so that this name be His alone. The people of the Sunnah and the community said: Paradise and Hell are the two abodes of eternity and they are for reward and punishment, so they do not perish. Indicating it is His statement, exalted: 'And the trumpet is blown, and whoever is in the heavens and whoever is on the earth falls unconscious, except whom Allah wills' (al-Zumar: 68) – meaning Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants from among the angels of punishment and the houris. And the people of the Sunnah and the community said: Seven things do not perish: the Throne, the Footstool, the Pen, Paradise, Hell, their inhabitants, and the souls.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a chapter (faṣl) on the topics of the trumpet blast (al-nafkhu), resurrection (al-baʿth), and gathering (al-nushūr). It presents an objection from the Mu'tazila and the answer of Ahl al-Sunnah. The Mu'tazila argue that when Allah commands the first trumpet blast, everything – including the heavens, earth, Paradise, Hell, and souls – will be annihilated. Then Allah creates everything anew on the Day of Resurrection. Their proof is the verse 'He is the First and the Last' (al-Hadid: 3). They reason that just as Allah was alone in pre-eternity with none of His creation, so in the hereafter He should be alone with none remaining, so that the title 'the Last' applies uniquely to Him. The Ahl al-Sunnah respond that Paradise and Hell are the two abodes of eternity (dārā al-khuld) designated for reward and punishment; therefore, they do not perish. They cite the verse from Surat al-Zumar (39:68) about the trumpet blast causing all to fall unconscious 'except whom Allah wills' and interpret that exception as referring to Paradise, Hell, and their inhabitants (angels of punishment and houris). Finally, they list seven things that do not perish: the Throne (al-ʿarsh), the Footstool (al-kursiyy), the Pen (al-qalam), Paradise, Hell, their inhabitants, and the souls (al-arwāḥ).

النفخ
البعث
النشور
المعتزلة
الفناء
الجنة

دارا الخلد
العرش
الكرسي
القلم

?

?
The Ahl al-Sunnah listed seven eternal creations, including your own soul. Do you treat your soul as if it will never die, or do you neglect it for the sake of the world? What will you change starting now to nurture your soul for its eternal existence?

The Sunni Interpretation of the Verse on Killing a Believer
Nasafi presents Ibn Abbas's interpretation limiting eternal punishment to mustahill.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni interpretation of Quran 4:93, particularly the condition of istihlal (deeming killing lawful) as the basis for eternal punishment.

Core Idea
The verse threatens eternal fire only for those who deem killing believers lawful.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses the Mu'tazilite argument from the Quranic verse threatening eternal punishment for intentional murder. He presents the interpretation of Ibn Abbas, which restricts the verse to those who consider such killing lawful (mustahill). This lesson explores that interpretation and its scriptural basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Nasafi begins by citing the verse, then provides Ibn Abbas's explanation.
The passage is a direct response to the Mu'tazilite proof.
2
Identify Ibn Abbas's interpretation
Find how Ibn Abbas reinterprets the phrase 'his recompense is Hell'. What does he limit it to?
Look for the phrase 'أراد به إذا استحل قتل المؤمنين'.
3
Examine the scriptural support
Notice the proof from Quran 2:178. How does it show that intentional killing does not necessarily negate faith?
The verse addresses believers even after killing.
4
Reflect on the key condition
Understand that the condition of istihlal (deeming killing lawful) is what makes the act kufr.
This distinguishes the Sunni position from the Mu'tazilite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن قوله تعالى: {وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًا مُتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَالِدًا فِيهَا وَغَضِبَ اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَلَعَنَهُ وَأَعَدَّ لَهُ عَذَابًا عَظِيمًا}. قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما: فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ : أي جزاه. يدل عليه قوله تعالى: {يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْقِصَاصُ فِي الْقَتْلَى} فسماه مؤمنًا بعد قَتْلِ العَمْدِ، على أنا نقول: أراد به إذا استحل قتل المؤمنين. وقد روي أن الآية نزلت في حق مقيس بن صبابة الكناني، حين قتل مسلما من بني فهر بعدما قتل أخوه هشام بن صبابة وارتد ولحق بدار الحرب، والدليل على ارتداده قوله في شعره: قتلت بني فهر، وجملت عقله سراة بني النجار أرباب قارع شفيت به نفسي وأدركت منيتي وكنت إلى الأوثان أول راجع. ومن قتل مؤمنا متعمدا واستحل قتله كما استحل مقيس بن صبابة يكون كافرا ويخلد في النار مع سائر الكفار. قلت: ومقيس بن صبابة، أحد النفر الذين أمر النبي بقتله يوم الفتح، وقد ذكر الإمام =
And the answer concerning the saying of the Exalted: {And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein, and Allah's wrath is upon him, and He has cursed him and prepared for him a great punishment}. Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, said: 'His recompense is Hell' – i.e., his recompense. This is indicated by His saying: {O you who have believed, prescribed for you is legal retribution in cases of murder} – so He called him a believer after intentional killing, on the basis that we say: He intended it for when he considers the killing of believers lawful. And it has been narrated that the verse was revealed concerning Miqyas ibn Subaba al-Kinani, when he killed a Muslim from Banu Fihr after his brother Hisham ibn Subaba had been killed, and he apostatized and joined the land of war. The evidence of his apostasy is his saying in his poetry: 'I killed Banu Fihr, and I collected their blood money, the nobles of Banu al-Najjar, masters of Qari', I thereby cured myself and achieved my desire, and I was the first to return to idols.' And whoever kills a believer intentionally and considers his killing lawful, as Miqyas ibn Subaba did, becomes a disbeliever and will abide forever in Hell with the rest of the disbelievers. I say: Miqyas ibn Subaba was one of the men whom the Prophet ordered to be killed on the day of the conquest, and the Imam mentioned =
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage provides a specific answer to the Mu'tazilite proof from Quran 4:93. The Sunni response, building on the earlier general answer, now focuses on the verse itself. Ibn Abbas interprets 'his recompense is Hell' as referring to a particular type of recompense, not necessarily immediate. He points out that in the same surah (2:178), Allah addresses believers about retribution, still calling them believers even after intentional killing, implying that such a killing does not necessarily negate faith. The key is the condition of istihlal (deeming the killing lawful). The verse was revealed concerning Miqyas ibn Subaba, who killed a Muslim after his own brother was killed, then apostatized and returned to idolatry. His poem explicitly states he returned to idols; thus he was a murtadd (apostate). Therefore, the eternal punishment applies to one who not only kills intentionally but also considers it lawful (mustahill), thereby committing disbelief (kufr). Such a person becomes a disbeliever and will be in Hell forever like other disbelievers. The editorial note at the end provides additional historical context but is cut off.

Key Terms
قتل المؤمن
استحل
جزاء
خلود في النار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse threatens eternal punishment for every intentional murderer without exception.
Correction: The Sunni interpretation restricts the eternal punishment to those who deem killing believers lawful (mustahill), as indicated by Ibn Abbas.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abbas, to whom does the verse apply?
A) All intentional murderers.
B) Those who kill accidentally.
C) Those who deem killing believers lawful (mustahill).
D) Those who kill non-believers.

Key Takeaway
The eternal threat in Quran 4:93 applies only to those who consider killing believers lawful, not to all intentional murderers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever looked at a person committing a major sin and felt certain they have lost their faith? How does this lesson force you to stop and examine your own heart instead of judging theirs? What will you do the next time that feeling arises?
?
If even the act of intentional murder does not automatically remove faith, then what does that say about the mercy of Allah? Are you truly relying on His mercy for your own sins, or do you secretly believe you are safe because your sins are 'smaller'?
?
This lesson teaches that istihlal – deeming a sin lawful – is the real danger. Are there any areas in your life where you have quietly made excuses for a sin, convincing yourself it's not that bad? Will you repent from that attitude today?

The Case of Miqyas ibn Subaba: Historical Context of the Verse
Nasafi relates the story of Miqyas ibn Subaba as the occasion for the verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical background of Quran 4:93 through the story of Miqyas ibn Subaba, and why his actions exemplified the condition of istihlal.

Core Idea
Miqyas's apostasy and poetry show he deemed killing believers lawful, incurring eternal punishment.

The previous lesson established that the verse's threat applies to those who consider killing believers lawful. This lesson examines the historical context: the verse was revealed concerning Miqyas ibn Subaba, who killed a Muslim, apostatized, and returned to idolatry. His story illustrates the category of mustahill.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage about Miqyas. Note the key events: his brother's death, his killing of a Muslim, apostasy, and poetry.
The passage is taken from the same source as the previous lesson.
2
Identify the evidence of apostasy
Find the line from Miqyas's poetry that proves his return to idolatry.
The line is: 'وكنت إلى الأوثان أول راجع' (I was the first to return to idols).
3
Connect to the general ruling
Notice how Nasafi generalizes from Miqyas's case: anyone who kills a believer intentionally and deems it lawful becomes a disbeliever and will be in Hell forever.
This confirms the condition of istihlal.
4
Reflect on the historical note
Read the editorial note about the Prophet ordering Miqyas's execution. How does this reinforce the severity?
The note is cut off but suggests Miqyas was a marked apostate.

Mu'tazili Views on Intercession and Refutation of the First Group
Nasafi classifies Mu'tazili views on intercession and refutes the first group.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the diverse Mu'tazili views on intercession and the internal inconsistency in their first position as refuted by Nasafi.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila are diverse on intercession; their own Quranic proof refutes one of their positions.

This passage presents a classification of Mu'tazili views on intercession (al-shafa'a), a key theological topic. Nasafi first notes that some Mu'tazila deny intercession entirely, while others affirm it for three distinct groups. He then refutes the first group using a Quranic verse that, according to Mu'tazili principles, renders intercession unnecessary for them. As you read, notice how the refutation exploits an inconsistency in their own doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification of Mu'tazili views
Notice the two main positions: some deny intercession entirely, others affirm it for three specific groups. Identify these groups as you read.
The denial is absolute; affirmation is limited to three categories.
2
Understand the three groups that affirm intercession
Each group has a distinct need for intercession: forgiveness of minor sins, acceptance of repentance, or increase in ranks. Observe the conditions for each.
The third group avoids both major and minor sins.
3
Analyze the refutation of the first group
Nasafi argues that according to Mu'tazili doctrine, avoiding major sins obligates God to forgive minor sins (Quran 4:31), making intercession unnecessary. Notice how this refutes their claim.
This refutation relies on Mu'tazili principles, not external arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في إثبات الشفاعة تفرقت المعتزلة في الشفاعة، منهم من أنكر الشفاعة أصلاً ورأساً، ومنهم من أثبت الشفاعة لثلاث فرق منهم من اجتنب الكبائر، وارتكب الصغائر، فيحتاج إلى مغفرة الصغائر بشفاعة الأنبياء والملائكة صلوات الله عليهم. ومنهم من ارتكب الكبائر، ثم تاب عن ذلك، فيحتاج إلى قبول توبتهم بشفاعة الأنبياء والملائكة حتى يقبل الله تعالى توبتهم بشفاعتهم. ومنهم من اجتنب الكبائر والصغائر، فيحتاج إلى زيادة الدرجات على أعمالهم بشفاعة الأنبياء والملائكة، ولا شفاعة لغير هؤلاء. والجواب عن الفصل الأول: هذا على مذهبهم لا يصح؛ لأن عندهم أن من اجتنب الكبائر فواجب على الله تعالى أن يغفر ذنوبهم البتة بقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِن تَجْتَنِبُوا كَبَائِرَ مَا تُنْهَوْنَ عَنْهُ نُكَفِّرْ عَنكُمْ سَيِّئَاتِكُمْ وَنُدْخِلْكُم مُّدْخَلًا كَرِيمًا ﴾ [النساء: 31] فلا يحتاج إلى الشفاعة. وأما الثاني: قالوا: إن من ارتكب الكبيرة ثم تاب فيحتاج إلى قبول توبته بشفاعة الأنبياء والملائكة (1) أي النوع الأول ممن له شفاعة، وليس كما في المطبوعة.
Section on establishing intercession. The Mu'tazila differed concerning intercession: among them are those who denied intercession entirely and completely; and among them are those who affirmed intercession for three groups: among them, those who avoid major sins and commit minor sins, so they need forgiveness of minor sins through the intercession of the prophets and angels, peace be upon them. And among them are those who committed major sins, then repented from that, so they need acceptance of their repentance through the intercession of the prophets and angels until Allah, exalted is He, accepts their repentance through their intercession. And among them are those who avoid major sins and minor sins, so they need increase of ranks beyond their deeds through the intercession of the prophets and angels, and there is no intercession for other than these. The answer concerning the first type: This, according to their doctrine, is not valid; because according to them, whoever avoids major sins, it is obligatory upon Allah, exalted is He, to forgive their sins absolutely, by His statement, exalted is He: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden, We will remove from you your lesser sins and admit you to a noble entrance' [An-Nisa 4:31]. So he does not need intercession. As for the second: They said: 'Whoever commits a major sin then repents, he needs acceptance of his repentance through the intercession of the prophets and angels.' (1) i.e., the first type from those who have intercession, and it is not as in the printed edition.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage classifies Mu'tazili views on intercession (al-shafa'a) and refutes the first category. The author begins by noting the Mu'tazila differed: some denied intercession entirely, while others affirmed it for three specific groups. The first group: those who avoid major sins but commit minor sins need intercession for forgiveness of minor sins. The second group: those who commit major sins then repent need intercession for acceptance of their repentance. The third group: those who avoid both major and minor sins need intercession for increase in ranks. However, no intercession is allowed for other than these three groups. Then the author responds to the first group: according to the Mu'tazila's own doctrine, if one avoids major sins, God is obliged to forgive minor sins based on Quran 4:31. Therefore, such a person does not need intercession, making their claim inconsistent. Then the author mentions the second group's view but does not provide a refutation in this passage (possibly continued on next page). The footnote clarifies that the first type refers to the first group of those who have intercession.

Key Terms
الشفاعة
الكبائر
الصغائر
التوبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Mu'tazila uniformly deny intercession.
Correction: The passage shows that many Mu'tazila affirm intercession for three specific groups; others deny it entirely.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group does the Mu'tazila believe needs intercession for forgiveness of minor sins?
A) Those who commit major sins and repent.
B) Those who avoid major sins but commit minor sins.
C) Those who avoid both major and minor sins.
D) Those who commit major sins without repentance.

Key Takeaway
Mu'tazila held varying views on intercession; Nasafi refutes one position by showing it contradicts their own obligation-based theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you believe that avoiding major sins leads to forgiveness of minor sins, do you nonetheless treat minor sins lightly? How does this lesson challenge you to take every sin seriously, knowing that Allah's forgiveness is not a license but a mercy?
?
Nasafi exposed inconsistency in Mu'tazili thought. Are there any inconsistencies in your own approach to intercession and personal accountability before Allah? What specific step will you take to align your faith with the Quran and Sunnah?
?
Do you rely more on the hope of intercession or on your own avoidance of sin? How would your life change if you truly internalized that Allah's forgiveness is tied to your sincere effort to obey Him, not merely to a claim of faith?

The Reality of Intercession and the Wrongdoer Objection
Nasafi cites Quran and hadith to prove intercession and answers the objection that wrongdoers have no intercessor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars prove the reality of intercession for sinful believers and answer the objection that wrongdoers have no intercessor.

Core Idea
Intercession is real and promised for sinful Muslims, not denied to wrongdoers.

This lesson presents the Sunni doctrine of intercession (shafa'a) as an established truth based on Quran and hadith. The author provides two proofs and then addresses a potential objection by interpreting 'wrongdoers' as polytheists. Through careful textual analysis, you'll see how intercession remains valid for believers who commit major sins.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the claim
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author begins by stating that intercession is true, then gives proofs.
2
Examine the proofs for intercession
The author cites Quran 2:255 and the hadith about intercession for major sinners. Reflect on how these support the doctrine.
3
Understand the objection
The objection quotes Quran 40:18, which says wrongdoers have no intercessor. Note how this seems to contradict the previous claim.
4
Analyze the answer
The author answers by specifying that 'wrongdoer' in that verse refers to polytheists, citing Quran 31:13 and 26:100-101. See how the Quran interprets itself.
5
Synthesize the lesson
Consider how this defense upholds intercession for sinful Muslims while maintaining consistency with Quranic texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: الشفاعة حق يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿مَن ذَا الَّذِي يَشْفَعُ عِندَهُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ﴾ ومن رحمة الله وفضله أن يأذن بالشفاعة إلى الأنبياء والأولياء تكريمًا لهم وتشهيرًا لقدرهم عند الله وكذا قول النبي عليه السلام: «شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتي». فإن قيل: قال الله تعالى: ﴿مَا لِلظَّلِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعٍ يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: 18] ومرتكب الكبيرة ظالم قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَمِنْهُمْ ظَالِمُ لِنَفْسِهِ﴾ [فاطر: 32]. والجواب: قلنا أراد به الكافر والمشرك، قال الله تعالى خبرًا عنهم: ﴿فَمَا لَنَا مِن شَفِعِينَ * وَلَا صَدِيقٍ حَمِيمٍ﴾ [الشعراء: 100-101] والشرك هو الظلم، قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الشِّرْكَ لَظُلْمٌ عَظِيمٌ﴾ [لقمان: 13].
And the People of the Sunna and the Community said: intercession is true; it is indicated by His saying: 'Who is it that can intercede with Him except by His permission' and it is from God's mercy and bounty that He permits intercession to the prophets and saints as an honor to them and a proclamation of their rank before God, and likewise the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'My intercession is for the people of major sins from my ummah.' If it is said: God Almighty said: 'For the wrongdoers there is no devoted friend and no intercessor to be obeyed' [Quran 40:18] and the committer of a major sin is a wrongdoer; God Almighty said: 'Among them are wrongdoers to themselves' [Quran 35:32]. The answer: we said: He intended by that the disbeliever and polytheist; God Almighty said, informing about them: 'For we have no intercessors and no devoted friend' [Quran 26:100-101] and polytheism is wrongdoing; God Almighty said: 'Indeed, polytheism is a great wrong' [Quran 31:13].
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage presents the Sunni doctrine of intercession (shafa'a) as an established truth. The author provides two proofs: first, a Quranic verse indicating that intercession occurs only with God's permission (Quran 2:255), implying that intercession is possible; second, the hadith in which the Prophet states that his intercession is specifically for the people of major sins from his community. The author then addresses an objection: the Quran says wrongdoers (zālimīn) have no intercessor (Quran 40:18), and a committer of major sins is called a wrongdoer in another verse (Quran 35:32). The answer is that 'wrongdoer' in the first verse refers to the disbeliever and polytheist, not the sinful believer. This is supported by another Quranic passage where the disbelievers lament having no intercessors (Quran 26:100-101), and the verse that equates polytheism (shirk) with great wrongdoing (zulm) (Quran 31:13). Thus, the general term 'zālim' is specified to mean those guilty of shirk, thereby preserving intercession for sinful Muslims. The commentary flows logically: first establish the truth of intercession, then defend it against a scriptural objection by textual interpretation, using the principle that the Quran interprets itself.

الظالم
الكافر
المشرك

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'wrongdoers' in Quran 40:18 applies to all sinful believers, including those who commit major sins.
Correction: The verse actually refers specifically to polytheists and disbelievers, not to sinful Muslims. The Quran itself clarifies that polytheism is a great wrong (31:13), and the context of 26:100-101 confirms this.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Intercession is a reality for all believers, and apparent contradictions in the Quran are resolved by interpreting ambiguous verses in light of clear ones.
