Intercession for Major Sinners: Proofs and Objection
Nasafi states the Ahl al-Sunnah position on intercession and answers the objection from the verse about wrongdoers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunnah proof for intercession for major sinners and how they answer the objection from the Qur'anic verse denying intercession for wrongdoers.

Core Idea
Intercession is real, and the verse denying it applies only to polytheists, not Muslim sinners.

Intercession (shafa'ah) is a key belief of Ahl al-Sunnah, affirming that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and others can intercede for believers who have committed major sins. This lesson presents the scriptural proofs for intercession and addresses a common objection based on a verse that seems to deny intercession for wrongdoers. By the end, you will see how the objection is resolved by understanding who the 'wrongdoers' really are.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage (source_arabic) and its literal translation. Pay attention to the flow: statement, proofs, objection, answer.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two proofs for intercession
Nasafi provides two proofs: a Qur'anic verse (2:255) and a hadith. Notice how the hadith explicitly mentions 'ahl al-kaba'ir' (major sinners).
3
Understand the objection
The objector cites verse 40:18 which says there is no intercessor for wrongdoers. They argue that a major sinner is a wrongdoer based on verse 35:32. See how the objection is formed.
The objector is using Qur'an against Qur'an.
4
Study Nasafi's answer
Nasafi refutes by restricting the term 'wrongdoer' in the objection verse to polytheists and disbelievers, citing verses 26:100-101 and 31:13 to support that shirk is the ultimate wrongdoing.
This preserves intercession for Muslim sinners.
5
Reflect on the lesson's significance
Consider how this argument defends the mercy of Allah and the honor of the Prophet. Why is it important that intercession is for major sinners?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: الشفاعة حق يدل عليه قوله تعالى: {مَن ذَا الَّذِي يَشْفَعُ عِندَهُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ}، ومن رحمة الله وفضله أن يأذن بالشفاعة إلى الأنبياء والأولياء تكريمًا لهم وتشهيرًا لقدرهم عند الله، وكذا قول النبي عليه السلام: «شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتي». فإن قيل: قال الله تعالى: {مَا لِلظَّلِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعِ يُطَاعُ}، ومرتكب الكبيرة ظالم، قال الله تعالى: {فَمِنْهُمْ ظَالِمُ لِنَفْسِهِ}. والجواب: قلنا أراد به الكافر والمشرك، قال الله تعالى خبرًا عنهم: {فَمَا لَنَا مِن شَفِعِينَ * وَلَا صَدِيق حَمِيم}، والشرك هو الظلم، قال الله تعالى: {إِنَّ الشِّرْكَ لَظُلْمٌ عَظِيمٌ}.
And Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah said: Intercession is true, and the proof of it is His statement, the Most High: 'Who is there that can intercede with Him except by His permission?' And it is from the mercy of Allah and His favor that He permits intercession to the prophets and saints, as an honor for them and a showing of their standing with Allah. And likewise the statement of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'My intercession is for the people of major sins among my nation.' Then if it is said: Allah, the Most High, said: 'For the wrongdoers there is no intimate friend nor any intercessor to be obeyed,' and the committer of a major sin is a wrongdoer, as Allah, the Most High, said: 'Then among them are some who wrong themselves.' The answer: We said: He meant by it the disbeliever and the polytheist. Allah, the Most High, said, informing about them: 'Now we have no intercessors nor any close friend.' And polytheism is wrongdoing, as Allah, the Most High, said: 'Indeed, polytheism is a great wrongdoing.'
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the Ahl al-Sunnah position on intercession (shafa'ah) for major sinners, followed by a refutation of an objection. The author begins by affirming that intercession is a reality (haqq) and provides two proofs: a Qur'anic verse (2:255) stating that no one can intercede without Allah's permission, and a hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) says his intercession is for the people of major sins (ahl al-kaba'ir) among his nation. The author then presents an objection based on the verse 'For the wrongdoers there is no intimate friend nor any intercessor to be obeyed' (40:18). The objector argues that a committer of a major sin is a wrongdoer (zalim), citing another verse (35:32) that includes 'those who wrong themselves' among believers. The refutation clarifies that 'wrongdoer' in the first verse refers specifically to the disbeliever and polytheist, not the Muslim sinner. The author supports this by quoting the verse in which the polytheists themselves say 'Now we have no intercessors nor any close friend' (26:100-101), and then cites the verse 'Indeed, polytheism (shirk) is a great wrongdoing' (31:13). Thus, the apparent contradiction is resolved: the verse denying intercessors applies only to polytheists and disbelievers, not to believers who commit major sins.

Key Terms
شفاعة (intercession)
كبيرة (major sin)
ظالم (wrongdoer)
مشرك (polytheist)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse 'no intercessor for wrongdoers' (40:18) applies to all sinners, including Muslims who commit major sins.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that this verse refers specifically to polytheists and disbelievers, not to Muslim sinners. The Quran itself calls polytheism a 'great wrongdoing' (31:13), and polytheists admit they have no intercessors (26:100-101). Thus, intercession remains valid for believers.

Checkpoint

B) Only polytheists and disbelievers

D) Only the prophets

Key Takeaway
Intercession for Muslim major sinners is proven by the Quran and hadith, and the verse that seems to deny it applies only to polytheists.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Refuting the Hadith Denying Intercession: Istihlal Interpretation
Nasafi refutes the first objection by interpreting the hadith conditionally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the hadith that denies intercession to major sinners by interpreting it as referring to those who deem major sins lawful.

Core Idea
The hadith denying intercession is interpreted as referring to those who deem sins lawful, not all sinners.

The first objection Nasafi addresses is the hadith 'The people of major sins among my nation will not attain my intercession.' He begins by citing a stronger hadith that affirms intercession for major sinners and then argues that even if the first hadith is authentic, it must be understood in a specific context. This lesson explores that context and the concept of istihlal.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the passage where the objector presents the hadith and Nasafi responds by citing another hadith and the condition of istihlal.
Notice how Nasafi does not outright reject the hadith but qualifies its meaning.
2
Understand istihlal
The key concept is 'istihlal' – deeming a sin lawful. Nasafi says if the hadith is authentic, it applies only to those who consider major sins permissible.
3
See the prioritization of sound hadith
Nasafi prioritizes the hadith 'My intercession is for the people of major sins' and interprets the other accordingly. This shows the principle of reconciling conflicting reports.
This step is implicit in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: رُوِيَ عن النبي أنه قال: «لا ينال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي». قلنا: قد ذكرنا قوله عليه السلام: «شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتي»، فلو صح ذلك الخبر أراد به إذا استحل ذلك. فإن قيل: أنتم أثبتم الشفاعة للمؤمنين، ومرتكب الكبيرة خرج عن الإيمان بقول النبي عليه السلام: «لا يزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن». قلنا: أما هذا الخبر عن الحسن لم يصح، ولم يرد في خبر صحيح ولا سقيم، وإنما هو اختلاق وكذب، ولا يعارض الآثار الصحاح المتفق على صحتها، ثم لو جاز أن يكون قد روي، فلم يسقط الصحيح المجمع على صحته بالضعيف السقيم الذي لا أصل له مع إمكان الجمع بين الكل واستعمال الجميع، فتحمل صحاح الأخبار على ما قُلنا، ويحمل هذا الخبر على أنه أراد به الكبائر التي تُخرج من الإسلام، نحو الكفر بعد الإيمان، أو استحلال ما حرم الله، أو تكذيب بعض الرسل أو نحو ذلك، كما قلنا: إنا نجمع بين كل ما ذُكر في القرآن، وإن كان ظاهره يناقض بعضها بعضًا عند الجهال مثلكم. فإن قيل: هذا لا يصح مع قوله عليه السلام: «لا ينال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي»، والكافر بما ذكر به ليس من أمته. قلنا: بل يصح ذلك من وجهين: أحدهما: أنه أراد بذلك من كان من أمتي ثم ارتد، أو نحو ذلك. فقد يجوز أن يُسمى الشيء بما كان عليه أولاً، وإن كان في الحال لا يسمى به، ألا ترى إلى ما قال صلى الله عليه وسلم في النبيذ: «ثمرة طيبة، وماء طهور» يعني كان ثمرة طيبة وماء طهوراً، لا يريد أنه في الحال ثمرة، وكذلك أمر بلالاً: «ارجع فناد، ألا إن العبد نام» ولم يرد أنه الآن عبد، بل أراد أنه كان عبداً، لأن الصديق أعتق بلالاً قبل ذلك، يقال لعتيق الرجل: عبد بني فلان، أي كان عبداً لهم، ونحو ذلك كثير. ويحتمل أن يكون سَمَّاهم من أمته، لأنهم كانوا في عصره ووقته وقرنه، وكل قرن يُسمَّى أمة، ويكون ذلك فيمن كان آمن به في وقته ثم ارتد، أو كان في وقته ولم يؤمن، وسماه من أمته لأنه في قرنه وعصره. فصح ما قلناه وبطل تعلقهم بما لا أصل له.
Then if it is said: It is narrated from the Prophet that he said: 'The people of major sins among my nation will not attain my intercession.' We said: We have already mentioned his statement, peace be upon him: 'My intercession is for the people of major sins among my nation.' So if that report is authentic, he meant by it when he deems it lawful. Then if it is said: You have affirmed intercession for the believers, but the committer of a major sin has left faith by the statement of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'The fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer.' We said: As for this report from al-Hasan, it is not authentic, and it has not been transmitted in a sound or weak report; rather it is fabrication and lying, and it does not refute the sound narrations agreed upon for their authenticity. Then if it is conceded that it might have been narrated, the sound narration agreed upon for its authenticity is not nullified by the weak, sick report that has no origin, while it is possible to reconcile all and use all. So the sound narrations are interpreted according to what we have said, and this report is interpreted to mean that he intended by it the major sins that remove one from Islam, such as disbelief after faith, or deeming lawful what Allah has forbidden, or denying some of the messengers, or similar to that, as we said: We reconcile everything mentioned in the Qur'an, even if its apparent meaning contradicts each other according to the ignorant like you. Then if it is said: This is not valid with his statement, peace be upon him: 'The people of major sins among my nation will not attain my intercession,' and the disbeliever by what was mentioned with it is not from his nation. We said: Rather, it is valid in two ways: One of them: that he meant by that whoever was from my nation then apostatized, or similar to that. For it is permissible to call a thing by what it was formerly, even if it is not called by that in the present. Do you not see what the Prophet, peace be upon him, said about nabidh: 'A good fruit and purifying water' — meaning it was a good fruit and purifying water, not meaning that it is fruit in the present. And likewise he commanded Bilal: 'Return and call out, indeed the slave slept' — and he did not mean that he is now a slave, but rather he meant that he was a slave, because as-Siddiq freed Bilal before that. It is said of a freedman of a man: 'Slave of the sons of so-and-so,' meaning he was their slave. And many examples like this. And it is possible that he called them 'from his nation' because they were in his era, his time, and his century, and every century is called a nation. And that applies to whoever believed in him in his time then apostatized, or was in his time and did not believe, and he called him from his nation because he is in his century and era. So what we said is correct, and their clinging to what has no basis is invalid.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection that claims a hadith denies intercession to major sinners. The author addresses two objections. First, the objector cites the hadith 'The people of major sins among my nation will not attain my intercession.' The author responds by recalling the earlier hadith 'My intercession is for the people of major sins among my nation' and argues that if the objector's report is authentic, it refers to those who deem major sins lawful (istihlal), not all sinners. Second, the objector argues that a major sinner ceases to be a believer based on the hadith 'The fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer.' The author first questions the authenticity of this report, stating it is fabrication, and even if it were authentic, it does not override the sound, agreed-upon narrations. The sound narrations are interpreted to mean that intercession is for major sinners, while the weak report is interpreted to refer to sins that remove one from Islam (kufr, istihlal, etc.). The author then addresses a further objection: the disbeliever (who commits such sins) is not from the Prophet's nation. The author offers two interpretations: (1) The hadith 'my nation' can refer to those who were once from his nation then apostatized, and it is linguistically acceptable to call a thing by its former state, citing examples from the Prophet's own statements about nabidh and Bilal. (2) The term 'nation' (ummah) can mean a generation or century, so it refers to people who lived in his time, whether they believed or not, thus including those who apostatized or never believed. The author concludes that the objectors' argument is baseless.

Key Terms
كبيرة (major sin)
إستحلال (deeming lawful)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'لا ينال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي' unconditionally denies intercession to all major sinners.
Correction: Nasafi shows the hadith is either inauthentic or applies only to those who deem major sins lawful, not to all sinners.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, if the hadith 'The people of major sins among my nation will not attain my intercession' is authentic, whom does it refer to?
A) All major sinners without exception
B) Those who repent from major sins
C) Those who deem major sins lawful (istihlal)
D) Those who commit minor sins

Key Takeaway
The hadith denying intercession is interpreted conditionally: it applies only to those who consider major sins lawful, not to the general body of believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there a sin in your life that you have normalized or made excuses for, convincing yourself it's 'not that bad'? How does this lesson expose the danger of such self-deception, and what step will you take today to repent from it?
?
The Prophet's intercession is denied only to those who deem sins lawful. Are there areas in your life where you know something is wrong but you treat it as acceptable? What would it cost you to abandon that justification and seek forgiveness?
?
If the ultimate test is not just committing a sin but justifying it, how many of your daily choices have you rationalized? Will you commit to checking your heart for istihlal and asking Allah for sincerity before the Day when intercession matters most?

Refuting the Hadith on the Fornicator's Faith
Nasafi refutes the second objection by questioning the hadith's authenticity and then interpreting it restrictively.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the claim that major sinners leave faith by questioning the authenticity of the supporting hadith and by reconciling it with sound narrations.

Core Idea
The hadith 'no fornicator fornicates while a believer' is fabricated and cannot override sound narrations.

The second objection uses the hadith 'The fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer' to argue that major sinners exit faith. Nasafi responds by first declaring the hadith inauthentic, then even if it were authentic, it must be interpreted in a way that does not contradict the definitive texts on intercession. This lesson examines his approach to hadith criticism and reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the objector's argument: major sinner leaves faith, so cannot receive intercession.
2
Nasafi's response: authenticity
Nasafi states the hadith is not authentic – it is fabrication. Note his strong language: 'اختلاق وكذب'.
He also notes it doesn't appear in any sound or weak collection.
3
Even if authentic, reconciliation
Nasafi argues that even if it were narrated, the sound hadiths are prioritized, and the weak one is interpreted to refer to sins that remove one from Islam, not all major sins.
He provides examples: kufr, istihlal, takdhib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: رُوِيَ عن النبي أنه قال: «لا ينال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي». قلنا: قد ذكرنا قوله عليه السلام: «شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتي»، فلو صح ذلك الخبر أراد به إذا استحل ذلك. فإن قيل: أنتم أثبتم الشفاعة للمؤمنين، ومرتكب الكبيرة خرج عن الإيمان بقول النبي عليه السلام: «لا يزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن». قلنا: أما هذا الخبر عن الحسن لم يصح، ولم يرد في خبر صحيح ولا سقيم، وإنما هو اختلاق وكذب، ولا يعارض الآثار الصحاح المتفق على صحتها، ثم لو جاز أن يكون قد روي، فلم يسقط الصحيح المجمع على صحته بالضعيف السقيم الذي لا أصل له مع إمكان الجمع بين الكل واستعمال الجميع، فتحمل صحاح الأخبار على ما قُلنا، ويحمل هذا الخبر على أنه أراد به الكبائر التي تُخرج من الإسلام، نحو الكفر بعد الإيمان، أو استحلال ما حرم الله، أو تكذيب بعض الرسل أو نحو ذلك، كما قلنا: إنا نجمع بين كل ما ذُكر في القرآن، وإن كان ظاهره يناقض بعضها بعضًا عند الجهال مثلكم. فإن قيل: هذا لا يصح مع قوله عليه السلام: «لا ينال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي»، والكافر بما ذكر به ليس من أمته. قلنا: بل يصح ذلك من وجهين: أحدهما: أنه أراد بذلك من كان من أمتي ثم ارتد، أو نحو ذلك. فقد يجوز أن يُسمى الشيء بما كان عليه أولاً، وإن كان في الحال لا يسمى به، ألا ترى إلى ما قال صلى الله عليه وسلم في النبيذ: «ثمرة طيبة، وماء طهور» يعني كان ثمرة طيبة وماء طهوراً، لا يريد أنه في الحال ثمرة، وكذلك أمر بلالاً: «ارجع فناد، ألا إن العبد نام» ولم يرد أنه الآن عبد، بل أراد أنه كان عبداً، لأن الصديق أعتق بلالاً قبل ذلك، يقال لعتيق الرجل: عبد بني فلان، أي كان عبداً لهم، ونحو ذلك كثير. ويحتمل أن يكون سَمَّاهم من أمته، لأنهم كانوا في عصره ووقته وقرنه، وكل قرن يُسمَّى أمة، ويكون ذلك فيمن كان آمن به في وقته ثم ارتد، أو كان في وقته ولم يؤمن، وسماه من أمته لأنه في قرنه وعصره. فصح ما قلناه وبطل تعلقهم بما لا أصل له.
Then if it is said: It is narrated from the Prophet that he said: 'The people of major sins among my nation will not attain my intercession.' We said: We have already mentioned his statement, peace be upon him: 'My intercession is for the people of major sins among my nation.' So if that report is authentic, he meant by it when he deems it lawful. Then if it is said: You have affirmed intercession for the believers, but the committer of a major sin has left faith by the statement of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'The fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer.' We said: As for this report from al-Hasan, it is not authentic, and it has not been transmitted in a sound or weak report; rather it is fabrication and lying, and it does not refute the sound narrations agreed upon for their authenticity. Then if it is conceded that it might have been narrated, the sound narration agreed upon for its authenticity is not nullified by the weak, sick report that has no origin, while it is possible to reconcile all and use all. So the sound narrations are interpreted according to what we have said, and this report is interpreted to mean that he intended by it the major sins that remove one from Islam, such as disbelief after faith, or deeming lawful what Allah has forbidden, or denying some of the messengers, or similar to that, as we said: We reconcile everything mentioned in the Qur'an, even if its apparent meaning contradicts each other according to the ignorant like you. Then if it is said: This is not valid with his statement, peace be upon him: 'The people of major sins among my nation will not attain my intercession,' and the disbeliever by what was mentioned with it is not from his nation. We said: Rather, it is valid in two ways: One of them: that he meant by that whoever was from my nation then apostatized, or similar to that. For it is permissible to call a thing by what it was formerly, even if it is not called by that in the present. Do you not see what the Prophet, peace be upon him, said about nabidh: 'A good fruit and purifying water' — meaning it was a good fruit and purifying water, not meaning that it is fruit in the present. And likewise he commanded Bilal: 'Return and call out, indeed the slave slept' — and he did not mean that he is now a slave, but rather he meant that he was a slave, because as-Siddiq freed Bilal before that. It is said of a freedman of a man: 'Slave of the sons of so-and-so,' meaning he was their slave. And many examples like this. And it is possible that he called them 'from his nation' because they were in his era, his time, and his century, and every century is called a nation. And that applies to whoever believed in him in his time then apostatized, or was in his time and did not believe, and he called him from his nation because he is in his century and era. So what we said is correct, and their clinging to what has no basis is invalid.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection that claims a hadith denies intercession to major sinners. The author addresses two objections. First, the objector cites the hadith 'The people of major sins among my nation will not attain my intercession.' The author responds by recalling the earlier hadith 'My intercession is for the people of major sins among my nation' and argues that if the objector's report is authentic, it refers to those who deem major sins lawful (istihlal), not all sinners. Second, the objector argues that a major sinner ceases to be a believer based on the hadith 'The fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer.' The author first questions the authenticity of this report, stating it is fabrication, and even if it were authentic, it does not override the sound, agreed-upon narrations. The sound narrations are interpreted to mean that intercession is for major sinners, while the weak report is interpreted to refer to sins that remove one from Islam (kufr, istihlal, etc.). The author then addresses a further objection: the disbeliever (who commits such sins) is not from the Prophet's nation. The author offers two interpretations: (1) The hadith 'my nation' can refer to those who were once from his nation then apostatized, and it is linguistically acceptable to call a thing by its former state, citing examples from the Prophet's own statements about nabidh and Bilal. (2) The term 'nation' (ummah) can mean a generation or century, so it refers to people who lived in his time, whether they believed or not, thus including those who apostatized or never believed. The author concludes that the objectors' argument is baseless.

Key Terms
كبيرة (major sin)
إستحلال (deeming lawful)
ارتداد (apostasy)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'لا يزني الزاني...' proves that all major sinners lose their faith.
Correction: Nasafi shows the hadith is inauthentic, and even if authentic, it refers to specific sins that constitute apostasy.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi primarily refute the hadith 'The fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer'?
A) He accepts it but says it is abrogated
B) He says it is fabricated and not found in any hadith collection
C) He says it applies only to minor sins
D) He says it was said before the prohibition of fornication

Key Takeaway
The hadith that seems to deny faith to major sinners is inauthentic, and even if considered, it only refers to sins that entail apostasy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a hadith that challenges your hope in Allah's mercy, do you rush to accept it without checking its authenticity? How has this lesson changed your approach to such narrations? This week, when you hear a stern warning, will you verify its source before letting it shape your understanding of Allah?
?
Are there sins you secretly believe are too great for Allah to forgive, despite the clear texts on intercession? What would it take for you to truly trust in His mercy as described by the sound narrations? Will you actively remind yourself of this lesson when despair creeps in?
?
If you were to defend the doctrine of intercession to someone who quotes this hadith, would you be able to explain both the authenticity issue and the interpretation? Do you have the courage to challenge a commonly cited 'proof' that you know is weak? Will you prepare to respond with knowledge, not just comfort?

Interpreting 'My Nation' in the Hadith on Intercession
Nasafi refutes the objection by offering two linguistic and contextual interpretations of 'my nation.'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's two linguistic and contextual interpretations of the term 'my nation' in the hadith denying intercession to major sinners.

Core Idea
The term 'my nation' can refer to former believers or to contemporaries, even if they apostatize.

The final objection argues that the hadith 'The people of major sins among my nation will not attain my intercession' cannot refer to disbelievers because they are not from the Prophet's nation. Nasafi offers two sophisticated interpretations based on Arabic usage and historical context. This lesson explains those interpretations and illustrates them with examples from the Prophet's own speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the passage where the objector says the disbeliever is not from the nation, and Nasafi's two-part response.
2
First interpretation: former state
Nasafi says 'my nation' can refer to those who were once Muslim then apostatized. He supports this with how the Prophet called nabidh 'fruit' and Bilal 'slave' based on former states.
This is a linguistic principle: calling something by its past state.
3
Second interpretation: contemporary generation
Nasafi says 'ummah' can mean a generation or century, so it includes people living in the Prophet's time, whether believers or not.
This interpretation widens the scope of 'my nation' to contemporaries.

Source Text

Refuting the Zina Hadith Objection
Author refutes the objection that major sins expel from faith using a hadith about zina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's refutation of the claim that the hadith about zina proves that major sins remove faith, and the principles of reconciling apparent contradictions in hadith.

Core Idea
Not every hadith cited is authentic; even authentic ones require correct interpretation.

This passage presents a common objection: the hadith 'No zina while believing' seems to show that major sins destroy faith. The author responds with two powerful arguments—first questioning the hadith's authenticity, then offering an interpretation consistent with mainstream Sunni belief. Let's examine each step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and the supporting hadith
Read the opening line 'فإن قيل...' and the hadith citation. Note how the opponent uses the hadith to argue that major sins remove faith.
The hadith is well-known, but its exact wording matters.
2
Examine the author's first refutation: authenticity
The author claims the hadith is not authentic, calling it fabrication. Notice he says it is not found in any sound or weak report. This is a strong rejection.
He attributes it to al-Hasan (al-Basri), meaning it's a weak chain.
3
Examine the author's second refutation: interpretation
The author argues that even if authentic, it should be interpreted as referring to sins that expel from Islam entirely (kufr, istihlal, takdhib). This reconciles it with other authentic hadith.
This is a standard hermeneutical move: reconcile apparent contradictions.
4
Understand the principle of reconciliation
The author emphasizes that authentic reports should not be abandoned for weak ones when reconciliation is possible. He compares this to Quranic verses that seem contradictory to the ignorant.
This principle is key in usul al-hadith and usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: أنتم أثبتم الشفاعة للمؤمنين، ومرتكب الكبيرة خرج عن الإيمان؛ بقول النبي عليه السلام: لا يزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن (۱). أحدهما: أن هذا عن الحسن لم يصح، ولم يرد في خبر صحيح ولا سقيم، وإنما هو اختلاق وكذب، ولا يعارض الآثار الصحاح المتفق على صحتها، ثم لو جاز أن يكون قد رُوي، فلم يسقط الصحيحُ المُجْمَعُ على صحته، بالضعيف السقيم الذي لا أصل له مع إمكان الجمع بين الكل واستعمال الجميع، فتحمل صحاح الأخبار على ما قلا، ويحمل هذا الخبر على أنه أراد به الكبائر التي تُخرج من الإسلام، نحو الكفر بعد الإيمان، أو استحلال ما حرم الله، أو تكذيب بعض الرسل أو بعض هذا كما قلنا: إنا نجمع بين كل ما ذُكر في القرآن، وإن كان ظاهره يناقض بعضها بعضًا عند الجهال مثلكم....
For if it is said: You affirm intercession for the believers, while the perpetrator of a major sin exits from faith, due to the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer' (1). One of them: That this (hadith) from al-Hasan is not authentic, and it has not been transmitted in a sound or weak report, rather it is fabrication and falsehood, and it does not oppose the authentic narrations that are agreed upon their authenticity. Then if it were possible that it had been narrated, the authentic (hadith) agreed upon its authenticity cannot be abrogated by the weak, sickly (hadith) that has no basis, while reconciliation between all and using all is possible. So the authentic reports are interpreted upon what [؟] said, and this report is interpreted to mean that he intended by it the major sins that expel from Islam, such as disbelief after faith, or deeming lawful what Allah has forbidden, or denying some of the messengers, or some of that, as we said: We reconcile between all that is mentioned in the Quran, even if its apparent meaning contradicts each other in the view of the ignorant like you....
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The opponent argues that major sins remove one from faith, citing the hadith 'No zina while believing.' The author responds with two points (though only one is fully elaborated): First, this hadith is from al-Hasan al-Basri and is not authentic; it is a fabrication not found in any sound or even weak collection. Therefore, it cannot contradict well-established authentic hadith. Second, even if it were authentic, it would be interpreted as referring to sins that totally expel from Islam, like apostasy, not ordinary major sins. The author emphasizes the principle of reconciling conflicting reports when possible, just as apparent contradictions in the Quran are reconciled.

Key Terms
شفاعة
كبائر
إيمان
زنا
خبر صحيح
خبر سقيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about zina proves that any major sin destroys faith completely.
Correction: The author argues the hadith is unauthentic; even if authentic, it refers only to sins that constitute apostasy, not all major sins.

Checkpoint
According to the author, how should the hadith 'No zina while believing' be interpreted if it were authentic?
A) It applies to all major sins without exception.
B) It refers only to sins that expel from Islam, such as apostasy.
C) It was abrogated by later verses.
D) It only applies to non-Muslims.

Key Takeaway
The hadith on zina does not prove that all major sins remove faith; either it is unauthentic or it refers to apostasy-level sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a hadith that seems to conflict with what you understand about Allah's mercy, do you immediately reject it or do you seek reconciliation with other texts? Which approach does this lesson compel you to adopt?
?
Think of a time you committed a major sin. Did you feel your faith was completely gone? Based on this lesson's distinction, how can you maintain hope in Allah's forgiveness while still fearing His justice?
?
Are you willing to question the authenticity of narrations that are popular among people you respect if they contradict clear, established teachings? How would you handle the social pressure to accept such narrations?

The Second Objection: Hadith Denying Intercession
Author refutes the objection that the Prophet denied intercession to major sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author resolves the apparent contradiction between the hadith 'My intercession does not reach the people of major sins from my ummah' and the doctrine of intercession for sinful believers.

Core Idea
The hadith denying intercession targets apostates and disbelievers, not all major sinners.

The opponent cites a clear Prophetic hadith that seems to prevent intercession for major sinners. However, the author shows that this hadith does not actually contradict the belief in intercession for sinful believers. Two strong linguistic and contextual arguments are presented, each independently sufficient to harmonize the texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the hadith
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the opponent's claim that the hadith 'لا ينال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي' (My intercession does not reach the people of major sins from my ummah) undermines intercession for major sinners.
The hadith is authentic, so the author must explain it, not reject it.
2
Understand the first response: naming by past state
The author argues that the hadith refers to those who were believers and then apostatized. Linguistically, a thing can be named by its past state, just as the Prophet called nabīdh 'good fruit' based on its original ingredients, or called Bilāl a 'slave' after he was freed.
This shows the phrase 'from my ummah' applies in a historical sense, not current faith.
3
Understand the second response: 'ummah' as generation
Alternatively, 'ummah' can mean a generation or era. The hadith would then refer to those who lived in the Prophet's time and either apostatized or never believed. They are called 'from my ummah' because they belonged to his generation, not because they were believers.
Both responses exclude sincere believers who commit major sins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : هذا لا يصح مع قوله عليه السلام: «لا ينال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي والكافر بما ذكر به ثم ليس من أمته، قلنا: بل يصح ذلك من وجهين: أحدهما: أنه أراد بذلك من كان من أمتي ثم ارتد، أو نحو ذلك. الكتب، ويصير فقد يجوز أن يُسمى الشيء بما كان عليه أولاً، وإن كان في الحال لا يسمى به، ألا ترى إلى ما قال صلى الله عليه وسلم في النبيذ: «ثمرة طيبة، وماء طهور» يعني كان ثمرة طيبة وماء طهوراً، لا يريد أنه في الحال ثمرة، وكذلك أمر بلالاً: «ارجع فناد، ألا إن العبد نام ولم يرو أنه الآن عبد، بل أراد أنه كان عبداً، لأن الصديق أعتق بلالاً قبل ذلك، يقال لعتيق الرجل: عبد بني فلان، أي كان عبداً لهم، ونحو ذلك كثير. ويحتمل أن يكون سَمَّاهم من أمته، لأنهم كانوا في عصره ووقته وقرنه، وكلُّ قرن يُسمَّى أمة، ويكون ذلك فيمن كان آمن به في وقته ثم ارتد، فمن ذكر من أهل الردة، أو كان في وقته ولم يؤمن، وسماه من أمته لأنه في قرنه وعصره فصح ما قلناه وبطل تعلقهم بما لا أصل له انتهى بتصرف يسير (1) أخرجه الإمام البخاري في صحيحه (۸): ١٥٧)، ومسلم في صحيحه» (١: ٥٤) من حديث أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه.
For if it is said: This is not sound along with his statement (peace be upon him): 'My intercession does not reach the people of major sins from my ummah' and the disbeliever with what is mentioned, then he is not from his ummah. We say: Rather that is sound from two aspects: One of them: That he intended by that whoever was from my ummah then apostasized, or similar to that. For it is permissible to name a thing by what it was initially, even if it is not called by that in the present state. Do you not see what the Prophet (peace be upon him) said regarding nabīdh: 'Good fruit and pure water' meaning it was good fruit and pure water, not meaning that it is in the present state fruit. And similarly he commanded Bilāl: 'Go back and call out, verily the slave slept' – and he did not relate that he is now a slave, but rather he intended that he was a slave, because al-Ṣiddīq had freed Bilāl before that. One says of the freed slave of a man: 'Slave of Banī so-and-so', meaning he was a slave to them. And similar examples are many. And it is possible that he called them from his ummah because they were in his era, time, and generation, and every generation is called an ummah. And that applies to whoever believed in him in his time then apostasized, so whoever is mentioned from the people of apostasy, or whoever was in his time and did not believe, and he called him from his ummah because he is in his generation and era. So what we have said holds true, and their clinging to that which has no basis is invalidated. End with slight adaptation. (1) Reported by al-Bukhārī in his Ṣaḥīḥ (8:157) and Muslim in his Ṣaḥīḥ (1:54) from the hadith of Abū Hurayra (may Allah be pleased with him).
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponent cites the hadith 'My intercession does not reach the people of major sins from my ummah,' implying that major sinners are not eligible. The author gives two responses. First, the hadith may refer only to those who apostasize after being believers; they are called 'from my ummah' in a historical sense, just as the Prophet called nabīdh 'good fruit' based on its prior state, or called Bilāl a 'slave' after his emancipation. Second, the term 'ummah' can mean a generation or era, so those who lived in the Prophet's time and either apostasized or never believed are still called 'from my ummah' in that temporal sense. Thus the apparent denial of intercession is actually limited to apostates and disbelievers, not all major sinners.

Key Terms
شفاعة
عتيق
أمة
قرن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'لا ينال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي' absolutely denies intercession for any Muslim who commits a major sin.
Correction: The hadith actually refers to apostates or those who never truly believed, not to faithful Muslims who sin.

Checkpoint
What is the second reason the author gives for why the hadith 'لا ينال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي' does not contradict intercession for major sinners?
A) The hadith is weak and cannot be used.
B) The term 'ummah' can mean a generation, so it refers only to those in the Prophet's era who rejected him.
C) The hadith applies only to the time before hijrah.
D) The hadith was abrogated by later verses.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'My intercession does not reach the people of major sins from my ummah' does not deny intercession for faithful sinners, but specifically targets apostates and disbelievers of the Prophet's generation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadith that seems to deny intercession to 'people of major sins' is explained to refer only to apostates. Are you confident that your faith is so firm that you will never fall into apostasy? What steps are you taking right now to protect your iman from erosion?
?
This lesson shows that the Prophet's intercession is vast, but it is not for those who abandon faith. If you were to die tonight, would you die as a believer or as someone who has turned away? What does your answer require you to change today?
?
The author used linguistic nuance to preserve hope for sinners. But this hope is not a license to sin. Are you using Allah's mercy as an excuse to persist in a sin you know is major? What concrete action will you take this week to repent and never return to that sin?

Hadith of Abu Dharr on Entering Paradise with Major Sins
Author supports intercession with hadith of Abu Dharr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of Abu Dharr supports the doctrine of intercession for major sinners who do not deem their sins lawful.

Core Idea
Sincere declaration of faith grants Paradise even with major sins, unless sins are deemed lawful.

The author concludes his defense of intercession by invoking a powerful hadith. The Prophet ﷺ instructed Abu Dharr to announce that whoever says 'There is no god but Allah' will enter Paradise, regardless of major sins like adultery and theft. This passage clarifies the key condition: the sinner must not deem the sin lawful.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and Translation
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb its wording. Then read the English translation to understand the meaning. Notice the direct citation of the hadith.
The Arabic is concise; the hadith is quoted in full.
2
Identify the Condition (Istihlal)
The author begins with 'قلنا: أراد به أنه إذا استحل ذلك' meaning 'We said: He intended by that when he deems it lawful.' This sets the condition that intercession applies only when the sin is not considered lawful.
Istihlal (deeming lawful) is a critical concept in kalam.
3
Connect to Intercession Doctrine
The hadith directly supports that major sinners can be forgiven through intercession if they maintain sincere faith (la ilaha illallah) and do not consider their sins permissible. This refutes the Kharijite position that major sins nullify faith entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلنا: أراد به أنه إذا استحل ذلك، لما رُوي عن النبي أنه قال لأبي ذر رضي الله عنه: نادِ في الناس مَنْ قال : لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة، وإن زنى وإن سرق» (۱). (۱) أخرجه الإمام البخاري في صحيحه (۸): (۹۵)، ومسلم في صحيحه» (٧: ٤٥).
We said: He intended by that that when he deems it lawful, due to what was narrated from the Prophet that he said to Abū Dharr (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Call out among the people: Whoever says there is no god but Allah will enter Paradise, even if he commits adultery and even if he steals.' (1) (1) Reported by al-Bukhārī in his Ṣaḥīḥ (8:95) and Muslim in his Ṣaḥīḥ (7:45).
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a final supporting argument. The author clarifies that the earlier statement about intercession for major sinners is understood when a person deems the sin lawful (istihlāl). To back this up, he cites the well-known hadith where the Prophet instructs Abū Dharr to announce that whoever sincerely declares 'There is no god but Allah' will enter Paradise, even if they commit major sins like adultery and theft. This hadith directly supports the possibility of intercession and forgiveness for major sinners who do not consider their sins lawful.

Key Terms
لا إله إلا الله
جنة
زنى
سرق
استحلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith encourages sin or negates punishment altogether, implying that one can commit sins freely after saying the Shahada.
Correction: The author explicitly conditions the promise on not deeming the sin lawful (istihlal). The hadith affirms that sincere faith leads to ultimate salvation, but sins still require repentance or intercession, and they are not to be taken lightly.

Checkpoint
According to the final response, what condition must be absent for the promise of Paradise to apply despite major sins?
A) The sin must be committed only once.
B) The person must not deem the sin lawful (istihlal).
C) The person must perform repentance immediately.
D) The sin must be against God only, not against others.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Abu Dharr shows that sincere faith in 'la ilaha illallah' leads to Paradise despite major sins, provided that the sins are not deemed lawful (istihlal).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used the hope of this hadith as a license to continue a sin, excusing yourself with 'I still believe, so I'll be okay'? What does that reveal about your trust in Allah's mercy versus your commitment to obedience?
?
Is there a sin in your life that you have slowly begun to justify or minimize, making it feel less serious—effectively deeming it lawful in your heart? How will you repent and restore the weight of that sin before Allah today?
?
If you truly internalized that a sincere 'la ilaha illallah' guarantees Paradise despite your failures, how would that change the way you view your past mistakes and your current struggle with sin? Would it make you more grateful or more careless?

Affirmation of the Balance, Reckoning, Path, Pond, and Intercession
Refutation of Mu'tazila denial of eschatological realities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunna affirm the literal reality of eschatological events (Balance, Reckoning, Path, Pond, Intercession) and the wisdom behind weighing deeds despite Allah's omniscience.

Core Idea
The scales of justice are real — not metaphor — and reveal to the servant what Allah already knows.

This passage tackles a fundamental disagreement between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna over the reality of eschatological events. The Mu'tazila dismiss the Balance, Reckoning, Path, Pond, and Intercession as metaphors for God's justice, while the Sunni position holds them as literal truths. As you read, notice how the author uses both Quranic evidence and rational explanation to defend the literal view.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila argument
Pay attention to their reasoning: they claim the Balance is only needed by common people and grocers, and that God's mention of it refers to justice metaphorically. They also argue that the people of Paradise do not need reckoning or intercession.
Mu'tazila rely on rationalist interpretation (ta'wil) to dismiss literal meanings.
2
Note the Sunni response
Ahl al-Sunna affirm all these as true (haqq). The author specifically states the Pond, Kawthar in Paradise, and the Path are true. He then cites Quran 23:102 and a report from Ibn Abbas describing the Balance's two pans.
The evidence is textual and literal, not metaphorical.
3
Analyze the objection and answer
The objection asks why deeds are weighed if Allah already knows them. The answer reveals a key wisdom: the weighing is for the servant's own knowledge, so he can personally realize his fate.
This addresses a common misunderstanding about necessity of physical processes alongside divine omniscience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في إثبات الميزان والحساب والصراط والحوض والشفاعة] قالت المعتزلة : لا ميزان ولا حساب ولا صِراطَ ، ولا حَوْضَ، ولا شفاعة، والميزان يحتاج إليه العامي والبقالون، وكل موضع ذكر الله تعالى الميزان والحساب أراد به العدل، لأن الميزان إنما يحتاج إلى معرفة قدر الحسنات والسيئات، والله تعالى عالم بذلك كله، فمن كانت حسناته أكثر يؤمر به إلى الجنة، ومن كانت سيئاته أكثر يبعث به إلى النار، ومن كان من أهل الجنة لا يوقف في القيامة ولا يحتاج إلى الشفاعة. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: كلُّ ذلك حقٌّ، والحوض في القيامة حقٌّ، والكَوْثَرُ في الجنة حق، والصراط حق. يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَن ثَقُلَتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَيكَ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ ﴾ [المؤمنون: 102]، وقال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما: الميزان له كفتان إحداهما بالمشرق والآخر بالمغرب. فإن قيل: أيش الحكمة في الميزان، ولماذا تُوزن الحسنات والسيئات، والله تعالى عالم بذلك؟ قلنا: نعم، إن الله تعالى عالم بذلك، ولكن العبد لا يعلم به، وإنما توزن الحسنات والسيئات حتى يعلم أنه من أهل الجنة أو النار.
Chapter on the establishment of the Balance, Reckoning, Path, Pond, and Intercession. The Mu'tazila said: There is no Balance, no Reckoning, no Path, no Pond, and no Intercession. The Balance is needed by the common person and grocers, and every place where Allah mentions the Balance and Reckoning, He meant justice, because the Balance is only needed to know the measure of good deeds and evil deeds, and Allah knows all of that. So whoever's good deeds are more, he is ordered to Paradise, and whoever's evil deeds are more, he is sent to Hell, and whoever is among the people of Paradise is not stopped on the Day of Resurrection and does not need intercession. Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said: All of that is true. The Pond on the Day of Resurrection is true, the Kawthar in Paradise is true, and the Path is true. It is evidenced by His saying: 'Then those whose scales are heavy, they are the successful' (al-Mu'minun 102). And Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, said: The Balance has two pans, one in the East and the other in the West. If it is said: What is the wisdom in the Balance, and why are good deeds and evil deeds weighed while Allah knows all that? We said: Yes, Allah knows that, but the servant does not know it, and good deeds and evil deeds are only weighed so that he knows whether he is among the people of Paradise or Hell.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal refutation of the Mu'tazila's denial of eschatological realities. The Mu'tazila argue that the Balance, Reckoning, Path, Pond, and Intercession are metaphorical references to God's justice, not physical entities; they claim that the Balance is only needed by common people and grocers to measure quantities, while God already knows deeds directly. They further argue that the people of Paradise do not need to be stopped for reckoning or intercession. Ahl al-Sunna respond by affirming all these as literal truths (haqq). They cite Quran 23:102, which speaks of scales weighing deeds, and a report from Ibn Abbas describing the Balance as having two pans. A potential objection asks the wisdom of weighing when God already knows. The answer explains that the weighing is for the servant's own knowledge: so that he may personally realize his fate. This underscores the Sunni commitment to the literal reality of these eschatological events without reducing them to mere allegory.

Key Terms
الميزان
الحساب
الصراط
الحوض
الشفاعة
الكوثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Balance, Reckoning, Path, etc., are metaphorical references to God's justice because God already knows deeds directly.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna affirm these as literal realities. The weighing of deeds is real and serves to inform the servant of his fate, not to inform Allah who already knows.

Checkpoint
Why do Ahl al-Sunna affirm that deeds are weighed on the Balance despite Allah's omniscience?
A) To inform Allah of the deeds
B) To inform the servant of his fate
C) To test the angels
D) To increase the weight of good deeds

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna affirm the Balance, Reckoning, Path, Pond, and Intercession as literal realities, and the weighing of deeds is for the servant's knowledge, not God's.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every deed—even a word you spoke yesterday—will be weighed on a literal scale? How would you live today if you knew the scale was already in motion? Commit to one deed you will try to make 'heavy' before tomorrow.
?
The author says the weighing is so that the servant knows his fate. If you could see your own scale right now, would the heavy side be good deeds or bad? What is the single sin you are most afraid to see on that scale? Write it down sincerely—between you and Allah—and resolve to leave it today.
?
The Mu'tazila denied intercession because they said the people of Paradise do not need it. But you and I are not certain we are among them. If the Prophet (peace be upon him) offered to intercede for you, would you accept it humbly, or would you rely only on your deeds? What does your answer reveal about your heart's trust in Allah's mercy?

Affirmation of the Balance, Account, Path, Pond, and Intercession
Nasafi states Mu'tazila denial and Sunni affirmation of eschatological realities with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the literal reality of the Balance, Account, Path, Pond, and Intercession, and the Mu'tazila metaphorical interpretation.

Core Idea
The five eschatological realities are literal truths, not metaphors.

This passage presents a classic theological dispute between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna over the nature of the afterlife. The Mu'tazila argue that terms like 'Balance' and 'Account' are metaphors for justice, while Sunnis insist on their literal reality. Understanding this debate clarifies the Sunni commitment to the tangible aspects of the Hereafter.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila argument
Notice how they deny each item and why they interpret the Quran metaphorically. They rely on reason over literal text.
Their reasoning is based on the idea that God already knows deeds.
2
Read the Sunni response
See how they affirm every item and provide a Quranic proof. The verse from Al-Mu'minun (23:102) is key.
Ibn Abbas' description of the Balance adds further detail.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this matters for belief in the unseen. Sunnis accept these as true realities, even if not fully comprehensible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

A chapter on establishing the Balance, the Account, the Path, the Pond, and Intercession. The Mu'tazila said: There is no Balance, no Account, no Path, no Pond, and no Intercession. The Balance is needed by the commoner and merchants, and every place where God Almighty mentions the Balance and Account He intended justice, because the Balance is only needed to know the measure of good deeds and bad deeds, and God Almighty knows all of that. So whoever's good deeds are more is commanded to go to Paradise, and whoever's bad deeds are more is sent to the Fire, and whoever is among the people of Paradise is not stopped on the Day of Resurrection and does not need intercession. And Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said: All of that is true, and the Pond on the Day of Resurrection is true, and al-Kawthar in Paradise is true, and the Path is true. The proof for it is His statement Most High: {Then those whose scales are heavy - they are the successful} (Al-Mu'minun 23:102). And Ibn Abbas, may God be pleased with them both, said: The Balance has two pans, one in the east and the other in the west.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter on five eschatological realities: the Balance (mīzān), Account (ḥisāb), Path (ṣirāṭ), Pond (ḥawḍ), and Intercession (shafāʿa). The author first presents the Mu'tazila position: they deny all these as literal entities. They argue that the Balance is only for common people and merchants to measure quantities; when God mentions it in the Quran, He intends justice metaphorically, not a physical scale. They claim that those destined for Paradise are not stopped for judgment and need no intercession. Then Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a affirm all as true, including the Pond, Kawthar (a river in Paradise), and the Path. A direct Quranic proof is cited: 'Then those whose scales are heavy — they are the successful' (23:102), indicating a literal weighing of deeds. Ibn Abbas further describes the Balance as having two pans spanning from east to west, emphasizing its immense reality.

ميزان
صراط
حوض
شفاعة
كوثر
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Balance, Account, Path, Pond, and Intercession are metaphors, not literal realities.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna affirm they are literal based on the Quran and hadith.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The five eschatological realities (Balance, Account, Path, Pond, Intercession) are literal truths affirmed by Ahl al-Sunna and supported by the Quran.

The Wisdom of Weighing Deeds
Nasafi answers an objection about the purpose of weighing deeds when God already knows.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why good and bad deeds are weighed on the Balance even though God already knows them completely.

Core Idea
The Balance shows the servant his own deeds so he can know his fate.

This passage addresses a common question: if God already knows all deeds, why weigh them on the Balance? Nasafi's answer reveals that the purpose is for the servant's own knowledge and certainty, not for God's. The weighing is a concrete demonstration of divine justice, allowing the servant to see the outcome firsthand.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully. Notice how the objection is framed and how the answer directly responds to it.
The objection uses 'فإن قيل' (if it is said), a common kalam technique.
2
Distinguish God's knowledge from the servant's
The answer concedes that God knows all deeds perfectly, but it emphasizes that the servant does not know his own fate beforehand. Weighing is for the servant's benefit.
This distinction is key to answering the objection.
3
Reflect on the wisdom argument
Consider why a visible, physical weighing is needed for the servant to know his outcome. This shows that the Balance is a mercy and a demonstration of justice, not a redundancy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: أيش الحكمة في الميزان، ولماذا تُوزن الحسنات والسيئات، والله تعالى عالم بذلك؟ قلنا: نعم، إن الله تعالى عالم بذلك، ولكن العبد لا يعلم به، وإنما توزن الحسنات والسيئات حتى يعلم أنه من أهل الجنة أو النار.
For it is said: What is the wisdom in the Balance, and why are good deeds and bad deeds weighed, while God Almighty knows about that? We said: Yes, indeed God Almighty knows about that, but the servant does not know it, and rather good deeds and bad deeds are weighed so that he may know whether he is among the people of Paradise or the Fire.

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer: an opponent asks what wisdom there is in the Balance if God already knows all deeds. The author replies that God's knowledge is complete, but the servant does not know his own fate beforehand. The weighing is a concrete demonstration for the servant, allowing him to see the outcome and thus know his destination. The wisdom is not for God's sake but for the servant's own certainty and acknowledgment of divine justice.

The Order of Reading Books and the Weighing
Nasafi resolves the order between reading books and the Balance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the order between reading the books and the weighing on the Balance is not explicitly mentioned in the Quran, but scholars have inferred that reading comes first.

Core Idea
The Balance comes after the books are read; no deed remains after weighing.

A question arises in Islamic eschatology: when the deeds are presented and weighed, which happens first? The Quran does not explicitly state the sequence. In this passage, Imam Nasafi explains that scholars have derived the order through reasoning, using a verse that implies the weighing is the final step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the structure: a question, then an answer, then a proof from the Quran.
The passage is concise; pay attention to the logical flow.
2
Identify the question and answer
The question is about precedence: which comes first, reading the books or the Balance? The answer states there is no explicit text, but scholars inferred the order.
The author uses 'قلنا' to present the accepted position.
3
Understand the inference from the verse
The verse (23:102) says those whose scales are heavy are successful. This implies that after the weighing, no deed remains—so the reading must have occurred before the weighing.
This is an example of istidlāl (deductive inference) in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : قراءة الكتب أسبق أم الميزان أسبق ؟ قلنا: ليس فيه نص، لكن استنبط العلماء على طريق الاستدلال أن قراءة الكتب أسبق، يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَن ثَقُلَتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُوْلَيْكَ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ١٠٢] وهذا يدل على أن لا يبقى عمل بعد الميزان.
For it is said: Is the reading of the books earlier or the Balance earlier? We said: There is no explicit text, but the scholars inferred through deduction that the reading of the books is earlier. The proof for it is His statement Most High: {Then those whose scales are heavy - they are the successful} (Al-Mu'minun 23:102), and this indicates that no deed remains after the Balance.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage answers a question about the chronological order of two events after resurrection: the reading of each person's book of deeds and the weighing on the Balance. The author states there is no explicit revealed text (naṣṣ) specifying the order. However, scholars have deduced through inference (istidlāl) that the reading comes first. The proof is the Quranic verse (23:102) which speaks about the results of the weighing, implying that after the weighing there is no further action or reckoning—so the reading must have already taken place before the weighing.

Key Terms
قراءة الكتب
ميزان
استدلال
نص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Quran explicitly states the order between reading books and weighing.
Correction: The author clarifies there is no explicit text (naṣṣ); the order is derived via inference using a verse about the Balance.

Checkpoint
What do scholars infer about the order between reading the books and the weighing?
A) The weighing comes first.
B) They are simultaneous.
C) Reading the books comes first.
D) The order is unknown.

Key Takeaway
The reading of the books precedes the weighing on the Balance, as deduced from the Quranic verse that no deed remains after the weighing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Balance on the Path
Nasafi locates the Balance on the Path and explains its function.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Balance and Account take place on the Path (al-ṣirāṭ) and that deeds determine one's final destination.

Core Idea
The Balance is on the Path; deeds weigh the fate.

Nasafi begins by addressing a common query about the location of the divine reckoning. He firmly places the Balance and Account on the Path, the bridge over Hell, and connects the weighing of deeds to the outcome of Paradise or Hell. A prophetic hadith illustrates the sudden fall of some into the Fire.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and answer
Read the opening question about the location of the Account and Balance, and Nasafi's clear answer that they are on the Path.
This establishes the location immediately.
2
Understand the weighing mechanism
Notice that deeds are weighed: heavy scales lead to Paradise, light scales to the Fire. Reflect on the direct connection between action and consequence.
3
Reflect on the prophetic simile
Read the hadith: some of the community fall into the Fire like rain. This emphasizes that falling is not rare but can happen to many.
This adds a somber note to the weighing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: أين الحساب والميزان؟ قلنا: الميزان والحساب علي الصِّراط، فتُوزن حسنات كل واحد وسيئاته، فمن ثقلت موازينه يمضي إلى الجنة، ومن كان من أهل الشقاوة يسقط في النار، لما رُوِيَ عن رسول الله أنه قال: من أمتي من يسقط في النار كالمطر. وفي الخبر: يوقف العبد على الصراط سبع مواقف، الموقف الأول: يُسأل عن الإيمان، والموقف الثاني: يُسأل عن الوضوء والاغتسال، والموقف الثالث: يُسأل عن الصلاة، والرابع: يُسأل عن الصوم، والخامس: يُسأل عن الحج، والسادس: يُسأل عن الزكاة، والموقف السابع : يُسأل عن بِرِّ الوَالدَيْن.
For it is said: Where is the Account and the Balance? We said: The Balance and the Account are on the Path, so the good deeds and bad deeds of each one are weighed. Whoever's scales are heavy proceeds to Paradise, and whoever is among the wretched falls into the Fire, as narrated from the Messenger of God that he said: 'Some of my community fall into the Fire like rain.' And in the report: 'The servant is stopped on the Path at seven stations: the first station: he is asked about faith; the second station: he is asked about ablution and ritual bathing; the third station: he is asked about prayer; the fourth: he is asked about fasting; the fifth: he is asked about Hajj; the sixth: he is asked about Zakat; and the seventh station: he is asked about kindness to parents.'
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage answers a question about the location of the Account and Balance. The author states they take place on the Path (al-ṣirāṭ), the bridge over Hell. After the weighing, those with heavy scales go to Paradise; those with light scales fall into Hell. A prophetic hadith illustrates that some people from the Muslim community will fall into the Fire like rain. Then a report (al-khabar) details seven stations on the Path where the servant is stopped for questioning: about faith (īmān), ablution and ritual bath (wuḍūʾ wa ghusl), prayer (ṣalāh), fasting (ṣawm), pilgrimage (ḥajj), alms tax (zakāh), and kindness to parents (birr al-wālidayn). These stations represent the comprehensive judgment on major religious duties and social obligations.

حساب
ميزان

Misconception: Some think the Balance is separate from the Path.
Correction: The text explicitly says 'الميزان والحساب علي الصراط' (the Balance and Account are on the Path).

Checkpoint

A) In the hand of God.
B) On the Path.
C) In Paradise.
D) In the book of deeds.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Order of Events After Death: Books Before the Scale
Nasafi answers whether reading the books or the scale comes first after death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why scholars deduced that reading the book of deeds precedes the weighing of deeds (al-mizan) after death, despite the absence of an explicit textual order.

Core Idea
Even without an explicit text, Quranic inference shows reading the books comes before the scale.

This lesson examines a common question about the sequence of events after death: When are our deeds read to us and when are they weighed? Imam Nasafi presents the scholarly view that reading the books of deeds occurs before the scale, based on deductive reasoning from the Quran. The verse about the scales being heavy implies that after the scale, no deed remains, so reading must come earlier.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the formula 'فإن قيل / قلنا' which signals an objection and response.
This is a standard dialectical structure in kalam.
2
Identify the key Quranic evidence
Locate the verse from Surat al-Mu'minun (102) and note how the scholars used the word 'ثم' (then) to deduce sequence.
3
Understand the deduction
Reflect on why the verse implies that no deed remains after the scale, and therefore reading must come before weighing.
This connects to the objective.
4
Consider the misconception
Some assume the scale comes first because deeds are weighed, but the verse shows the scale is the final event.
The correction is that reading precedes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : قراءة الكتب أسبق أم الميزان أسبق ؟
قلنا: ليس فيه نص، لكن استنبط العلماء على طريق الاستدلال أن قراءة الكتب أسبق، يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَن ثَقُلَتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُوْلَيْكَ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ١٠٢] وهذا يدل على أن لا يبقى عمل بعد الميزان.
If it is said: Is reading the books earlier or is the scale earlier? We say: There is no explicit text, but the scholars inferred through deduction that reading the books is earlier. It is indicated by His statement, the Exalted: 'Then those whose scales are heavy, those are the successful' [al-Mu'minun: 102]. And this indicates that no deed remains after the scale.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (فإن قيل/قلنا) unit. The objector asks about the temporal order of two events after death: reading the book of deeds and the weighing of deeds (الميزان). Which comes first? The answer begins by admitting there is no explicit textual (نص) teaching, but the scholars have deduced from Quranic evidence that reading the books comes first. The proof is verse 102 of Surat al-Mu'minun: 'Then those whose scales are heavy...' The word 'then' (ثم) indicates sequence, and because it mentions the scales after implying previous actions, and states that those whose scales are heavy are the successful, it implies that the weighing is the final stage after which no deed remains. Therefore, the reading of the books must occur before the scale, because after the scale there is no remaining work.

Key Terms
قراءة الكتب
الميزان
استدلال
نص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The scale (al-mizan) comes before reading the books because deeds are weighed.
Correction: Scholars deduced from the Quran that reading the books precedes because the verse states that after the scale, no deed remains, implying the scale is the final event.

Checkpoint
According to the scholars' deduction, which event comes first after death?
A) The scale (al-mizan)
B) Reading the books (qira'at al-kutub)
C) Both happen simultaneously
D) Neither, the order is unknown

Key Takeaway
Even without an explicit text, the Quran indicates that reading the book of deeds occurs before the weighing, as the scale is the final judgment leaving no deeds afterward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imagine standing before your Lord while your book of deeds is read aloud to you. Knowing that the weighing comes after that reading, what do you fear more: the reading or the weighing? Why? What does that reveal about how you view your own actions?
?
The scholars deduced the order of these events without an explicit text because they trusted that every detail of the afterlife has wisdom. How much effort have you personally invested in understanding what will happen after death? Are you relying on your intellect and the Quran to prepare, or are you avoiding the thought altogether?
?
After the scale, no deed remains. If your life ended right now, what would your book contain that you hope will tip the scales? What action can you take today—however small—to add weight to that side, before the reading begins?

The Sirat Bridge: Location of the Scale and Account
Nasafi explains that the scale and account take place on the Sirat bridge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the weighing of deeds and the account occur on the Sirat bridge, and that believers are questioned at seven stations there.

Core Idea
The scale and account are set on the Sirat bridge over Hell.

A common question about the afterlife is where the weighing of deeds and the account will take place. Imam Nasafi answers clearly: it happens on the Sirat, the bridge spanning over Hell. He then details the consequences of the weighing and supports it with a hadith describing seven stations where each person is questioned about their faith and duties.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Begin by reading the Arabic passage where the question 'Where is the account and the scale?' is posed and answered. Notice that the answer directly places them on the Sirat.
2
Understand the weighing and its consequences
The passage explains that deeds are weighed on the Sirat. Those with heavy scales go to Paradise; those with light scales fall into the Fire. Reflect on the imagery of falling like rain from the hadith.
3
Examine the seven stations of questioning
The longer tradition lists seven stations where the servant is stopped and asked about specific obligations: faith, purity, prayer, fasting, pilgrimage, zakat, and kindness to parents. Consider the comprehensiveness of this examination.
4
Connect to the broader eschatological framework
Think about how the Sirat integrates multiple events: the scale, the account, and the questioning. This shows that salvation depends on both belief and righteous actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: أين الحساب والميزان؟
قلنا: الميزان والحساب علي الصِّراط، فتُوزن حسنات كل واحد وسيئاته، فمن ثقلت موازينه يمضي إلى الجنة، ومن كان من أهل الشقاوة يسقط في النار، لما رُوِيَ عن رسول الله أنه قال: من أمتي [مَنْ] يسقط في النار كالمطر.
وفي الخبر: «يوقف العبد على الصراط سبع مواقف، الموقف الأول: يُسأل عن الإيمان، والموقف الثاني: يُسأل عن الوضوء والاغتسال، والموقف الثالث: يُسأل عن الصلاة، والرابع: يُسأل عن الصوم، والخامس: يُسأل عن الحج، والسادس: يُسأل عن الزكاة، والموقف السابع : يُسأل عن بِرِّ الوَالدَيْن.
If it is said: Where is the account and the scale? We say: The scale and the account are upon the Sirat. So the good deeds and evil deeds of each person are weighed. Whoever's scales are heavy proceeds to Paradise, and whoever is among the people of wretchedness falls into the Fire, because of what is related from the Messenger of Allah that he said: 'Some of my nation fall into the Fire like rain.' And in the report: 'The servant is stopped on the Sirat at seven stations. The first station: he is asked about faith. The second station: he is asked about ablution and ritual washing. The third station: he is asked about prayer. The fourth: he is asked about fasting. The fifth: he is asked about pilgrimage. The sixth: he is asked about zakat. The seventh station: he is asked about kindness to parents.'
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is another objection-and-answer unit. The objector asks about the location (أين) of the account (حساب) and the scale (ميزان). The answer states both occur on the Sirat (الصِّراط) – the bridge over Hell. On that bridge, each person's good and bad deeds are weighed (تُوزن). Those with heavy scales go to Paradise; those with light scales fall into Hell. This is supported by a hadith: 'Some of my nation fall into the Fire like rain.' Then a longer tradition (وفي الخبر) enumerates seven stations (سبع مواقف) on the Sirat where the servant is questioned. Each station asks about a specific religious duty: faith, ablution and washing (probably referring to ritual purity), prayer, fasting, pilgrimage, zakat, and kindness to parents. This emphasizes that salvation depends not just on belief but also on fulfilling practical obligations and moral duties.

The Plural 'Mawazin' Referring to a Single Scale
Nasafi explains that the plural 'mawazin' can refer to a single scale per person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran uses the plural 'mawazin' for the scales and how it is a valid linguistic usage meaning a single scale per person.

Core Idea
In Arabic, the plural can mean the singular, as with 'mawazin'.

This lesson addresses a common question about the weighing scales in the afterlife. The Quran uses the plural 'mawazin', but does that mean multiple scales? Imam Nasafi clarifies that each person has one scale, and the plural is a linguistic usage found elsewhere in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow of the question and response.
Notice the structure: objection then answer.
2
Understand the literal meaning
The first part of the answer states that each person has a separate scale for weighing their deeds.
This is a direct explanation: no multiple scales per person.
3
Learn the linguistic rule
The second part explains that in Arabic, the plural can be used to mean the singular, supported by Quranic examples.
Examples: 'angels' meaning Jibril, 'messengers' meaning Muhammad.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this linguistic flexibility resolves apparent contradictions and preserves the intended meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : ذكر الموازين بلفظ الجمع كيف يكون هذا؟
قلنا : لكلّ إنسان ميزان على حِدَة، فتوزن حسناته وسيئاته. ولأن الجمع يذكر ويراد به الواحد كما في قصة زكريا ) فَنَادَتْهُ الْمَلَيكَةُ وَهُوَ قَاهُم يُصَلِّي فِي الْمِحْرَابِ ) [آل عمران: ٣٩] والمراد من الملائكة جبريل عليه السلام، وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿يَاتها الرُّسُلُ كُلُوا مِنَ الطَّيِّبَتِ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ٥١] والمراد به محمدا صلى الله عليه وسلم وحده.
If it is said: 'The scales' (al-mawazin) is mentioned in the plural form — how is this? We say: For each person there is a separate scale; his good deeds and bad deeds are weighed. And because the plural is mentioned and the singular is intended, as in the story of Zakariyya: 'Then the angels called him while he was standing praying in the niche' [Al 'Imran: 39] and the intended meaning from 'angels' is Jibril (peace be upon him). Similarly, His statement, the Exalted: 'O messengers, eat from the good things' [al-Mu'minun: 51] and the intended meaning is Muhammad (peace be upon him) alone.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer that addresses a linguistic issue. The Quran uses the plural 'mawazin' (موازين) when referring to the scales of judgment. The objector asks: why the plural? Does each person have multiple scales? The answer has two parts. First, the literal fact: each person has one individual scale (ميزان على حِدَة) on which his deeds are weighed. Second, a grammatical explanation: in Arabic, the plural form is sometimes used to mean the singular (الجمع يذكر ويراد به الواحد). The author gives two Quranic proofs. In the story of Zakariyya, the angels are mentioned in plural but only Jibril is meant. In Surat al-Mu'minun 51, 'O messengers' is plural but addressed only to Prophet Muhammad. Thus, 'mawazin' being plural does not imply multiple scales per person; rather, each person has one scale.

Key Terms
موازين
جمع
واحد
ملائكة
رسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The plural 'mawazin' implies that each person has multiple scales.
Correction: The plural is a linguistic usage; each person has exactly one scale.

Checkpoint
Why is the plural 'al-mawazin' used for the scales in the Quran?
A) Because each person has multiple scales
B) Because the plural is sometimes used to mean the singular in Arabic
C) Because it refers to scales of different nations
D) Because it is a grammatical error

Key Takeaway
The plural 'mawazin' in the Quran refers to a single scale per person, as Arabic allows the plural to indicate the singular.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
