The Plural 'Balances' Explained
Author answers objection about plural 'balances' with Quranic examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran uses the plural 'balances' (موازين) and how it is justified through Quranic examples of plural used to mean singular.

Core Idea
The plural 'balances' refers to individual balances for each person.

This passage addresses a subtle point of Quranic interpretation: why the word 'balances' appears in the plural when each person has only one scale. The author provides a clear answer using examples from the Quran itself, showing that the plural can refer to a singular entity.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Begin by reading the objection about the plural form and the author's direct answer. Notice the structure: 'If it is said... We say...'
The objection is a common question about Quranic wording.
2
Examine the two Quranic examples
The author cites two verses: the angels calling Zakariyya, and the address to all messengers. Understand how each example shows plural referring to a single individual.
In the first example, 'angels' means Jibril alone; in the second, 'messengers' means Muhammad alone.
3
Apply the principle to 'balances'
Connect the examples to the original question: just as plural can mean singular in those verses, 'balances' (plural) can refer to each person's individual balance.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : ذكر الموازين بلفظ الجمع كيف يكون هذا؟ قلنا : لكلّ إنسان ميزان على حِدَة، فتوزن حسناته وسيئاته. ولأن الجمع يذكر ويراد به الواحد كما في قصة زكريا فَنَادَتْهُ الْمَلَائِكَةُ وَهُوَ قَائِمٌ يُصَلِّي فِي الْمِحْرَابِ والمراد من الملائكة جبريل عليه السلام، وكذلك قوله تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا الرُّسُلُ كُلُوا مِنَ الطَّيِّبَاتِ والمراد به محمدا صلى الله عليه وسلم وحده.

And because the plural is used and the singular is intended, as in the story of Zachariah: 'Then the angels called him while he was standing in prayer' and what is meant by the angels is Jibril, peace be upon him, and likewise His statement: 'O messengers, eat from the good things' and what is meant by it is Muhammad, peace be upon him, alone.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The objector questions why the Quran uses the plural 'balances' (موازين) when the weighing seems to be for each person individually. The author answers that each person has their own balance, and the plural can be used to refer to a single entity, as demonstrated by two Quranic examples: (1) the angels calling Zakariyya, where only Jibril is meant, and (2) addressing all messengers, but the address is specifically to the Prophet Muhammad. Thus, 'balances' does not imply multiple balances for one person.

The Servant Is Weighed with His Deeds
Author answers how weighing is done, citing Ibn Mas'ud hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the weighing on the Day of Judgment includes the servant himself along with his deeds, as established by a prophetic hadith.

Core Idea
The servant himself is weighed, not just his deeds.

The objection raised is procedural: how can deeds be weighed? The author answers by presenting a key view: the servant is weighed along with his deeds. This is supported by a powerful hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) declared Ibn Mas'ud's thin legs heavier in the balance than the heavens and earth. This lesson unpacks the argument and its implication for our understanding of the scales.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Start by reading the full Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the format: an objection is raised, then answered with a scholarly view and a hadith.
The hadith is the core evidence.
2
Understand the significance of weighing the person
The answer claims the servant is weighed with his deeds. Reflect on why this is significant: it emphasizes that the person's very being—including physical form—is evaluated.
3
Analyze the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
Examine the hadith: the Prophet's remark about Ibn Mas'ud's thin legs being heavier than the heavens and earth. Consider how this anecdote functions as proof that the person is weighed.
The hadith shows a tangible aspect (legs) being weighed.
4
Connect to the broader lesson on samiyyat
This passage belongs to the category of samiyyat (matters known only through revelation). Recognize that the exact mechanism of weighing is known only through transmitted texts, not reason alone.
This reinforces trust in revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : كيف يُوزن؟ قلنا : قال بعضهم: يُوزن العبد مع عمله، لما رُوِيَ عن ابن مسعود رضيَ أنه صعد شجرةً، وكان صغير الساقين، فتبسم أصحاب النبي عليه السلام، فقال النبي : أتعجبون من دقة ساقيه وإنهما لأثقل في الميزان من السموات والأرضين فثبت أن العبد يُوزن مع عمله.
If it is said: How is it weighed? We say: Some have said: The servant is weighed with his deeds, based on what was narrated from Ibn Mas'ud, may God be pleased with him, that he climbed a tree, and he had thin legs, so the companions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, smiled, so the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: Do you marvel at the thinness of his legs? Yet they are heavier in the balance than the heavens and the earth. So it is established that the servant is weighed with his deeds.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This is another objection-and-answer. The objector asks about the mechanism of weighing. The author presents the view that the servant himself is weighed along with his deeds, supporting it with a hadith: when the companions smiled at Ibn Mas'ud's thin legs while climbing a tree, the Prophet stated that those legs are heavier in the balance than the heavens and earth. This indicates that the person (or his body parts) can be weighed, establishing that the servant is weighed together with his deeds.

ميزان
ساق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Some think that only deeds are weighed, not the person.
Correction: The hadith shows that Ibn Mas'ud's legs (a part of his person) are weighed, establishing that the servant himself is weighed along with his deeds.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Scale of Deeds: Good and Evil in Scrolls
Ibn Abbas describes the writing and weighing of deeds in two scrolls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how good and bad deeds are written and weighed according to the narration of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Good and bad deeds are recorded on scrolls and weighed on a scale.

Ibn Abbas describes a concrete picture of the weighing of deeds. He tells us that each deed is written on a scroll, and the scrolls are placed on opposite pans of the scale. This gives us a tangible understanding of a metaphysical reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage from Ibn Abbas
Read the Arabic and translation of Ibn Abbas' statement.
2
Identify the key elements
Note the scrolls (صحيفة) and the two pans (كفتان).
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask why deeds are written and weighed. This demonstrates divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن ابن عباس رضِيَ الله تعالي عنهما أنه قال: تُكتب الحسناتُ في صحيفة وتوضع في كِفَّةٍ، وتُكتب السيئاتُ في صحيفة، وتوضع في كفة أخري وتوزن. وقال محمد بن علي الترمذي رحمه الله: يُوزن العمل مِنْ غير الرجل، فيرى ذلك كالنور والشمس والقمر، وهذا للمسلم. أما عمل الكافر كظلمة الليل، ثم إن العمل وإن كان عَرَضًا، فالله تعالى قادر على أن يصيّره بحالٍ يُمْكِنُ أَن يُوزَنَ ويُرَى.
And from Ibn Abbas, may God be pleased with them both, that he said: Good deeds are written in a scroll and placed in a pan, and bad deeds are written in a scroll and placed in another pan, and they are weighed. And Muhammad bin Ali al-Tirmidhi, may God have mercy on him, said: The deed is weighed apart from the man, and he sees it like light, the sun, and the moon, and this is for the Muslim. As for the deed of the disbeliever, it is like the darkness of the night. Then, even though the deed is an accident, God Almighty is able to make it in a state in which it can be weighed and seen.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage collects statements from two authorities. Ibn Abbas describes the physical process: good and bad deeds are written on scrolls and placed in opposite pans of the scale to be weighed. Tirmidhi adds that deeds themselves are weighed separately from the person; the Muslim sees his deed as bright as light, sun, or moon, while the disbeliever's deed appears as dark as night. He then addresses a potential objection: deeds are accidents (أعراض) and not physical objects, so how can they be weighed? The answer is that God has the power to transform them into a state where they can be weighed and seen.

Key Terms
صحيفة
كفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abbas, how are deeds presented for weighing?
A) As spoken words
B) As written scrolls in two pans
C) As physical objects like gold and silver
D) As thoughts

Key Takeaway
Ibn Abbas teaches that every good and bad deed is recorded on a scroll and placed on a divine scale for weighing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Every moment of your life is being written—every word, action, and thought. When you imagine that scroll being placed on the scale tomorrow, what deed from today would you most want to add weight to that good pan?
?
If you knew that the scrolls are being filled right now, would you change what you are about to do in the next hour? How can you act on that awareness immediately?
?
The scales will balance justice perfectly. Are there any sins you are neglecting to repent from, thinking they are too small to matter? What will you confess and abandon right now so that your scroll is lighter?

Faith Is Not Weighed Because It Has No Opposite
The sheikh states that faith is not weighed due to lack of opposite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why faith itself is not weighed in the scale, based on the logical argument that it has no coexisting opposite.

Core Idea
Faith cannot be weighed because its opposite, disbelief, cannot coexist within the same person at the same time.

This brief but profound statement from the sheikh addresses a subtle theological point: the weighing of faith. While deeds are weighed, faith itself is not subject to weighing because it lacks an opposite that could be placed in the other pan. The sheikh explains that the opposite of faith is disbelief, and these two cannot exist together in one person at one moment.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original Arabic carefully. Note the key terms: إيمان, ضد, كفر.
2
Understand the argument
The sheikh argues that weighing requires two opposing substances. Since faith's opposite is disbelief and they cannot coexist, faith cannot be placed in a scale.
3
Connect to broader theology
This clarifies that the weighing in the afterlife applies to deeds, not to the essence of faith itself. Reflect on why this distinction matters.
4
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you grasp the reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الشيخ الإمام المفسر رحمه الله: إن إيمان العبد لا يوزن؛ لأنه ليس له ضد يوضع في كفة أخرى؛ لأنَّ ضده الكفر، والإنسان الواحد لا يكون فيه الإيمان والكفر في زمان واحد.
And the sheikh, the imam, the exegete, may God have mercy on him, said: Indeed, the faith of the servant is not weighed because it has no opposite to be placed in the other pan, for its opposite is disbelief, and a single person cannot have faith and disbelief at the same time.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This is a standalone statement from a scholarly authority (likely the author or a teacher). The argument is that faith cannot be weighed in the balance because weighing requires two opposing substances in the two pans. The opposite of faith is disbelief, yet faith and disbelief cannot coexist in a single person at the same time. Therefore, faith itself is not weighed; rather, deeds are weighed. This distinguishes between the weighing of faith and the weighing of actions.

Key Terms
إيمان
ضد
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that faith is weighed along with deeds.
Correction: This passage clarifies that faith itself is not weighed because it lacks a coexisting opposite; only deeds are weighed.

Checkpoint

A) Faith is too light to weigh.
B) Faith has no opposite that can be placed in the other pan.
C) Faith is not an accident.
D) Faith is immeasurable.

Key Takeaway
Faith itself is not weighed in the scale because its opposite, disbelief, cannot coexist in the same person at the same time, making weighing impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson reveals that faith and disbelief cannot be present in the same heart at the same moment. Look back at your day—were there any moments when you felt both attraction to obedience and hesitation? If faith is whole, what does that hesitation reveal? What will you do to root it out before tomorrow?
?
If faith cannot be weighed, then you cannot quantify it by your deeds. Have you been treating your prayers or charity as a measure of your iman? What would change in your worship if you stopped trying to 'earn' more faith and instead focused on purifying your heart of its opposite?
?
The sheikh's argument hinges on the impossibility of coexistence. Consider an attachment to this world—wealth, status, or a relationship—that competes for your loyalty. Is it possible that this attachment is a shade of disbelief? Will you examine one such attachment today and ask Allah to remove its hold on your heart?

Faith Is Not Weighed: The Rationale
The author concludes the discussion on weighing deeds and states why faith is not weighed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why faith is not weighed on the Day of Judgment, based on its unique relation to disbelief.

Core Idea
Faith is not weighed because it has no opposite to place in the other scale.

In this passage, the author concludes a discussion about the weighing of deeds by addressing a key question: is faith itself weighed? Drawing on scriptural references and scholarly opinions, he explains that while deeds are weighed and become visible, faith is not subject to the same weighing process. This lesson unpacks the reason: faith's opposite is disbelief, but a person cannot hold both at once, so no counterweight exists.

Guided Path
1
Read the complete passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the full argument. Notice how the author moves from an example about limbs to the conclusion about faith.
Pay special attention to the final sentence where the author gives his reasoning.
2
Identify the key points in the author's argument
List the claims: (1) deeds are weighed and become visible, (2) even accidents can be made weighable by Allah, (3) faith is not weighed because it has no opposite.
3
Understand the rationale for faith not being weighed
The author argues that weighing requires two opposite things in the two pans. Faith's opposite is disbelief, but a person cannot have both simultaneously. Therefore faith cannot be weighed.
This is a theological point unique to faith compared to other deeds.
4
Test your understanding with the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to confirm you grasped why faith is not weighed, and read the feedback to solidify the concept.
The answer is directly from the author's statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أتعجبون من دقة ساقيه وإنهما لأثقل في الميزان من السموات والأرضين فثبت أن العبد يُوزن مع عمله. وعن ابن عباس رضِيَ الله تعالي عنهما أنه قال: «تُكتب الحسناتُ في صحيفة وتوضع في كِفَّةٍ، وتُكتب السيئاتُ في صحيفة، وتوضع في كفة أخري [وتوزن]. وقال محمد بن علي الترمذي رحمه الله: «يُوزن العمل مِنْ غير الرجل، فيرى ذلك كالنور والشمس والقمر، وهذا للمسلم. أما عمل الكافر كظلمة الليل، ثم إن العمل وإن كان عَرَضًا، فالله تعالى قادر على أن يصيّره بحالٍ يُمْكِنُ أَن يُوزَنَ ويُرَى». وقال الشيخ الإمام المفسر رحمه الله: «إن إيمان العبد لا يوزن؛ لأنه ليس له ضد يوضع في كفة أخرى؛ لأنَّ ضده الكفر، والإنسان الواحد لا يكون فيه الإيمان والكفر في زمان واحد.
Do you marvel at the thinness of his shanks? Verily they are heavier in the balance than the heavens and the earths. So it is established that the servant is weighed with his deed. And from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, that he said: 'The good deeds are written in a scroll and placed in one pan, and the evil deeds are written in a scroll and placed in another pan, and then they are weighed.' And Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tirmidhi, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'The deed is weighed separately from the man, and he sees it like light, the sun, and the moon. This is for the Muslim. As for the deed of the disbeliever, it is like the darkness of the night. Then, even though the deed is an accident (عَرَض), Allah is able to make it into a state in which it can be weighed and seen.' And the Shaykh al-Imam al-Mufassir, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'The faith of the servant is not weighed, because it has no opposite to place in the other pan; for its opposite is disbelief, and a single person cannot have both faith and disbelief in one time.'
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage concludes a discussion about the weighing of deeds on the Day of Judgment. It begins with a hadith showing that the limbs (sāqayn) are weighed. Then it quotes Ibn Abbas describing the weighing process: deeds are written and placed in scales. Al-Tirmidhi explains that the deed itself becomes visible and weighty, even though it is an accident (عَرَض). The author then adds that faith is not weighed because it has no opposite — disbelief is its opposite, but a person cannot have both simultaneously. So the scale of faith is not balanced against an opposing weight. Note that the author's statement about faith not being weighed is a point of doctrine.

Key Terms
ميزان
إيمان
عمل
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think faith is weighed like other deeds on the Day of Judgment.
Correction: The author clarifies that faith is not weighed because it has no opposite; disbelief cannot coexist with faith in a person at the same time, so there is nothing to balance against.

Checkpoint
Why is faith not weighed according to the author?
A) Because it is too light.
B) Because it has no opposite to place in the other scale.
C) Because it is an accident (عَرَض).
D) Because it is only for the Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Faith is not weighed on the Day of Judgment because it has no opposite—disbelief cannot be present in the same person to serve as a counterweight.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If faith is not weighed because it has no opposite in you, then what does that say about the state of your heart right now? Are you living as if your faith is solid, or do you fear that its opposite—disbelief—may be lurking? How does this truth change the way you evaluate your own spiritual state?
?
The deeds of a disbeliever are like darkness, but the deeds of a believer are light. When you consider your own deeds—not just the ones you can see but the hidden ones—do they appear more like light or darkness? What one change can you make today to ensure your deeds shine brighter?
?
The author argues that 'a single person cannot have both faith and disbelief in one time.' This is a comfort, but also a warning. Are there areas in your life where you act as if you can have both—maybe by mixing faith with actions that imply disbelief? What would it look like to purify your intention so that only faith remains?

The Creation and Eternity of Paradise and Hell
The author proves that Paradise and Hell are already created and will never perish.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that Paradise and Hell are already created and eternal, and the rational and scriptural proofs for this belief.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are created now and will never perish.

The author addresses a key theological dispute about the temporal creation of Paradise and Hell. He first presents the objection from the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya, then provides the Sunni response supported by Quranic verses and rational argument. This passage establishes the eternal nature of reward and punishment, which is foundational for Islamic eschatology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Notice the structure: first the opposing view, then the Sunni view with proofs.
2
Identify the opposing view
The Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya argued that Paradise and Hell are not yet created. Why? Understand their two reasons: it is unwise to create before inhabitants, and they would perish with the heavens and earth.
This is typical of kalam: stating the opponent's argument first.
3
Examine the Sunni proofs
The author gives three proofs: 1) The exception in Surah Zumar 68 shows Paradise and Hell survive the trumpet blast; 2) The word 'prepared' (أُعِدَّتْ) in two verses indicates prior creation; 3) A rational argument: knowing reward and punishment exist motivates obedience.
Notice how the author uses both scripture and reason.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
This belief impacts how Muslims view accountability. If Paradise and Hell are already created, they are real and imminent, which should increase sincerity in worship and avoidance of sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في إثبات أن الجنة والنار مخلوقتان الآن. قال بعض المعتزلة والجهمية : إن الله تعالى لم يخلق الجنة والنار بعد؛ لأنه لا يحسن من حكمة الحكيم أن يخلق دار النعمة قبل أن يخلق أهلها، ويخلق السجن والحبس قبل أن يخلق أهلهما؛ لأنهما لو كانتا مخلوقتين لكانتا تفنيان بفناء السموات والأرض، لأنهما كانتا في السماء والأرض وتفنى السموات والأرض، فكذلك الجنة والنار. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة : إن الله تعالى خلق الجنة والنار، ولا تفنيان أبدًا لأنهما ثواب وعقاب، والثواب والعقاب لا يفنيان، لأن الله تعالى استثناهما بقوله: (وَنُفِخَ فِي الصُّورِ فَصَعِقَ مَن فِي السَّمَوَاتِ وَمَن فِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا مَن شَاءَ اللَّهُ ثُمَّ نُفِخَ فِيهِ أُخْرَىٰ فَإِذَا هُمْ قِيَامُ يَنظُرُونَ) [الزمر: 68] يعني الجنة والنار وأهلهما من ملائكة العذاب والحور العين. يدل عليه أن الإنسان إذا خُلق ثوابه يكون أحرص على العبادة، وإذا خُلق عقوبته يكون أخوف وأكثر امتناعاً عن المعاصي. ويدل عليه قوله تعالى: (وَسَارِعُوا إِلَى مَغْفِرَةٍ مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ وَجَنَّةٍ عَرْضُهَا السَّمَوَاتُ وَالْأَرْضُ أُعِدَّتْ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ) [آل عمران: 133] وقوله تعالى: (فَاتَّقُوا النَّارَ الَّتِي وَقُودُهَا النَّاسُ وَالْحِجَارَةُ أُعِدَّتْ لِلْكَفِرِينَ) [البقرة: 24] فلو كانتا غير مخلوقتين، لكان ذلك منه كذبًا، والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك، ويدل عليه أن الله تعالى خلق الجنة فوق سبع سموات
Section on proving that Paradise and Hell are created now. Some Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya said: Allah has not created Paradise and Hell yet, because it is not befitting the wisdom of the Wise to create the abode of bliss before creating its inhabitants, and to create the prison and confinement before creating its inhabitants; because if they were created, they would perish with the perishing of the heavens and the earth, since they were in the heavens and the earth and the heavens and the earth perish, so likewise Paradise and Hell. And the People of the Sunnah and the Community said: Allah created Paradise and Hell, and they will never perish because they are reward and punishment, and reward and punishment do not perish, because Allah excluded them in His saying: 'And the Trumpet will be blown, and whoever is in the heavens and whoever is in the earth will be stunned except whom Allah wills. Then it will be blown another time, and at once they will be standing looking on.' [Zumar 68] meaning Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants from the angels of punishment and the houris. It indicates that if a person's reward is created, he will be more eager for worship, and if his punishment is created, he will be more fearful and more restrained from sins. And it is indicated by His saying: 'And hasten to forgiveness from your Lord and a Paradise whose width is the heavens and the earth, prepared for the righteous.' [Aal Imran 133] and His saying: 'Then fear the Fire whose fuel is people and stones, prepared for the disbelievers.' [Baqarah 24] So if they were not created, that would be a lie from Him, and Allah is exalted above that. And it is indicated that Allah created Paradise above the seven heavens.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a kalam argument about the present existence and permanence of Paradise and Hell. The author first presents the opposing view: some Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya argue that Allah has not yet created Paradise and Hell because it would be unwise to create them before inhabitants, and they would be destroyed with the heavens and earth. Then the author gives the Sunni position: Paradise and Hell are created and eternal. The proof includes Quranic verses: the exception in Surah Zumar 68 shows that Paradise and Hell survive the trumpet blast; and the use of 'prepared' (أُعِدَّتْ) in Surah Aal Imran 133 and Baqarah 24 indicates they were created in advance. The author also adds a rational argument: knowing reward and punishment are already created motivates obedience and deters sin.

جنة
نار
خلق
ثواب
عقاب
أبد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Paradise and Hell will be destroyed at the end of time.
Correction: They are permanent and never perish because they are reward and punishment, as proven by Quranic verses and rational argument.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument of the Mu'tazila against the creation of Paradise and Hell?
A) They are too great to be created.
B) It is unwise to create them before inhabitants.
C) They are only spiritual.
D) The Quran does not mention them.

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell are already created and will never perish, as they are reward and punishment; this is established by reason and revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Paradise and Hell are already created and waiting for you, what sin would you abandon today—starting right now—because Hell is already prepared?
?
Knowing that your reward is already created and ready, what one act of worship will you commit to doing consistently from today, not out of fear but out of hope and love?
?
Does your daily life reflect the reality that Paradise and Hell exist now, or do you live as if they are distant? What would change if you woke up tomorrow in either place? Decide one tangible change you will make today.

The Objection and Rational Foundation for the Creation of Paradise and Hell
Nasafi presents the Mu'tazila/Jahmiyya objection and Sunni rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila/Jahmiyya objection to the creation of Paradise and Hell before the Day of Judgment and the Sunni rational response based on the nature of reward and punishment.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell exist now because reward and punishment cannot be temporary.

This lesson presents a key theological debate about the timing of Paradise and Hell's creation. The Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya argue that it would be unwise for Allah to create them before their inhabitants, while the Sunni response affirms their existence based on rational arguments about the perpetuity of reward and punishment. We will examine the objection and the first part of the Sunni proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first paragraph where the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya present their argument. Note their reasoning: it is not wise to create reward/punishment before the people, and if created, they would perish with the heavens.
They assume Paradise and Hell are located within the heavens/earth.
2
Identify the Sunni response's starting premise
The Sunni response begins by asserting that Paradise and Hell are created and never perish. Why? Because they are reward and punishment, which are eternal. Find the key statement.
The author cites the verse of Az-Zumar as evidence that Paradise and Hell are exempt from annihilation.
3
Understand the rational argument
The author then gives a rational argument: knowing that one's reward exists now motivates worship, and knowing punishment exists now deters sin. Reflect on how this counters the objection.
This argument shows that advance creation is beneficial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال بعض المعتزلة والجهمية : إن الله تعالى لم يخلق الجنة والنار بعد؛ لأنه لا يحسن من حكمة الحكيم أن يخلق دار النعمة قبل أن يخلق أهلها، ويخلق السجن والحبس قبل أن يخلق أهلهما؛ لأنهما لو كانتا مخلوقتين لكانتا تفنيان بفناء السموات والأرض، لأنهما كانتا في السماء والأرض وتفنى السموات والأرض، فكذلك الجنة والنار.
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة : إن الله تعالى خلق الجنة والنار، ولا تفنيان أبدًا لأنهما ثواب وعقاب، والثواب والعقاب لا يفنيان، لأن الله تعالى استثناهما بقوله: ﴿وَنُفِخَ فِي الصُّورِ فَصَعِقَ مَن فِي السَّمَوَاتِ وَمَن فِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا مَن شَاءَ اللَّهُ ثُمَّ نُفِخَ فِيهِ أُخْرَىٰ فَإِذَا هُمْ قِيَامُ يَنظُرُونَ ﴾ [الزمر: ٦٨] يعني الجنة والنار وأهلهما من ملائكة العذاب والحور العين. يدل عليه أن الإنسان إذا خُلق ثوابه يكون أحرص على العبادة، وإذا خُلق عقوبته يكون أخوف وأكثر امتناعاً عن المعاصي.
ويدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَسَارِعُوا إِلَى مَغْفِرَةٍ مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ وَجَنَّةٍ عَرْضُهَا السَّمَوَاتُ وَالْأَرْضُ أُعِدَّتْ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٣٣] وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاتَّقُوا النَّارَ الَّتِي وَقُودُهَا النَّاسُ وَالْحِجَارَةُ أُعِدَّتْ لِلْكَفِرِينَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤] فلو كانتا غير مخلوقتين، لكان ذلك منه كذبًا، والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك، ويدل عليه أن الله تعالى خلق الجنة فوق سبع سموات لا في السَّموات فلا يقال بأنهما يفنيان بفناء السموات والأرض، وكيف يقال بأنها في السموات وهي ألف ألف مرةً مثل السموات.
قال الله تعالى: عِندَ سِدْرَةِ الْمُنتَهَى عِندَهَا جَنَّةُ الْمَأْوَى ﴾ [النجم: ١٤-١٥] والسدرة فوق السَّماء السابعة، وكذلك جهنم تحت الأرض السابعة.
قال الله تعالى: ﴿كَلَّا إِنَّ كِتَبَ الْفُجَارِ لَفِي سِعِينِ ﴾ [المطففين: ٧) كَلَّا إِنَّ كتَبَ الْأَبْرَارِ لَفِي عِلَينَ ﴾ [المطففين: ۱۸] والسجين تحت الأرضين السبع، وأرواح الكفار يُذهب بها إلى سجين، وأرواح المؤمنين والشهداء يُذهب بها إلى عليين.
والدليل على أن الجنة والنار خلقتا للجزاء ما رُوِيَ عن النبي عليه الصلاة السلام أنه قال: رأيت ليلة المعراج في الجنة كذا وفي النار كذا الحديث إلى آخره.
Some of the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya said: Verily, Allah Most High has not created Paradise and Hell yet; because it is not befitting from the wisdom of the Wise to create the abode of blessing before creating its inhabitants, and to create the prison and confinement before creating their inhabitants; because if they were created, they would perish with the perishing of the heavens and the earth, since they were in the sky and the earth, and the heavens and earth perish, and likewise Paradise and Hell. And Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said: Verily, Allah Most High created Paradise and Hell, and they never perish ever, because they are reward and punishment, and reward and punishment do not perish, because Allah Most High excepted them by His saying: {And the Trumpet will be blown, and whoever is in the heavens and whoever is on the earth will swoon, except whom Allah wills. Then it will be blown again, and at once they will be standing, looking on} [Az-Zumar: 68] meaning Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants from the angels of punishment and the houris. It indicates that if a person's reward is created, he is more eager for worship, and if his punishment is created, he is more fearful and more refrainant from sins. And it is indicated by His saying Most High: {And hasten to forgiveness from your Lord and a Paradise whose width is the heavens and the earth, prepared for the righteous} [Aal-Imran: 133] and His saying Most High: {Then fear the Fire whose fuel is people and stones, prepared for the disbelievers} [Al-Baqarah: 24]. If they were not created, that would be from Him a lie, and Allah Most High is exalted above that. And it indicates that Allah Most High created Paradise above seven heavens, not in the heavens, so it cannot be said that they perish with the perishing of the heavens and the earth. And how can it be said that it is in the heavens when it is a thousand thousand times the like of the heavens? Allah Most High said: {At the Lote Tree of the Utmost Boundary, near it is the Garden of Refuge} [An-Najm: 14-15] and the Lote Tree is above the seventh heaven, and likewise Hell is beneath the seventh earth. Allah Most High said: {No! Indeed, the record of the wicked is in Sijjin} [Al-Mutaffifin: 7] {No! Indeed, the record of the righteous is in Illiyin} [Al-Mutaffifin: 18] and Sijjin is beneath the seven earths, and the souls of the disbelievers are taken to Sijjin, and the souls of the believers and martyrs are taken to Illiyin. And the proof that Paradise and Hell were created for recompense is what was narrated from the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, that he said: 'On the night of the Mi'raj, I saw such-and-such in Paradise and such-and-such in Hell' — the hadith to its end.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya position and a proof for the Sunni belief that Paradise and Hell are already created and eternal. The author first presents the objection: the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya argue that it is not wise for Allah to create Paradise and Hell before their inhabitants, because if they were created, they would perish with the heavens and the earth (since they are located within them). Then the Sunni response begins: Ahl al-Sunna affirm that Allah has created both, and they will never perish because they are reward and punishment, which are perpetual. The author supports this with several arguments. First, he cites the Qur'anic verse (Az-Zumar 68) which exempts some from the swooning at the Trumpet blast; he interprets the exempted as Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants (angels of punishment and houris). Second, he argues that creating reward and punishment in advance increases motivation for good and fear of sin. Third, he quotes verses (Aal-Imran 133 and Al-Baqarah 24) that describe Paradise and Hell as 'prepared' (أُعِدَّتْ), implying they already exist; if they were not created, the divine word would be false, which is impossible. Fourth, he addresses the location issue: Paradise is above the seven heavens, not inside them, so it does not perish with them; its size is immense, far larger than the heavens. He supports this with the verse about the Lote Tree and the Garden of Refuge (An-Najm 14-15) and the verses about Sijjin and Illiyin (Al-Mutaffifin 7, 18), showing the locations. Finally, he cites the hadith of the Mi'raj in which the Prophet saw Paradise and Hell firsthand, confirming their existence. The author thus systematically refutes the objection and establishes the Sunni doctrine.

Key Terms
الجنة
النار
مخلوقتان
ثواب
عقاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Paradise and Hell have not been created yet because Allah would not create them before their inhabitants and they would perish with the heavens.
Correction: Allah created them now as eternal reward and punishment, and they are located outside the perishable heavens.

Checkpoint
According to the Sunni response, why will Paradise and Hell never perish?
A) Because they are located in the heavens
B) Because they are reward and punishment
C) Because Allah wills
D) Because they are infinite

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position affirms that Paradise and Hell are created now and eternal because they are reward and punishment, and this is rationally beneficial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that Paradise and Hell exist right now, this very moment, what does that demand of you in your next prayer? Will you pray with the urgency of someone who believes the reward is already prepared, or will you remain heedless?
?
The Sunni proof includes that the prior creation of punishment deters sin. Think about a sin you are struggling with. Does the reality that Hell exists now truly deter you? If not, why does your heart not fear as it should, and what will you do to change that starting today?
?
If the Trumpet were blown tonight and you were among those exempted because of your faith, would you be among the inhabitants of Paradise that are already created? What evidence in your daily life proves that you are heading there, and what will you change to be certain?

Scriptural Proofs and the Location of Paradise and Hell
Nasafi cites Qur'anic verses, spatial arguments, and hadith for creation of Paradise and Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural proofs (Qur'an and Hadith) and the spatial argument that Paradise and Hell are created now and located beyond the heavens and earth.

Core Idea
Qur'anic verses prove Paradise and Hell are already prepared, and their location above and below ensures they will not perish.

In this lesson, we continue the Sunni case for the present existence of Paradise and Hell. The author presents multiple Qur'anic verses that describe them as 'prepared,' and a spatial argument showing they are located outside the perishable heavens and earth. Finally, he cites the Prophet's hadith of the Mi'raj as direct eyewitness testimony.

Guided Path
1
Examine the 'prepared' verses
Read the verses from Aal-Imran and Al-Baqarah that use the word 'prepared' (أُعِدَّتْ). Note the argument: if they were not already created, Allah would be lying, which is impossible.
2
Understand the spatial argument
The author argues that Paradise is above the seven heavens, not inside them, so it does not perish with them. He quotes verses about Sidrat al-Muntaha and Sijjin/Illiyin to show their locations.
This directly refutes the objection that they would perish if located in the heavens.
3
Consider the hadith of Mi'raj
The Prophet's night journey is presented as proof that Paradise and Hell exist now, as he saw them. This is a conclusive evidence from revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال بعض المعتزلة والجهمية : إن الله تعالى لم يخلق الجنة والنار بعد؛ لأنه لا يحسن من حكمة الحكيم أن يخلق دار النعمة قبل أن يخلق أهلها، ويخلق السجن والحبس قبل أن يخلق أهلهما؛ لأنهما لو كانتا مخلوقتين لكانتا تفنيان بفناء السموات والأرض، لأنهما كانتا في السماء والأرض وتفنى السموات والأرض، فكذلك الجنة والنار.
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة : إن الله تعالى خلق الجنة والنار، ولا تفنيان أبدًا لأنهما ثواب وعقاب، والثواب والعقاب لا يفنيان، لأن الله تعالى استثناهما بقوله: ﴿وَنُفِخَ فِي الصُّورِ فَصَعِقَ مَن فِي السَّمَوَاتِ وَمَن فِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا مَن شَاءَ اللَّهُ ثُمَّ نُفِخَ فِيهِ أُخْرَىٰ فَإِذَا هُمْ قِيَامُ يَنظُرُونَ ﴾ [الزمر: ٦٨] يعني الجنة والنار وأهلهما من ملائكة العذاب والحور العين. يدل عليه أن الإنسان إذا خُلق ثوابه يكون أحرص على العبادة، وإذا خُلق عقوبته يكون أخوف وأكثر امتناعاً عن المعاصي.
ويدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَسَارِعُوا إِلَى مَغْفِرَةٍ مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ وَجَنَّةٍ عَرْضُهَا السَّمَوَاتُ وَالْأَرْضُ أُعِدَّتْ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٣٣] وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاتَّقُوا النَّارَ الَّتِي وَقُودُهَا النَّاسُ وَالْحِجَارَةُ أُعِدَّتْ لِلْكَفِرِينَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤] فلو كانتا غير مخلوقتين، لكان ذلك منه كذبًا، والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك، ويدل عليه أن الله تعالى خلق الجنة فوق سبع سموات لا في السَّموات فلا يقال بأنهما يفنيان بفناء السموات والأرض، وكيف يقال بأنها في السموات وهي ألف ألف مرةً مثل السموات.
قال الله تعالى: عِندَ سِدْرَةِ الْمُنتَهَى عِندَهَا جَنَّةُ الْمَأْوَى ﴾ [النجم: ١٤-١٥] والسدرة فوق السَّماء السابعة، وكذلك جهنم تحت الأرض السابعة.
قال الله تعالى: ﴿كَلَّا إِنَّ كِتَبَ الْفُجَارِ لَفِي سِعِينِ ﴾ [المطففين: ٧) كَلَّا إِنَّ كتَبَ الْأَبْرَارِ لَفِي عِلَينَ ﴾ [المطففين: ۱۸] والسجين تحت الأرضين السبع، وأرواح الكفار يُذهب بها إلى سجين، وأرواح المؤمنين والشهداء يُذهب بها إلى عليين.
والدليل على أن الجنة والنار خلقتا للجزاء ما رُوِيَ عن النبي عليه الصلاة السلام أنه قال: رأيت ليلة المعراج في الجنة كذا وفي النار كذا الحديث إلى آخره.
Some of the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya said: Verily, Allah Most High has not created Paradise and Hell yet; because it is not befitting from the wisdom of the Wise to create the abode of blessing before creating its inhabitants, and to create the prison and confinement before creating their inhabitants; because if they were created, they would perish with the perishing of the heavens and the earth, since they were in the sky and the earth, and the heavens and earth perish, and likewise Paradise and Hell. And Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said: Verily, Allah Most High created Paradise and Hell, and they never perish ever, because they are reward and punishment, and reward and punishment do not perish, because Allah Most High excepted them by His saying: {And the Trumpet will be blown, and whoever is in the heavens and whoever is on the earth will swoon, except whom Allah wills. Then it will be blown again, and at once they will be standing, looking on} [Az-Zumar: 68] meaning Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants from the angels of punishment and the houris. It indicates that if a person's reward is created, he is more eager for worship, and if his punishment is created, he is more fearful and more refrainant from sins. And it is indicated by His saying Most High: {And hasten to forgiveness from your Lord and a Paradise whose width is the heavens and the earth, prepared for the righteous} [Aal-Imran: 133] and His saying Most High: {Then fear the Fire whose fuel is people and stones, prepared for the disbelievers} [Al-Baqarah: 24]. If they were not created, that would be from Him a lie, and Allah Most High is exalted above that. And it indicates that Allah Most High created Paradise above seven heavens, not in the heavens, so it cannot be said that they perish with the perishing of the heavens and the earth. And how can it be said that it is in the heavens when it is a thousand thousand times the like of the heavens? Allah Most High said: {At the Lote Tree of the Utmost Boundary, near it is the Garden of Refuge} [An-Najm: 14-15] and the Lote Tree is above the seventh heaven, and likewise Hell is beneath the seventh earth. Allah Most High said: {No! Indeed, the record of the wicked is in Sijjin} [Al-Mutaffifin: 7] {No! Indeed, the record of the righteous is in Illiyin} [Al-Mutaffifin: 18] and Sijjin is beneath the seven earths, and the souls of the disbelievers are taken to Sijjin, and the souls of the believers and martyrs are taken to Illiyin. And the proof that Paradise and Hell were created for recompense is what was narrated from the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, that he said: 'On the night of the Mi'raj, I saw such-and-such in Paradise and such-and-such in Hell' — the hadith to its end.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya position and a proof for the Sunni belief that Paradise and Hell are already created and eternal. The author first presents the objection: the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya argue that it is not wise for Allah to create Paradise and Hell before their inhabitants, because if they were created, they would perish with the heavens and the earth (since they are located within them). Then the Sunni response begins: Ahl al-Sunna affirm that Allah has created both, and they will never perish because they are reward and punishment, which are perpetual. The author supports this with several arguments. First, he cites the Qur'anic verse (Az-Zumar 68) which exempts some from the swooning at the Trumpet blast; he interprets the exempted as Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants (angels of punishment and houris). Second, he argues that creating reward and punishment in advance increases motivation for good and fear of sin. Third, he quotes verses (Aal-Imran 133 and Al-Baqarah 24) that describe Paradise and Hell as 'prepared' (أُعِدَّتْ), implying they already exist; if they were not created, the divine word would be false, which is impossible. Fourth, he addresses the location issue: Paradise is above the seven heavens, not inside them, so it does not perish with them; its size is immense, far larger than the heavens. He supports this with the verse about the Lote Tree and the Garden of Refuge (An-Najm 14-15) and the verses about Sijjin and Illiyin (Al-Mutaffifin 7, 18), showing the locations. Finally, he cites the hadith of the Mi'raj in which the Prophet saw Paradise and Hell firsthand, confirming their existence. The author thus systematically refutes the objection and establishes the Sunni doctrine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verses describing Paradise as 'prepared' are figurative and do not imply present existence.
Correction: The word 'prepared' indicates actual existence; otherwise Allah would be lying.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue would happen if Paradise and Hell were not created, given the verses that say they are 'prepared'?
A) It would be a lie from Allah
B) It would be a metaphor
C) It would be impossible
D) It would be wise

Key Takeaway
Qur'anic verses and the Prophet's Mi'raj confirm that Paradise and Hell exist now, located beyond the perishable universe.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Paradise is already prepared and waiting for you, what would you change about how you spend your time today?
?
The Prophet saw Hell on the night of Mi'raj. If that scene were shown to you right now, what habit or sin would you immediately abandon?
?
Your soul, at this moment, is recorded either in Illiyin or Sijjin. What is one concrete action you can take before the end of this day to ensure your name is among the righteous?

Paradise and Hell: Created and Located
Nasafi states the locations of Paradise and Hell and gives a proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence from Quran and hadith that Paradise and Hell are already created and their specific locations beyond the heavens and earth.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are created now, located beyond the heavens and earth.

This passage addresses two key questions: Are Paradise and Hell already created? And where are they? Nasafi refutes the idea that they are in the heavens, citing Quranic verses and a hadith from the Night Journey to establish both their existence and their locations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the flow: refutation → Quranic evidence → hadith proof.
2
Identify the refutation
The passage begins by denying that Paradise and Hell are located in the heavens. Why? Because they are far larger and would not perish with them.
This answers a potential objection that they are temporary.
3
Note the Quranic locations
Find the two Quranic proofs: Paradise is at the Lote Tree above the seventh heaven; Hell is beneath the seventh earth, with Sijjeen and 'Illiyoon as destinations for souls.
These verses are from Surah An-Najm and Al-Mutaffifin.
4
Recognize the hadith proof
The Prophet's report of seeing Paradise and Hell on the Night Journey proves they are already created and exist for recompense.
This directly refutes the idea that they will be created later.
5
Reflect on the misconception
Many think Paradise and Hell are not yet created. This passage shows they exist now, as the Prophet saw them.
The Quranic locations and the hadith together confirm this.

Source Text

لا في السَّموات فلا يقال بأنهما يفنيان بفناء السموات والأرض، وكيف يقال بأنها في السموات وهي ألف ألف مرةً مثل السموات.
قال الله تعالى: عِندَ سِدْرَةِ الْمُنتَهَى عِندَهَا جَنَّةُ الْمَأْوَى ﴾ [النجم: ١٤-١٥] والسدرة فوق السَّماء السابعة، وكذلك جهنم تحت الأرض السابعة.
قال الله تعالى: ﴿كَلَّا إِنَّ كِتَبَ الْفُجَارِ لَفِي سِعِينِ ﴾ [المطففين: ٧) كَلَّا إِنَّ كتَبَ الْأَبْرَارِ لَفِي عِلَينَ ﴾ [المطففين: ۱۸] والسجين تحت الأرضين السبع، وأرواح الكفار يُذهب بها إلى سجين، وأرواح المؤمنين والشهداء يُذهب بها إلى عليين.
والدليل على أن الجنة والنار خلقتا للجزاء ما رُوِيَ عن النبي عليه الصلاة السلام أنه قال: رأيت ليلة المعراج في الجنة كذا وفي النار كذا» (۱) الحديث إلى آخره.
Not in the heavens, so it cannot be said that they (Paradise and Hell) perish with the perishing of the heavens and the earth. And how can it be said that they are in the heavens while they are a thousand thousand times like the heavens? Allah said: 'At the Lote Tree of the Utmost Boundary, near it is the Garden of Refuge' [53:14-15]. And the Lote Tree is above the seventh heaven, and likewise Hell is beneath the seventh earth. Allah said: 'No indeed! The record of the wicked is in Sijjeen... No indeed! The record of the righteous is in 'Illiyoon' [83:7, 18]. And Sijjeen is beneath the seven earths, and the souls of the disbelievers are taken to Sijjeen, and the souls of the believers and martyrs are taken to 'Illiyoon. And the proof that Paradise and Hell are created for recompense is what was related from the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) that he said: 'I saw on the Night of the Ascension in Paradise such-and-such and in Hell such-and-such.' The hadith to its end.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that Paradise and Hell will perish. It argues that they are not located within the heavens, so they do not perish when the heavens perish, and they are much larger than the heavens. Then it provides Quranic evidence: Paradise is at the Lote Tree of the Utmost Boundary above the seventh heaven, and Hell is beneath the seventh earth. It also cites verses about Sijjeen and 'Illiyoon, explaining that these are places beneath the earths and above, respectively, and that souls are taken there. Finally, it presents a proof from the Prophet's hadith of the Night Journey, where he saw Paradise and Hell, indicating that they are already created and exist now for the purpose of recompense.

?

The Rational Argument Against Punishment of the Grave
Mu'tazila present a rational dilemma to disprove punishment of the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, and Jahmiyya rational argument that punishment in the grave is impossible.

Core Idea
Punishment in the grave is rationally impossible: the body without soul feels nothing, and the soul cannot return for a second death.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi presents the objection raised by several theological schools against the established Sunni belief in punishment of the grave. They use a rational dilemma to argue that the very concept is logically untenable. By following their argument, we see how reason alone might seem to contradict revelation, setting the stage for the Sunni response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Identify the two horns of the dilemma presented by the Mu'tazila.
2
Analyze the first horn
Understand why punishment of flesh without soul is considered false: the body cannot feel pain without the soul.
3
Analyze the second horn
See why punishment after soul re-enters is false: it would require a second death, contradicting Quran 3:185.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [ في إثبات عذاب القبر ]
قالت المعتزلة والنجارية والجهمية : عذاب القبر وسؤال منكر ونكير لا يقبله العقل والقياس، لأنه لو عذَّبه لا يخلو إما أن يُعذِّب اللحم بغير الروح، أو يدخل فيه الرُّوح ثم يعذبه، وباطل أن يعذَّب اللحم بغير الرُّوح؛ لأن اللحم بغير الرُّوح لا يتألم، وباطل أن تدخل فيه الرُّوح ثم يعذَّبه، لأنه لو دخل فيه الروح يحتاج إلى الموت. ثانياً: وهذا لا يجوز؛ لأن الله تعالى قال: كُل نَفْسٍ ذَائِقَةُ الموتِ ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٨٥] أخبر أنهم لا يذوقون فيها الموتَ إِلَّا مرةً واحدة، فإذا بطل القسمان تعيَّن القسم الثالث وهو أن لا يعذَّب في القبر.
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: عذاب القبر حق، وسؤال منكر ونكير حقٌّ، وضيق (۱) القبر سواء كان مؤمناً أو كافراً أو مطيعاً أو فاسقاً، لكن إذا كان كافراً فعذابه يدوم في القبر إلى يوم القيامة، ويرفع عنهم العذاب يوم الجمعة، وشهر رمضان بحرمة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لأنهم ما داموا في الأحياء لا يعذبهم الله تعالى في الدنيا بحرمة النبي ، فكذلك في القبر يرفع عنهم العذاب يوم الجمعة وكل رمضان بحرمته فيعذب اللحم متصلا بالروح والروح متصلاً بالجسد، فيتألم الروح مع الجسد وإن كان خارجاً منه.
ثم المؤمن على وجهين إن كان مطيعا لا يكون له عذاب القبر، ويكون له ضغطته
Chapter [On Establishing the Punishment of the Grave]
The Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, and Jahmiyya said: The punishment of the grave and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir are not accepted by reason and analogy, because if He punishes, it is not free from either that He punishes the flesh without the soul, or that He causes the soul to enter it and then punishes it. It is false that the flesh is punished without the soul, because the flesh without the soul does not feel pain. And it is false that the soul enters it and then punishes it, because if the soul enters it, it would need death a second time. And this is not permissible, because Allah said: 'Every soul will taste death' [3:185]; He informed that they will not taste death therein except once. So when the two possibilities are invalid, the third possibility is determined, which is that He does not punish in the grave.
And Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said: The punishment of the grave is true, and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir is true, and the tightness (squeeze) of the grave is for both the believer and the disbeliever, the obedient and the sinful. But if he is a disbeliever, his punishment continues in the grave until the Day of Resurrection, and the punishment is lifted from them on Friday and the month of Ramadan, due to the sanctity of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Because as long as they are among the living, Allah does not punish them in this world due to the sanctity of the Prophet, so likewise in the grave the punishment is lifted from them on Friday and every Ramadan due to his sanctity. So He punishes the flesh connected to the soul, and the soul connected to the body, so the soul feels pain with the body even though it is outside of it.
Then the believer is of two types: if he is obedient, he has no punishment of the grave, but he has its squeeze.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer argument regarding the punishment of the grave. First, the Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, and Jahmiyya argue rationally that punishment in the grave is impossible. They present a dilemma: either the body is punished without the soul, or the soul re-enters the body and then it is punished. They invalidate the first because a body without a soul cannot feel pain. They invalidate the second because re-entry of the soul would require a second death, contradicting the Quranic verse that each soul tastes death only once. Therefore, they conclude that punishment in the grave does not occur.

Then Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a respond by affirming the reality of the punishment of the grave and the questioning. They explain that the grave is tight for everyone, but for the disbeliever the punishment is continuous until the Day of Judgment, though it is lifted on Fridays and during Ramadan due to the honor of the Prophet. They explain the mechanism: the flesh is connected to the soul, and the soul is connected to the body, so the soul feels pain with the body even though it is outside it. Finally, they distinguish between the believer who is obedient—he has no punishment but does experience a 'squeeze' (ضغطة).

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
منكر ونكير
المعتزلة
النجارية
الجهمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the punishment of the grave must be physical and that the dead body cannot feel pain.
Correction: The Mu'tazila used this very reasoning to deny it, but Ahl al-Sunna affirm that the soul is connected to the body and experiences pain.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse do the Mu'tazila cite to support the impossibility of a second death?
A) 3:185
B) 2:255
C) 36:65
D) 21:35

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila argued that punishment of the grave is rationally impossible by eliminating both the punishment of a soulless body and the re-entry of the soul.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to argue for the punishment of the grave, how would you respond to the Mu'tazila's rational dilemma? Does your faith in the unseen rest on rational proofs or on submission to revelation? What does your answer reveal about your reliance on your own intellect versus divine authority?
?
When you read the Mu'tazila's argument that the body without a soul cannot feel pain, does that shake your belief in the punishment of the grave? Or do you trust that Allah is able to create pain in ways beyond your understanding? Where in your life do you need to submit your reason to revelation?
?
The Mu'tazila used the verse 'Every soul will taste death' to deny a second death. But what if you have to face a trial after death that is not a physical death? Are you prepared for the questioning of Munkar and Nakir? What would you say if they ask you about your Lord, your religion, and your prophet?

The Sunni Doctrine of Punishment of the Grave
Sunna response affirming punishment and explaining its mechanism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni belief in the punishment of the grave, its mechanism, and the special rulings for believers and disbelievers.

Core Idea
The punishment of the grave is real: the soul feels pain through its connection to the body, and it is lifted on Fridays and Ramadan for disbelievers due to the Prophet's sanctity.

After presenting the Mu'tazila objection, Imam Nasafi now states the position of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. He affirms the reality of the punishment and the questioning, explains how the soul and body are involved, and gives details about the lifting of punishment on holy days. This passage provides the orthodox response to the rationalist objection.

Guided Path
1
Affirm the Sunni belief
Read the opening statement that punishment of the grave, questioning, and squeeze are real.
2
Understand the mechanism
Note that the soul is connected to the body, so the soul feels pain even if outside.
3
Distinguish between disbeliever and believer
Punishment is continuous for disbelievers but lifted on Fridays and Ramadan; obedient believers only experience squeeze.
The passage cuts off before completing the believer's case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [ في إثبات عذاب القبر ]
قالت المعتزلة والنجارية والجهمية : عذاب القبر وسؤال منكر ونكير لا يقبله العقل والقياس، لأنه لو عذَّبه لا يخلو إما أن يُعذِّب اللحم بغير الروح، أو يدخل فيه الرُّوح ثم يعذبه، وباطل أن يعذَّب اللحم بغير الرُّوح؛ لأن اللحم بغير الرُّوح لا يتألم، وباطل أن تدخل فيه الرُّوح ثم يعذَّبه، لأنه لو دخل فيه الروح يحتاج إلى الموت. ثانياً: وهذا لا يجوز؛ لأن الله تعالى قال: كُل نَفْسٍ ذَائِقَةُ الموتِ ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٨٥] أخبر أنهم لا يذوقون فيها الموتَ إِلَّا مرةً واحدة، فإذا بطل القسمان تعيَّن القسم الثالث وهو أن لا يعذَّب في القبر.
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: عذاب القبر حق، وسؤال منكر ونكير حقٌّ، وضيق (۱) القبر سواء كان مؤمناً أو كافراً أو مطيعاً أو فاسقاً، لكن إذا كان كافراً فعذابه يدوم في القبر إلى يوم القيامة، ويرفع عنهم العذاب يوم الجمعة، وشهر رمضان بحرمة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لأنهم ما داموا في الأحياء لا يعذبهم الله تعالى في الدنيا بحرمة النبي ، فكذلك في القبر يرفع عنهم العذاب يوم الجمعة وكل رمضان بحرمته فيعذب اللحم متصلا بالروح والروح متصلاً بالجسد، فيتألم الروح مع الجسد وإن كان خارجاً منه.
ثم المؤمن على وجهين إن كان مطيعا لا يكون له عذاب القبر، ويكون له ضغطته
Chapter [On Establishing the Punishment of the Grave]
The Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, and Jahmiyya said: The punishment of the grave and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir are not accepted by reason and analogy, because if He punishes, it is not free from either that He punishes the flesh without the soul, or that He causes the soul to enter it and then punishes it. It is false that the flesh is punished without the soul, because the flesh without the soul does not feel pain. And it is false that the soul enters it and then punishes it, because if the soul enters it, it would need death a second time. And this is not permissible, because Allah said: 'Every soul will taste death' [3:185]; He informed that they will not taste death therein except once. So when the two possibilities are invalid, the third possibility is determined, which is that He does not punish in the grave.
And Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said: The punishment of the grave is true, and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir is true, and the tightness (squeeze) of the grave is for both the believer and the disbeliever, the obedient and the sinful. But if he is a disbeliever, his punishment continues in the grave until the Day of Resurrection, and the punishment is lifted from them on Friday and the month of Ramadan, due to the sanctity of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Because as long as they are among the living, Allah does not punish them in this world due to the sanctity of the Prophet, so likewise in the grave the punishment is lifted from them on Friday and every Ramadan due to his sanctity. So He punishes the flesh connected to the soul, and the soul connected to the body, so the soul feels pain with the body even though it is outside of it.
Then the believer is of two types: if he is obedient, he has no punishment of the grave, but he has its squeeze.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer argument regarding the punishment of the grave. First, the Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, and Jahmiyya argue rationally that punishment in the grave is impossible. They present a dilemma: either the body is punished without the soul, or the soul re-enters the body and then it is punished. They invalidate the first because a body without a soul cannot feel pain. They invalidate the second because re-entry of the soul would require a second death, contradicting the Quranic verse that each soul tastes death only once. Therefore, they conclude that punishment in the grave does not occur.

Then Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a respond by affirming the reality of the punishment of the grave and the questioning. They explain that the grave is tight for everyone, but for the disbeliever the punishment is continuous until the Day of Judgment, though it is lifted on Fridays and during Ramadan due to the honor of the Prophet. They explain the mechanism: the flesh is connected to the soul, and the soul is connected to the body, so the soul feels pain with the body even though it is outside it. Finally, they distinguish between the believer who is obedient—he has no punishment but does experience a 'squeeze' (ضغطة).

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
منكر ونكير
أهل السنة والجماعة
ضغطة القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the punishment of the grave is exclusively physical, affecting only the body.
Correction: The Sunni position states that the soul feels pain through its connection to the body, even if outside it.

Checkpoint
When is the punishment of the disbeliever in the grave lifted?
A) Only on Fridays
B) Fridays and Ramadan
C) Never
D) On Eid days

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position is that the punishment of the grave is real, the soul is connected to the body in experiencing it, and the punishment of disbelievers is suspended on Fridays and Ramadan.

The Punishment of the Grave and the Disbeliever's Case
Affirmation of grave punishment and disbeliever's case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni affirmation of the punishment of the grave, how it is experienced through the soul-body connection, and how it applies to disbelievers with periodic relief.

Core Idea
Grave punishment is real, and even disbelievers receive mercy on Fridays and during Ramadan.

The author opens by stating the Sunni creed: punishment of the grave, questioning by Munkar and Nakir, and constriction are all true. He then explains how punishment works—the flesh is connected to the soul, so they feel pain together. For disbelievers, punishment is continuous but is mercifully lifted on Fridays and during Ramadan by the Prophet's sanctity. This lesson unpacks these foundational doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Affirmation of grave punishment
Read the opening sentence where the author states that Ahl al-Sunnah affirms the punishment of the grave, questioning, and constriction.
Note that these are all considered realities in Sunni belief.
2
Mechanism of punishment
Study the explanation of how the soul remains connected to the body in the grave, allowing the soul to feel pain with the body even when external.
This explains how punishment is possible even after death.
3
Disbeliever's continuous punishment and relief
Understand that disbelievers suffer continuous punishment but it is lifted on Fridays and during Ramadan by the Prophet's sanctity.
This is a special mercy linked to the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: عذاب القبر حق، وسؤال منكر ونكير حقٌّ، وضيق القبر سواء كان مؤمناً أو كافراً أو مطيعاً أو فاسقاً، لكن إذا كان كافراً فعذابه يدوم في القبر إلى يوم القيامة، ويرفع عنهم العذاب يوم الجمعة، وشهر رمضان بحرمة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لأنهم ما داموا في الأحياء لا يعذبهم الله تعالى في الدنيا بحرمة النبي ، فكذلك في القبر يرفع عنهم العذاب يوم الجمعة وكل رمضان بحرمته فيعذب اللحم متصلا بالروح والروح متصلاً بالجسد، فيتألم الروح مع الجسد وإن كان خارجاً منه. ثم المؤمن على وجهين إن كان مطيعا لا يكون له عذاب القبر، ويكون له ضغطة فيجد هَوْلَ ذلك وخوفه؛ لما أنه كان تنعم بنعمة الله تعالى ولم يشكر النعمة، وإن كان عاصيا يكون له عذاب القبر وضغطة القبر، لكن ينقطع عنه عذاب القبر يوم الجمعة وليلته ثم لا يعود العذابُ إلى يوم القيامة، وإن مات يوم الجمعة أو ليلة الجمعة يكون له العذاب ساعة واحدة وضغطة القبر ثم ينقطع عنه العذاب ولا يعود إلى يوم القيامة، ويكون الروح متصلاً الجسد، وكذلك إذا صار ترابًا يكون روحه متصلاً بترابه فيتألم الرُّوح والتراب معًا.
And Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah said: Punishment of the grave is true, and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir is true, and the constriction of the grave [is true] whether one is a believer or disbeliever, obedient or sinful. However, if one is a disbeliever, his punishment continues in the grave until the Day of Resurrection, and the punishment is lifted from them on Friday and during the month of Ramadan by the sanctity of the Prophet ﷺ. Because as long as they are alive, Allah does not punish them in this world by the sanctity of the Prophet, so likewise in the grave the punishment is lifted from them on Friday and every Ramadan by his sanctity. So He punishes the flesh connected to the soul, and the soul connected to the body, so the soul feels pain with the body even though it is external to it. Then the believer is of two types: if he is obedient, he has no punishment of the grave, but he experiences its pressure, finding the terror and fear of it, because he had been enjoying Allah's blessing and did not thank for the blessing. And if he is disobedient, he has punishment of the grave and its pressure, but the punishment of the grave is cut off from him on Friday and its night, then the punishment does not return until the Day of Resurrection. And if he dies on Friday or the night of Friday, he has punishment for one hour and pressure of the grave, then the punishment is cut off from him and does not return until the Day of Resurrection. And the soul remains connected to the body, and likewise when he becomes dust, his soul remains connected to his dust, so the soul and the dust feel pain together.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents the Sunni doctrine on punishment of the grave. It opens by affirming three realities: punishment, questioning by Munkar and Nakir, and constriction of the grave, which apply to all—believer or disbeliever, obedient or sinful. For disbelievers, punishment is continuous but is lifted on Fridays and during Ramadan out of respect for the Prophet. The mechanism of punishment is explained: the flesh is punished while connected to the soul, and the soul, though external to the body, remains connected to it, allowing sensation. For believers, there are two categories: obedient believers feel only the pressure and fear (owing to ingratitude) but no actual punishment; disobedient believers experience punishment and pressure, but this punishment is suspended on Fridays (or on the night of Friday if they die then). After death, even when the body becomes dust, the soul remains connected to that dust, so both feel pain together. This affirms both the reality of punishment and the mercy extended to believers and even disbelievers on sacred occasions.

Grave Punishment for Believers: Obedient vs Disobedient
Differentiated punishment for believers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how grave punishment applies differently to obedient and disobedient believers, including the special case of dying on Friday.

Core Idea
Obedient believers feel only pressure, disobedient believers face punishment but get relief on Fridays.

The author now distinguishes between two types of believers in the grave: the obedient, who experience only constriction and fear due to ingratitude, and the disobedient, who undergo actual punishment. However, even the disobedient receive mercy—their punishment is suspended on Fridays. A special ruling is given for those who die on Friday: only one hour of punishment. This lesson examines these nuanced teachings.

Guided Path
1
Two categories of believers
Identify the two types: obedient (muti‘) and disobedient (‘asi).
The obedient have no punishment, only pressure; the disobedient have both.
2
Punishment for disobedient believers
Understand that their punishment is cut off on Friday and its night, and does not return.
This is a mercy similar to that for disbelievers but permanent.
3
Special case of dying on Friday
If a disobedient believer dies on Friday or its night, he only suffers one hour of punishment and pressure, then it ceases forever.
This highlights the blessedness of Friday.
4
Soul-dust connection
Note that the soul remains connected even to the dust after decomposition, so the pain continues.
This reinforces the earlier mechanism.

Evidence for Punishment of the Grave: Hadith and Reason
The author provides prophetic hadiths and rational analogies to support grave punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand both the transmitted (hadith) and rational proofs for the punishment of the grave, and how they refute objections.

Core Idea
Punishment of the grave is proven by prophetic hadiths and rational analogy from sleep and toothache.

This lesson presents two types of evidence for the punishment of the grave. First, we examine two hadiths from the Prophet ﷺ addressed to 'A'ishah and 'Umar, demonstrating the gentle nature of the experience for believers and the retention of intellect. Then, a rational proof is given using the phenomenon of dream sensations and the analogy of a toothache, showing that physical connection allows sensation even without the soul being present. These proofs together establish the doctrine firmly within Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall flow. Notice the two types of evidence: hadith and rational.
The passage uses prophetic narratives and then a rational argument.
2
Analyze the first hadith
Focus on the hadith to 'A'ishah. Notice the similes: the pressure of the grave is like a mother's embrace, and the questioning is like kohl for inflamed eyes. What does this teach about the believer's experience?
This shows the experience is not purely punitive but also merciful.
3
Analyze the second hadith
Look at the hadith to 'Umar. Observe the question about retaining intellect. How does this address fear of the grave?
The believer retains his intellect, so he can respond correctly.
4
Understand the rational proof
Examine the analogy from sleep: the soul leaves but remains connected, causing dreams and sensations. How does this show that connection is sufficient for sensation?
This refutes the idea that soul must be inside the body for sensation.
5
Examine the toothache analogy
The Prophet's analogy: a tooth hurts because it is connected to flesh, even without a soul. How does this directly answer the objection?
This shows that physical connection to the soul suffices for pain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يدل عليه ما رُوِيَ عن النبي الله و أنه قال لعائشة رضي الله عنها: «كيف حالك عند ضيق القبر وسؤال منكر ونكير ؟ ثم قال: يا حميراء، إن ضغطة القبر للمؤمن كغَمْرِ الأم رجل ولدها بيدها، وسؤال منكر ونكير للمؤمن كالإثمد للعين إذا رمدت» (۱). وكذلك رُوِيَ عن النبي الله أنه قال لعمر رضي الله عنه: «كيف حالك إذا أتاك فتّانا القبر؟ فقال عمر رضي الله عنه: أنا أكون في مثل هذه الحالة ويكون معي عقلي؟ قال: نعم، فقال عمر رضي الله عنه : إذاً لا أبالي» (۲). والدليل على أن عذاب القبر مما يقبله العقل، ألا ترى أن النائم تخرج روحه ويكون روحه متصلاً حتى أنه يتألم في المنام، ويتوصل إليه الألم أو الاستراحة، وقد يتكلم في المنام؛ لأن روحه متصل بجسده، وعن النبي أنه قيل له: «كيف يوجع اللحم في القبر ولم يكن فيه الروح ؟ فقال : كما يوجع سنك وإن لم يكن فيه الروح (۳). ) ألا ترى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أخبر أنَّ السِّنَّ قد يُوجَع لما أنه متصل باللحم وإن لم يكن فيه
This is supported by what was narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he said to 'A'ishah, may Allah be pleased with her: 'How is your state regarding the constriction of the grave and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir?' Then he said: 'O Humayra', indeed the pressure of the grave for the believer is like the embrace of a mother [squeezing] her child with her hand, and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir for the believer is like kohl for the eye when it is inflamed.' And likewise it was narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he said to 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'How will you be when the two testers of the grave come to you?' 'Umar said: 'Will I be in such a state and will I have my intellect with me?' He said: 'Yes.' So 'Umar said: 'Then I do not care.' And the proof that punishment of the grave is acceptable to reason is that do you not see that the sleeping person's soul leaves his body and his soul remains connected such that he feels pain in his dream, and pain or comfort reaches him, and he may speak in his dream, because his soul is connected to his body. And from the Prophet ﷺ that it was said to him: 'How does the flesh hurt in the grave when there is no soul in it?' He said: 'Just as your tooth hurts even though there is no soul in it.' Do you not see that the Prophet ﷺ informed that the tooth may hurt because it is connected to the flesh even though there is no soul in it?
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage provides two types of evidence for the punishment of the grave: transmitted (hadith) and rational. First, two hadiths: one to 'A'ishah describes the pressure of the grave for a believer as gentle as a mother's embrace, and the questioning as healing like kohl for sore eyes. The second hadith to 'Umar reassures that the believer will retain his intellect during the questioning, so 'Umar says he fears not. Then a rational proof is given: during sleep, the soul leaves the body but remains connected, so the sleeper feels pain or pleasure in dreams and may speak. This shows that connection is sufficient for sensation. Finally, a hadith from the Prophet answers a question about how flesh can hurt without the soul: it is like a toothache, where the tooth hurts because it is connected to the flesh, even though there is no soul in the tooth itself. This analogy demonstrates that physical connection allows sensation even without the soul being present inside the part. Together, these evidences refute the rationalist objection and support the Sunni doctrine.

سؤال منكر ونكير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some deny the punishment of the grave because they think the soul leaves the body entirely, so no sensation is possible.
Correction: The passage shows that the soul remains connected to the body even after death, just as during sleep, enabling sensation.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the Prophet use to explain how flesh can feel pain in the grave without a soul inside it?
A) A dead tree feeling the wind.
B) A tooth that hurts due to its connection to the flesh.
C) A lamp without oil giving light.
D) A dream without the dreamer.

Key Takeaway
Punishment of the grave is established by both prophetic hadiths and rational analogy, demonstrating that the soul remains connected to the body allowing sensation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet described the pressure of the grave for a believer as gentle as a mother's embrace. Do you live in such a way that you can hope for that mercy? What sin in your life today would make you fear the opposite?
?
Umar was told he would retain his intellect during the questioning and responded, 'Then I do not care.' Could you honestly say the same? What are you doing now to ensure that your intellect is guided by faith when that moment comes?
?
The sleep analogy shows that your soul can experience pain even when your body is inactive. If you were to die tonight, what state would your soul be in based on your actions today? What is one thing you will change right now to prepare for that reality?

Unseen Matters
beginner
6 min
The Nature of Punishment of the Grave for the Believer
Nasafi describes the believer's grave punishment and cites hadiths on questioning and compression.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of punishment of the grave for believers, including its temporary reprieve on Friday and the reality of the questioning and compression.

Core Idea
Punishment of the grave is real, but believers find relief on Friday.

Imam Nasafi begins by describing the specific state of a believer in the grave: though punishment may be experienced, it is suspended on Friday. He then narrates hadiths from the Prophet to 'Aisha and 'Umar that confirm the compression of the grave and the questioning by Munkar and Nakir.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of punishment for believers
Read how the author describes the punishment and its cessation on Friday and Friday night for a believer who was sinful but received some mercy.
Notice that the punishment returns after Friday until the Day of Judgment, except for those who die on Friday.
2
Study the hadith to 'Aisha
The Prophet comforts 'Aisha by comparing the compression of the grave to a mother's embrace and the questioning to soothing collyrium for inflamed eyes.
This shows that for believers, these experiences are not terrifying but gentle.
3
Study the hadith to 'Umar
The Prophet asks 'Umar how he will face the two testers of the grave. 'Umar's confident response stems from having his intellect intact, showing the importance of knowledge and faith.

Source Text
