Fasting: Obligation, Exceptions, and Superiority
Nasafi enumerates rulings on fasting obligation, exceptions, and make-up.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation of fasting, the categories of people exempted, and the rulings for menstruating and postpartum women.

Core Idea
Fasting is a firm obligation for every capable Muslim with clear exceptions and make-up rules.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi lays out the foundational rulings on fasting. He begins with the Quranic promise of reward for bearing hardship, then establishes fasting as an obligation from two clear verses. He explains who is exempted (sick, traveler, menstruating/postpartum women) and the principle of make-up (qada). This lesson walks through each element so you can grasp the complete framework of Islamic fasting law.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation slowly. Notice how each ruling is connected to a Quranic verse or a rational point.
Pay attention to the flow: rationale → obligation → conditions → exceptions → superiority → special rulings.
2
Identify the Quranic proofs
Find the two verses that establish the obligation of fasting (2:185 and 2:183) and the verse about its superiority (2:184). Understand how they are used as evidence.
3
Note the exceptions and their logic
The text mentions the sick and traveler as permitted to break the fast, and menstruating/postpartum women as prohibited from fasting and praying. Observe that the sick/traveler make up later, while the women only make up the fasts, not prayers.
The reason given for not making up prayers is hardship due to multiplicity.
4
Reflect on the wisdom behind the rulings
Think about why the obligation is tied to belief, sanity, and adulthood, and why concessions are given for hardship. This shows the balance between duty and mercy in Islamic law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن التمتع بلا تحمل عناء التكليف موعود (۱) في الجنة كما قال الله تعالى: كُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا هَنِيَا بِمَا أَسْلَفْتُمْ فِي الْأَيَّامِ الْخَالِيةِ ﴾ [الحاقة: ٢٤] [أي صُمْتُم في الأيام الخالية (٢)] (۳). وقد أمر الله تعالى عباده بالصوم حيث قال: فَمَن شَهِدَ مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمْهُ ) [البقرة: ١٨٥] وقال: ﴿ يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الصِّيَامُ كَمَا كُتِبَ عَلَى الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَتَّقُونَ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۳] فما دام العبد مؤمناً عاقلاً بالغا لا يسقط عنه الصّوم وكذا سائر الفرائض كالصلاة والزكاة بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلَوَةَ وَمَاتُوا الزَّكَوةَ ) [البقرة: ١١٠] بخلاف المريض والمسافر حيث أُبيح لهما الأكل والشرب. والصوم أفضل لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَبَاءٍ أُخَرَ) [البقرة: ١٨٥] وقوله تعالى: وَأَن تَصُومُوا خَيْرٌ لَكُمْ إِن كُنتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٤] بخلاف الحائض والنفساء حيث لا تصوم ولا تصلي وتقضي الصوم ولا تقضي الصلاة؛ لأن في قضاء الصلاة حرجًا لتضاعفها ولا حرج في قضاء الصوم.
And because enjoyment without bearing the hardship of obligation is promised (1) in Paradise, as Allah Almighty said: 'Eat and drink pleasantly for what you sent ahead in past days' (al-Haqqah 69:24) [i.e., you fasted in past days] (2) (3). And Allah Almighty commanded His servants to fast when He said: 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' (al-Baqarah 2:185) and said: 'O you who have believed, prescribed upon you is fasting as it was prescribed upon those before you, that you may become righteous' (al-Baqarah 2:183). So as long as the servant is a believer, sane, and of age, fasting is not dropped from him, and likewise the rest of the obligations such as prayer and zakat, by His saying: 'And establish prayer and give zakat' (al-Baqarah 2:110), contrary to the sick and the traveler, for whom eating and drinking are permitted. And fasting is better because of His saying: 'Then a number of other days' (al-Baqarah 2:185) and His saying: 'And that you fast is better for you, if you only knew' (al-Baqarah 2:184), contrary to the menstruating woman and the woman in postpartum bleeding, for she does not fast nor pray, and she makes up the fast but does not make up the prayer, because in making up the prayer there is hardship due to its multiplicity, and no hardship in making up the fast.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings on fasting within a theological context. It begins by citing enjoyment in Paradise without hardship as a rationale, quoting Quran 69:24. Then it establishes the obligation of fasting from Quran 2:185 and 2:183, specifying that the obligation applies to every believer who is mature and sane. Travelers and the sick are excused, allowed to eat and drink. Fasting is emphasized as superior using Quran 2:184. Finally, it addresses menstruating and postpartum women: they must not fast or pray during that time, but they must make up the fasts, not the prayers, because making up prayers would be excessively burdensome due to their multiplicity.

Key Terms
الصوم
الحائض
النفساء
قضاء
الفرائض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that sick or travelers are permanently exempt from fasting, or that menstruating women do not need to make up fasts.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the sick and traveler are permitted to break but must make up later (implied by 'عدة من أيام أخر'), and menstruating/postpartum women must make up the fasts but not prayers.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a menstruating woman regarding fasting and prayer?
A) She must fast and pray as usual.
B) She must not fast or pray, and she must make up both.
C) She must not fast or pray, and she must make up the fast but not the prayer.
D) She is permanently exempt from both.

Key Takeaway
Fasting is a fundamental obligation for every capable Muslim, with specific allowances and make-up requirements for those unable to fast due to valid reasons.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used a valid excuse (like travel or minor illness) to skip fasting without truly assessing whether you could have endured the hardship? How can you strengthen your resolve to fast even when it's permissible to break it?
?
When you make up missed fasts, do you do so with the same sincerity and urgency as you do during Ramadan, or do you delay them carelessly? What does your attitude reveal about your appreciation for this obligation?
?
If you are a woman, have you ever felt resentment at having to make up fasts after your period while being exempt from prayers? How can you transform that feeling into gratitude for Allah’s mercy in light of the wisdom mentioned in the passage?

Unseen Matters
beginner
4 min
Location of the Sun, Moon, and Stars in the Heavens
Imam Nasafi presents two views on the placement of the sun, moon, and stars, and cites Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two competing views on the location of the celestial bodies and the Quranic evidence that supports the Sunni position.

Core Idea
The Quran places the stars in the lowest heaven, not the fourth.

This lesson addresses a specific theological question: Where are the sun, moon, and stars located? Astronomers (ahl al-nujum) held one view, but the Ahl al-Sunnah, relying on the Quran, hold another. Imam Nasafi presents both and then brings Quranic proofs to settle the matter. Let's explore the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two views
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice that two distinct groups and their claims are presented: the astronomers and the people of tafsir.
The bracket indicates alternative naming for the second group.
2
Examine the Quranic verses cited
Find the two verses from Surah al-Saffat and al-Mulk. Notice how they explicitly mention the lowest heaven as the location of the stars.
3
Reflect on the Dhu al-Qarnayn argument
Consider the third proof from Surah al-Kahf. Why does the story of Dhu al-Qarnayn reaching the setting place of the sun argue against the sun being in the fourth heaven? This is a logical inference.
The conclusion is that the correct view is the one supported by Quranic evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في محل الأفلاك في السموات
قال أهل النجوم: الشمس والقمر والنجوم في السماء الرابعة.
وقال [أهل السنة والجماعة أو] أهل التفسير: في السماء الدنيا.
يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا زَيَّنَّا السَّمَاءَ الدُّنْيَا بِزِينَةِ الْكَوَاكِبِ﴾ [الصافات: ٦] وقوله: ﴿وَلَقَدْ زَيَّنَّا السَّمَاءَ الدُّنْيَا بِمَصَابِيحَ﴾ [الملك: ٥].
وكذلك قوله تعالى في قصة ذي القرنين: ﴿حَتَّى إِذَا بَلَغَ مَغْرِبَ الشَّمْسِ وَجَدَهَا تَغْرُبُ فِي عَيْنٍ حَمِئَةٍ﴾ [الكهف: ٥٨] وهو لم يبلغ إلى السماء الرابعة، والله الهادي إلى سبيل الرشاد.
Chapter: On the location of the celestial spheres in the heavens. The astronomers said: The sun, the moon, and the stars are in the fourth heaven. And [the Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah or] the people of tafsir said: They are in the lowest heaven. That is indicated by His statement, Exalted is He: {Indeed, We adorned the lowest heaven with an adornment of the stars} [al-Saffat: 6] and His statement: {And We have indeed adorned the lowest heaven with lamps} [al-Mulk: 5]. And likewise His statement, Exalted is He, in the story of Dhu al-Qarnayn: {Until, when he reached the setting of the sun, he found it setting in a muddy spring} [al-Kahf: 86]—and he had not reached the fourth heaven. And Allah is the Guide to the path of right guidance.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal classification and proof. Imam Nasafi presents two conflicting views on the location of the sun, moon, and stars: the astronomers (ahl al-nujum) claim they are in the fourth heaven, while the Ahl al-Sunnah or the people of Quranic exegesis (ahl al-tafsir) hold they are in the lowest heaven (al-sama' al-dunya). The author then provides Quranic evidence to support the latter view. First, he cites verse 6 of Surat al-Saffat, which states that Allah adorned the lowest heaven with the beauty of the stars. Second, he cites verse 5 of Surat al-Mulk, which says Allah adorned the lowest heaven with lamps (masabih, i.e., stars). These verses explicitly place the stars in the lowest heaven, not the fourth. Third, he invokes the story of Dhu al-Qarnayn from Surat al-Kahf (verse 86), where Dhu al-Qarnayn travels to the west and finds the sun setting in a muddy spring. Nasafi argues that if the sun were in the fourth heaven, Dhu al-Qarnayn could not have reached it or observed it setting so closely; since he did, the sun must be in the lower heavens, specifically the lowest. The passage concludes with a prayer: 'And Allah is the Guide to the path of right guidance.'

Key Terms
أفلاك
السماء الرابعة
السماء الدنيا
الكواكب
مصابيح
أهل النجوم
أهل التفسير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the sun and moon are in the fourth heaven based on astronomical theories.
Correction: The Quran places them in the lowest heaven, as shown by verses from al-Saffat, al-Mulk, and the story of Dhu al-Qarnayn.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, where does the Quran place the stars?
A) In the fourth heaven
B) In the lowest heaven
C) In the seventh heaven
D) In the second heaven

Key Takeaway
The Quran places the sun, moon, and stars in the lowest heaven, contrary to the astronomers' claim of the fourth heaven.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the night sky, do you see the stars as Allah's adornment of the lowest heaven, or as mere astronomical objects? How does this verse change your perspective on the heavens?
?
The astronomers had a theory, but the Quran corrected it. Are there areas in your life where you trust human knowledge over divine revelation? What would it take for you to submit to the Quran's teaching even when it contradicts common knowledge?
?
Dhu al-Qarnayn reached the setting of the sun—a miracle. Do you believe Allah can override the laws of nature? How does this story challenge your assumptions about the physical world and its limitations?
